1 of 368 DOCUMENTS


State v. Olsen


Docket No. 43496-2015, 2016 Opinion No. 147


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


161 Idaho 385; 386 P.3d 908; 2016 Ida. LEXIS 417



December 21, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Jefferson County. Hon. Gregory W. Moeller, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is affirmed in part and remanded with intructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The prosecution of defendant for misuse of public funds in violation of Idaho Code Ann. § 18-5701(10) did not violate the separation of powers under Idaho Const. art. II, § 1 because the county commissioners had no power to absolve defendant of any criminal liability upon learning of the use of a backup cell phone by his wife; [2]-There was no showing that § 18-5701was unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant because the contrast between public and governmental on the one hand and personal on the other provided sufficient definiteness for an ordinary person to understand what conduct was prohibited and provided sufficient guidelines for law enforcement; [3]-Two of the convictions had to be vacated because when the State chose to aggregate the separate incidents, it was required under Idaho Code Ann. § 18-5702(4)(a) to aggregate all of them into one count.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed in part and vacated in part.

 

2 of 368 DOCUMENTS


State v. Clark


Docket No. 44123, 2016 Opinion No. 151


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


161 Idaho 372; 386 P.3d 895; 2016 Ida. LEXIS 416



December 21, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Gerald Schroeder, Senior District Judge; Hon. Kevin Swain, Magistrate Judge.
State v. Clark, 2016 Ida. App. LEXIS 21 (Idaho Ct. App., Feb. 23, 2016)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The district court properly affirmed the denial of defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal under Idaho Crim. R 29 because a rational jury could have found the essential elements of misdemeanor trespass under Idaho Code Ann. § 18-7008(8) beyond a reasonable doubt; [2]-The State presented competent evidence that defendant refused to depart from the Industrial Commission building after first being notified verbally by an authorized agent of the owner of the Commission building to immediately depart from the building; [3]-Defendant failed to show a violation of his due process rights because he entered the governmental office to seek corrections based on a supreme court opinion and not to exercise First Amendment rights; [4]-He had no constitutional right to remain on the Commission premises after he was asked to depart.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Farfan-Galvan


Docket No. 44360, 2016 Opinion No. 144


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


161 Idaho 610; 389 P.3d 155; 2016 Ida. LEXIS 395



December 8, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Twin Falls County. Hon. G. Richard Bevan, District Judge.
State v. Farfan-Galvan, 2016 Ida. App. Unpub. LEXIS 148 (Idaho Ct. App., Mar. 22, 2016)



DISPOSITION: The district court's decision denying Farfan-Galvan's motion to dismiss or remand is reversed and the judgement of conviction is vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Because the record did not contain any indication that defendant waived his right to counsel in a prior case, that conviction could not serve as the basis to enhance defendant's DUI charge to a felony and the trial court erred in denying defendant's motion to dismiss.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed, conviction vacated.

State v. Baeza


Docket No. 42988, 2016 Opinion No. 116


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


161 Idaho 38; 383 P.3d 1208; 2016 Ida. LEXIS 315



November 2, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Blaine County. Hon. Jonathan Brody, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The district court's judgment of conviction is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a case in which a jury found defendant guilty of lewd conduct with a minor child under the age of 16, the district court's order allowing the victim to testify by closed-circuit television did not violate defendant's due process right to a fair trial or infringe on the presumption of innocence; [2]-The alternative method of testimony was not inherently prejudicial; [3]-The district court considered the relative rights and interests of the parties under Idaho Code Ann. § 9-1806 when it ordered the alternative method.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

6 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Warner v. Idaho Transp. Dep't


Docket No. 43484, 2016 Opinion No. 71


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


160 Idaho 732; 378 P.3d 1031; 2016 Ida. LEXIS 192



June 28, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Warner v. Idaho Transp. Dep't, 2016 Ida. LEXIS 286 (Idaho, Sept. 13, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Blaine County. Hon. Robert J. Elgee, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The district court erred in reducing the suspension of defendant's driver's license from one year to 30 days because the record disclosed two DUI convictions within 10 years--one in Idaho in 2012 and one in Montana in 2014--subjecting defendant to the one-year suspension mandated in Idaho Code Ann. § 18-8005(4)(e) where driving under the influence was a violation which, if committed in Idaho, would be grounds for suspension, nothing on the face of the Montana court's "Disposition Report" in the record indicated that the DUI was charged as a first offense, defendant's assertion that she would have successfully bargained for an unenhanced DUI charge in Idaho was mere speculation, Idaho Code Ann. §§ 49-326(1) and 49-324 authorized the Department of Transportation to suspend her license, and defendant's constitutional arguments were vague, conclusory, and failed on the merits.


OUTCOME: Decision vacated.

 

7 of 368 DOCUMENTS


James v. City of Boise


Docket No. 42053-2014, 2016 Opinion No. 36


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


160 Idaho 466; 376 P.3d 33; 2016 Ida. LEXIS 83



March 23, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] SUBSTITUTE OPINION. THE COURT'S PRIOR OPINION DATED MAY 21, 2015 IS HEREBY WITHDRAWN.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Ada County. Hon. Steven J. Hippler, District Judge.
James v. City of Boise, 136 S. Ct. 685, 193 L. Ed. 2d 694, 2016 U.S. LEXIS 947 (U.S., 2016)



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A district court did not err in holding that the police officers were entitled to qualified immunity with respect to an individual's 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims where their use of a police dog to find and subdue by biting a suspected burglar in a building did not violate a clearly established right; [2]-The district court did not err in dismissing the assault, battery, false arrest, and wrongful imprisonment claims where there was no evidence that the police acted with criminal intent; [3]-The Idaho Code Ann. § 25-2808 claim was properly dismissed where the individual was the suspected offender who the police were using the police dog to locate and apprehend so that they could arrest, and thus, Idaho Code Ann. §§ 25-2805 and 25-2808 did not apply; [4]-Attorney fees were awarded against the individual under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988, but not Idaho Code Ann. § 12-117.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; police officers and city awarded costs and attorneys fees.

 

8 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Alexander v. Stibal


Docket No. 41604, 2016 Opinion No. 17


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


161 Idaho 253; 385 P.3d 431; 2016 Ida. LEXIS 40



February 26, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Alexander v. Stibal, 2016 Ida. LEXIS 137 (Idaho, Apr. 29, 2016)
Rehearing denied by Alexander v. Stibal, 2016 Ida. LEXIS 138 (Idaho, Apr. 29, 2016)
Stay granted by Alexander v. Stibal, 2016 Ida. LEXIS 173 (Idaho, June 15, 2016)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Stibal v. Alexander, 137 S. Ct. 258, 196 L. Ed. 2d 136, 2016 U.S. LEXIS 4819 (U.S., 2016)
Stay lifted by, Remittitur granted Alexander v. Stibal, 2016 Ida. LEXIS 389 (Idaho, Nov. 30, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bonneville County. Hon. William H. Woodland, Senior District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The district court's order denying Stibal's motion for JNOV on the contract claim is reversed. The judgment of the district court is vacated and the case is remanded for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Because the terms of a purported contract were too uncertain for a court to enforce, a district court erred in denying a motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict on the contract claim; [2]-As to fraud, substantial evidence was presented as to all nine elements of fraud which reasonable minds could accept; [3]-An alleged healer's claim to have healed herself of cancer was proven to be a fraudulent misrepresentation by clear and convincing evidence; [4]-There was no abuse of discretion in allowing the amendment of the complaint to include a claim for punitive damages under Idaho Code Ann. § 6-1604; [5]-An award of $250,000 in punitive damages would be unconstitutional, and punitive damages in the amount of $100,000, approximately a ratio of 6:1, was the maximum which was constitutionally permissible under the facts of this case.


OUTCOME: Reversed; vacated; remanded for further proceedings.

 

9 of 368 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rawlings


Docket No. 42697-2014, 2015 Opinion No. 114


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


159 Idaho 498; 363 P.3d 339; 2015 Ida. LEXIS 324



December 22, 2015, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Kootenai County. Hon. Charles W. Hosack, District Judge, and Hon. Rich Christensen, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The district court did not err in holding that Idaho Code Ann. § 18-1401 did not violate defendant's First Amendment rights where the First Amendment did prohibit the use of speech to establish the elements of a crime or to prove motive or intent; [2]-The district court did not err in permitting testimony about defendant's statement that he had previously gotten away with stealing at a retailer where it implicitly held that the Rule 404(b) notice was filed and served reasonably in advance of trial when it denied a motion in limine, the jury could have inferred from a deputy's testimony that because defendant had shoplifted in the past, he was less likely to have entered the store with innocent intent, and the jury was properly instructed as to the use of such evidence.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Dunlap v. State


Docket No. 41105, 2015 Opinion No. 103


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


159 Idaho 280; 360 P.3d 289; 2015 Ida. LEXIS 273



November 2, 2015, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 5, 2016.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Dunlap v. Idaho, 2016 U.S. LEXIS 4969 (U.S., Oct. 3, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Sixth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Caribou County. Hon. Mitchell W. Brown, District Judge.
State v. Dunlap, 125 Idaho 530, 873 P.2d 784, 1993 Ida. LEXIS 142 (Idaho, 1993)



DISPOSITION: District court summary dismissal of successive petition for post-conviction relief, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant's substantive claims for postconviction relief were barred by Idaho Code Ann. § 19-2719 where he made no argument or showing that his claims of error regarding the jury instructions and voir dire were not known or could not have been known within 42 days of the judgment, and he had not timely raised a claim based upon a page limit; [2]-Appellate counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise the claim that the propensity aggravator instruction was unconstitutional; [3]-Appellate counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise the claim that the aggravating and mitigating circumstances instruction was unconstitutional; [4]-The district court properly granted the State's motion for summary dismissal of defendant claims that the public defender provided ineffective assistance of appellate counsel by failing to raise issues related to the impartiality of the jury.


OUTCOME: Dismissal affirmed.

 

11 of 368 DOCUMENTS


In re Greater Boise Auditorium Dist. v. Frazier


Docket No. 43074, 2015 Opinion No. 100


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


159 Idaho 266; 360 P.3d 275; 2015 Ida. LEXIS 264



October 15, 2015, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Greater Boise Auditorium Dist. v. Frazier, 2015 Ida. LEXIS 305 (Idaho, Nov. 23, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Lynn Norton, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is reversed. No attorney fees on appeal are awarded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Under Idaho Code Ann. §§ 7-1304 and 7-1308, courts had a duty to examine other documents which affected the question submitted, and then to determine the propriety of the contracts before them; [2]-A lease for a new facility did not subject the auditorium district to greater liabilities that it could pay in the fiscal year by virtue of its non-appropriate provisions, and thus, the district court erred in concluding that the lease did not satisfy Idaho Const. art. VIII, § 3; [3]-The relevant determination under Idaho Const. art. VIII, § 3, was whether the governmental subdivision had presently bound itself to a liability greater than it had funds to pay for in the year in which it bound itself; [4]-The overall agreement, which included the restated development agreement, a master development agreement, and a purchase and sale agreement, also passed constitutional muster.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; attorney's fees denied.

 

12 of 368 DOCUMENTS


State v. Haynes


Docket No. 41924-2014, 2015 Opinion No. 80


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


159 Idaho 36; 355 P.3d 1266; 2015 Ida. LEXIS 208



August 20, 2015, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Kootenai County. Hon. Rich Christensen, District Judge, and Hon. Scott L. Wayman, Magistrate Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The district court did not err in upholding the granting of the State's motion for a continuance; [2]-Because defendant did not offer any evidence as to how the state trooper conducted the breath test or whether the testing instrument was properly calibrated, she failed to show that the State could not lay a sufficient foundation for the admissibility of the test results; [3]-The district court did not err in upholding the denial of defendant's motion in limine to exclude the results of the breath test on the ground that procedures for administering the test had not been properly adopted by the Idaho State Police; [4]-Although defendant contended that her consent to a breath test was invalid because it was obtained by the threat of a monetary penalty and loss of her driver's license for one year, requiring a breath test in this circumstance was not an unreasonable search.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed.

TracFone Wireless, Inc. v. State


Docket No. 41868-2014, 2015 Opinion No. 60


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


158 Idaho 671; 351 P.3d 599; 2015 Ida. LEXIS 160



June 23, 2015, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected August 26, 2015.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Ada County. Hon. Michael E. Wetherell, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A district court properly concluded that a wireless company was not a wireless carrier under Idaho Code Ann. § 31-4802(13)(b) where it was not licensed by the FCC, and under the unambiguous definition set forth in Idaho Code Ann. § 31-4802(15) and 47 C.F.R. § 20.18, it was not a specialized mobile radio provider; [2]-The district court properly held that the company was a provider of any other communications service, as set forth in Idaho Code Ann. § 31-4802(13)(d) where it was undisputed that it provided communications service that connected an individual having either a service address or a place of primary use within Idaho to an established public safety answering point by dialing 911; [3]-The district court did not err in refusing to strike the affidavits offered in connection with the company's motion for partial judgment; [4]-No parties were granted attorney fees.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

14 of 368 DOCUMENTS


James v. City of Boise


Docket No. 42053-2014, 2015 Opinion No. 49


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


158 Idaho 713; 351 P.3d 1171; 2015 Ida. LEXIS 130



May 21, 2015, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by James v. City of Boise, 2015 Ida. LEXIS 146 (Idaho, June 19, 2015)
Later proceeding at James v. City of Boise, 2015 Ida. LEXIS 169 (Idaho, June 23, 2015)
Rehearing denied by James v. City of Boise, 2015 Ida. LEXIS 200 (Idaho, July 20, 2015)
Reversed by, Remanded by James v. City of Boise, 136 S. Ct. 685, 193 L. Ed. 2d 694, 2016 U.S. LEXIS 947 (U.S., Jan. 25, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Ada County. Hon. Steven J. Hippler, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendants police sued under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 when their dog bit plaintiff individual mistakenly thought to be a burglar were qualifiedly immune because no clearly established law held this was excessive force; [2]-It was no error to dismiss assault, battery, false arrest, or wrongful imprisonment claims because "criminal intent," under Idaho Code Ann. § 6-904(3), meant intentionally committing what a person knew to be a crime, which nothing showed; [3]-Idaho Code Ann. §§ 25-2808 and 25-2805 did not apply because the individual was a suspect apprehended by a police dog; [4]-Police were not liable for negligent failure to train due to the dog training method they used because Idaho Code Ann. § 6-904(1) exempted this discretionary decision; [5]-Police were entitled to attorney fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988 because qualified immunity clearly barred the individual's claim.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

15 of 368 DOCUMENTS


State v. Olivas


Docket No. 41644, 2015 Opinion No. 44


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


158 Idaho 375; 347 P.3d 1189; 2015 Ida. LEXIS 124



May 4, 2015, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho,Canyon County. Hon. Thomas J. Ryan, District Judge.
State v. Olivas, 2013 Ida. App. LEXIS 72 (Idaho Ct. App., Sept. 6, 2013)



DISPOSITION: The judgment of conviction and sentence is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Supreme Court concluded that Idaho Code Ann. § 18-8311(1) fails to impose a mandatory minimum sentence as contemplated by Idaho Const. art. V, § 13; [2]-The Supreme Court adopted an interpretation of § 18-8311(1) that does not restrict the trial court's authority to suspend the offender's original sentence; [3]-The district court appropriately used its discretion to sentence defendant for his original offense (sexual abuse of a child) and to set the penalty for his probation violation; [4]-The district court continued to have the discretion to manage defendant's probation violation for his original offense after abiding by any directives in § 18-8311(1); [5]-The district court did not err by suspending defendant's original sentence and placing him on probation after the second period of retained jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: Conviction and sentence affirmed.

State v. Abdullah


Docket Nos. 31659, 39417, 2015 Opinion No. 29


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


158 Idaho 386; 348 P.3d 1; 2015 Ida. LEXIS 78



March 2, 2015, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Azad Haji Abdullah, 2015 Ida. LEXIS 140 (Idaho, May 28, 2015)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Abdullah v. Idaho, 2016 U.S. LEXIS 1387 (U.S., Feb. 29, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the district court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Cheri C. Copsey, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The convictions, sentences, and the order denying post-conviction relief are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant's first-degree murder, attempted first-degree murder, arson, and felony injury to a child convictions were affirmed where, inter alia, the request for funding an expert to evaluate DNA evidence was properly denied, the evidence was sufficient to sustain the convictions, and the evidence was properly admitted; [2]-Defendant's death sentence was affirmed where, inter alia, imposition of the death penalty did not violated the Ex Post Facto Clauses or defendant's right to due process, Idaho's death penalty did not violate the Eighth Amendment, and the limiting construction of the statutory aggravating factors did not violate the separation of powers doctrine; [3]-Defendant was properly denied postconviction relief where, inter alia, the district court applied the correct standard for the ineffective assistance of counsel claims, and counsel was not ineffective.


OUTCOME: Judgments affirmed.

 

17 of 368 DOCUMENTS


State v. Thiel


Docket No. 41811, 2015 Opinion No. 27


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


158 Idaho 103; 343 P.3d 1110; 2015 Ida. LEXIS 70



February 27, 2015, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Michael R. McLaughlin, District Judge. Hon. Carolyn Minder, Magistrate Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The district court properly overturned a magistrate's rejection of a sheriff's recommendation that defendant be granted an early release for good behavior pursuant to Idaho Code Ann. § 20-621 because the magistrate court was vested with no discretion in the good-time early release process where the plain language of § 20-621 vested the authority to determine a good-time early release solely with the sheriff, there was no similar express grant or reference to judicial discretion, but created a ministerial duty for the court, and the magistrate court was included in the process for administrative record-keeping and finality; [2]-Section 20-621 did not encroach upon the judiciary's inherent sentencing authority in violation of Idaho Const. art. II, § 1 because the legislature had authority to delegate the good-behavior determination to an executive branch agency.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

18 of 368 DOCUMENTS


State v. Grathol


Docket No. 40168, 2015 Opinion No. 17


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


158 Idaho 39; 343 P.3d 480; 2015 Ida. LEXIS 48



February 11, 2015, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District, State of Idaho, Kootenai County. Hon. Charles W. Hosack, Senior District Judge.
State DOT v. HJ Grathol, 153 Idaho 87, 278 P.3d 957, 2012 Ida. LEXIS 137 (Idaho, 2012)



DISPOSITION: District court decision in eminent domain case, affirmed in part, vacated in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Substantial evidence supported the district court's holding that 56.8 acres was the larger parcel where at the time of the taking, the property owner had obtained zoning of that acreage as commercial, the acreage's highest and best use was commercial development, and there was little support for a smaller sized acreage; [2]-Substantial evidence supported the holding that the owner's remaining property suffered zero severance damages where the lack of fair market value testimony meant the court could not consider the owner's claimed evidence of increased costs; [3]-The district court did not abuse its discretion when it excluded testimony about a proposed frontage road where there was no evidence that the property taken was for the purpose of a frontage road; [4]-The district court erred in denying the transportation department attorney fees, but properly awarded it costs.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part and vacated in part. Case remanded.

 

19 of 368 DOCUMENTS


State v. Knutsen


Docket No. 40803-2013, 2015 Opinion No. 10


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


158 Idaho 199; 345 P.3d 989; 2015 Ida. LEXIS 25



January 26, 2015, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Knutsen, 2015 Ida. LEXIS 113 (Idaho, Apr. 13, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Twin Falls County. Hon. G. Richard Bevan, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant's indictment was not void for being issued after the grand jury's term expired, under Idaho Crim. R. 6.8, because the term began when it first met; [2]-He did not show "vulnerable adult," for purposes of Idaho Code Ann. § 18-1505B, criminalizing sex with a vulnerable adult, was vague because he did not reasonably believe his victim was not a vulnerable adult; [3]-He did not show Idaho Code § 18-1505B was overbroad for limiting adult sex because they had no such constitutional right, consent was not involved, and the State had a legitimate state interest in protecting vulnerable adults; [4]-Substantial evidence supported his conviction because the victim had difficulty quickly deciding complex issues, and the jury could weigh her ability to answer questions; [5]-He did not show his sentence violated double jeopardy because he based his claim on a repealed statute.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Wulff

DISPOSITION: District court order granting motion to suppress, affirmed.

21 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. Idaho State Bd. of Real Estate Appraisers


Docket No. 41193, 2014 Opinion No. 116


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


157 Idaho 496; 337 P.3d 655; 2014 Ida. LEXIS 288



October 29, 2014, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Kathryn A. Sticklen, District Judge.
Williams v. Bd. of Real Estate Appraisers (In re Williams), 149 Idaho 675, 239 P.3d 780, 2010 Ida. LEXIS 164 (Idaho, 2010)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Although a complainant became a member of the Idaho State Board of Real Estate Appraisers by the time the agency was ruling on the appraiser's case, the appraiser's due process rights were not violated, because the complainant recused himself and did not vote on the recommendation to the Board; [2]-There was substantial evidence in the record to support the hearing officer's finding of professional misconduct, including evidence that the appraiser used other appraisers' information to access an on-line bidding system and underbid them, that such action amounted to a misrepresentation of identity, and the appraiser issued a misleading appraisal report; [3]-The revocation of the appraiser's license and imposition of a fine was not improper; [4]-The Board improperly awarded itself attorney fees, as Idaho Code Ann. § 54-1806A(9)(e), did not explicitly provide for such an award.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

22 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Conner v. Hodges


Docket No. 40742, 2014 Opinion No. 89


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


157 Idaho 19; 333 P.3d 130; 2014 Ida. LEXIS 230



August 22, 2014, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As corrected October 21, 2014.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Ronald J. Wilper, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is affirmed in part, vacated in part and the case is remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The district court erred in granting a doctor summary judgment on the ground that a medical malpractice claim was barred by the two-year statute of limitations, Idaho Code Ann. § 5-219(4), because the cause of action for malpractice did not accrue on the date of a wife's surgery; [2]-The wife presented expert testimony challenging the contention of the doctor's expert that her injury was capable of being objectively ascertained.; [3]-She offered the affidavit of a physician, who explained that the procedures the expert identified were invasive, painful, risky, and costly, and any physician who recommended or performed them would be subject to disciplinary action; [4]-The district court properly ruled that the gravamen of the claim was the failure to provide proper health care, and under Idaho Code § 6-1012, the wife was precluded from bringing a breach of contract claim.


OUTCOME: Judgment dismissing malpractice action vacated and summary judgment with respect to breach of contract claim affirmed.

 

23 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Profits Plus Capital Mgmt., LLC v. Podesta


Docket No. 39964, 2014 Opinion No. 65


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


156 Idaho 873; 332 P.3d 785; 2014 Ida. LEXIS 186



July 8, 2014, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Profits Plus Capital Mgmt., LLC v. Podesta, 2014 Ida. LEXIS 257 (Idaho, Sept. 15, 2014)

Docket No. 40827, 2014 Opinion No. 32


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO

DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A district court properly affirmed a magistrate's award of attorney fees to a collection agency in the amount of the principal owed by the debtors for medical services, as opposed to $350, which was the minimum amount that each debtor contracted to pay because the agency's collection actions were unquestionably subject to the provisions of the Idaho Collection Agency Act, Idaho Code Ann. §§ 26-2221-2251, § 26-2229A(4) prohibited the agency from collecting any fees incidental to the principal obligation (the money the debtors owed to the health care provider for the services it provided), the attorney fees were subordinate and incidental to the principal obligation, and the agency had no standing to enforce the contracts entered into between the debtors and the provider.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed.

Telford v. Nye


Docket No. 39497, 2013 Opinion No. 52


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


154 Idaho 606; 301 P.3d 264; 2013 Ida. LEXIS 128



April 23, 2013, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Telford v. Nye, 2013 Ida. LEXIS 184 (Idaho, May 31, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Sixth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Oneida County.



DISPOSITION: The order of the District Court is affirmed. Costs on appeal are awarded to Respondent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent administrative judge for the District Court of the Sixth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Oneida County, issued a pre-filing order declaring petitioner litigant to be a vexatious litigant pursuant to Idaho Ct. Admin. R. 59. After the litigant failed to file an amended response within the time allowed, the judge entered a final order declaring the litigant to be vexatious. The litigant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The judge issued the pre-filing order following requests from several district court and magistrate judges. The final order precluded the litigant from filing any new pro se litigation in the courts of Idaho without first obtaining leave of a judge. The reviewing court held that the litigant waived challenges to the adequacy of service of the pre-filing order because she admitted to receiving service and submitted to the court's jurisdiction, that the final order was not premature because the litigant was given sufficient time to respond, that the judge did not have a duty to disqualify himself under Idaho R. Civ. P. 40(d)(1) or 40(d)(2) because those rules did not apply in the proceedings, that Idaho Ct. Admin. R. 59 was not unconstitutionally vague, and that the litigant was afforded adequate due process of law. The final order did not constitute an abuse of the judge's discretion because the record showed that the litigant had filed three pro se litigations within the past seven years that were finally determined adversely to her, which could not be relitigated, and because she had been declared vexatious by other state and federal courts.


OUTCOME: The administrative judge's order was affirmed.

Seiniger Law Offices, P.A. v. State ex rel. Indus. Comm'n


Docket No. 38037, 2013 Opinion No. 46


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


154 Idaho 461; 299 P.3d 773; 2013 Ida. LEXIS 115



April 12, 2013, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
SUBSTITUTE OPINION, THE COURT'S PRIOR OPINION DATED FEBRUARY 22, 2013 IS HEREBY WITHDRAWN.
Rehearing denied by Seiniger Law Offices, P.A. v. State ex rel. Indus. Comm'n, 2013 Ida. LEXIS 133 (Idaho, Apr. 15, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Industrial Commission of the State of Idaho.
Seiniger Law Offices, P.A. v. State ex rel. Indus. Comm'n, 2013 Ida. LEXIS 54 (Idaho, Feb. 22, 2013)



DISPOSITION: The orders of the Industrial Commission are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant law firm challenged a decision from the Industrial Commission of the State of Idaho, which determined that claimed attorney fees in a worker's compensation case did not comply with Idaho Admin. Code r. 17.02.08.033 (1994).


OVERVIEW: The law firm was retained to represent clients in worker's compensation proceedings. The Commission determined that the claimed attorney fees did not comply with Idaho Admin. Code r. 17.02.08.033 (1994) as to permanent partial impairment. The law firm filed a notice of appeal in order to challenge the Commission's rule. In affirming, the supreme court found that Idaho Code Ann. § 3-205 did not limit the Commission's authority to adopt administrative rules that regulate the amount that it determined to be a reasonable attorney fee in worker's compensation proceedings. Idaho Code Ann. § 72-803 did not conflict with Idaho Code Ann. § 3-205. The Commission did not repeal § 3-205 by adopting the rule. The rule did not infringe upon judicial power where it required an attorney to show that the attorney's services operated primarily or substantially to secure the fund from which a contingent fee was sought. There was no free speech violation because it did not prevent the law firm from being paid for legal advice. Finally, there was no deprivation of liberty without due process of law under U.S. Const. amend. XIV or Idaho Const. art. I, § 13.


OUTCOME: The orders of the Commission were affirmed, and it was awarded costs on appeal. A prior opinion rendered in this case was withdrawn, and this opinion was substituted in its place.

CDA Dairy Queen, Inc. v. State Ins. Fund


Docket No. 38492, 2013 Opinion No. 44


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


2013 Ida. LEXIS 111



April 9, 2013, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] 
SUBSTITUTE OPINION, THE COURT'S PRIOR OPINION DATED JANUARY 23, 2013 IS HEREBY WITHDRAWN.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Canyon County. Hon. Renae J. Hoff, District Judge.
CDA Dairy Queen, Inc. v. State Ins. Fund, 299 P.3d 186, 2013 Ida. LEXIS 17 (Idaho, Jan. 23, 2013)



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is reversed and the case is remanded for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Third Judicial District, Canyon County, Idaho, granted respondent Idaho State Insurance Fund's (SIF) motion for summary judgment on appellant policyholder's suit seeking a declaratory judgment that SIF violated Idaho Code Ann. § 72-915 by failing to distribute premium rate adjustments on a pro rata basis. The district court fund that the retroactive repeal of § 72-915 was constitutional. The policyholder appealed.


OVERVIEW: The policyholder asked the supreme court to reverse the decision of the district court and remand for further proceedings consistent with the determination that the retroactive appeal of Idaho Code Ann. § 72-915 was unconstitutional. The supreme court noted that it would use federal rules and methodology unless clear precedent or circumstances unique to Idaho or its constitution provided greater protection. The supreme court has recognized a limited exception, based upon the state's police power, to the protection provided by Idaho Const. art. I, § 16. The challenges based upon article I, § 16 should be evaluated under the federal framework and rules. The retroactive appeal of Idaho Code Ann. § 72-915 substantially impaired the policyholder's contract rights because the dividend was part of the consideration. Repealing the statute that provided for the possibility of a premium refund reduced the maximum value of the contract to the policyholder. The legislative act adversely affected an essential element of the contracts between the parties. The retroactive repeal was not reasonable and necessary to support a significant and legitimate public purpose.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded for further proceedings.

 

37 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Seiniger Law Offices, P.A. v. State ex rel. Indus. Comm'n


Docket No. 38037, 2013 Opinion No. 21


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


2013 Ida. LEXIS 54



February 22, 2013, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at Seiniger Law Offices, P.A. v. State ex rel. Indus. Comm'n, 299 P.3d 773, 2013 Ida. LEXIS 115 (Idaho, Apr. 12, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Industrial Commission of the State of Idaho.



DISPOSITION: The orders of the Industrial Commission are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant law firm challenged orders from respondent Industrial Commission (Idaho), which denied fee requests pursuant to Idaho Admin. Code r. 17.02.08.033.01.c.ii. (1994) because the firm did not prove that its attorneys were primarily or substantially responsible for securing certain worker's compensation benefits for its clients or that such benefits were disputed.


OVERVIEW: In each case, the fee agreement provided for a 25 percent contingent fee, and the case was settled without a hearing. It was undisputed that the firm's attorneys were not primarily or substantially responsible for securing the awards from which the firm sought a percentage. The court held that the rule did not exceed the Commission's authority under Idaho Code Ann. §§ 72-803, 72-508 to adopt administrative rules regulating the amount of a reasonable attorney fee in worker's compensation proceedings. Because the measure of compensation for attorneys in worker's compensation cases was restrained by law, the rule did not improperly limit the firm's freedom to contract and did not conflict with Idaho Code Ann. § 3-205. There was no separation of powers violation because the rule did not infringe upon legislative power or upon the judiciary's power to regulate the practice of law. The First Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. I, was not violated because the firm was not prevented from giving advice to a client. The firm was given notice and an opportunity for a hearing, thus, it received due process under the Fourteenth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and Idaho Const. art. I, § 13.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders.

 

38 of 368 DOCUMENTS


CDA Dairy Queen, Inc. v. State Ins. Fund


Docket No. 38492, 2013 Opinion No. 6


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


154 Idaho 379; 299 P.3d 186; 2013 Ida. LEXIS 17



January 23, 2013, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at CDA Dairy Queen, Inc. v. State Ins. Fund, 2013 Ida. LEXIS 111 (Idaho, Apr. 9, 2013)
Rehearing denied by Cda Dairy Queen v. State Ins. Fund, 2013 Ida. LEXIS 140 (Idaho, Apr. 9, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Canyon County. Hon. Renae J. Hoff, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is reversed and the case is remanded for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants employers sought a declaratory judgment in the District Court of the Third Judicial District, Canyon County (Idaho), that respondent Idaho State Insurance Fund (SIF) violated Idaho Code Ann. § 72-915 (repealed) by not distributing premium rate readjustments on a pro rata basis. The trial court granted SIF's summary judgment motion, and the employers appealed, arguing the statute's retroactive repeal violated Idaho Const. art. I, § 16.


OVERVIEW: The employers said the repeal impaired their workers' compensation contracts with SIF. The supreme court held federal contract clause principles were applied to find if the repeal violated Idaho Const. art. I, § 16 because the Idaho Constitution did not protect contracts more than the federal constitution. The retroactive repeal of Idaho Code Ann. § 72-915 violated Idaho Const. art. I, § 16 because (1) it substantially impairs existing contracts, as it substantially impaired the employers' contract rights to a premium-based pro rata share of dividends, which was part of the consideration they paid for insurance, and (2) it was not reasonable and necessary to support a significant and legitimate public purpose, as the repeal was in response to a judicial decision requiring rate readjustments to be paid on a pro rata basis, to clarify the law on the payment of dividends.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Hom v. Idaho Fish & Game Dep't (Citizens Against Range Expansion)


Docket No. 39297, 2012 Opinion No. 137


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


153 Idaho 630; 289 P.3d 32; 2012 Ida. LEXIS 214



November 15, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 7, 2012.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Kootenai County. Hon. John T. Mitchell, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The post-judgment orders of the district court are reversed and the case is remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Idaho Department of Fish and Game (IDFG) challenged a decision from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Kootenai County, which refused to lift a portion of an injunction and declared that the Idaho Outdoor Sport Shooting Range Act was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: In response to a nuisance claim, an injunction was issued. There were two components listed for lifting the injunction. After range improvements were made, the IDFG sought to lift both components of the injunction. The trial court denied relief and found that the Act was unconstitutional. This appeal followed. In reversing, the supreme court decided to review the trial court's interpretation of its injunctive order with an abuse of discretion standard. The trial court erred by refusing to lift the 500-shooter component of the injunction because the trial court's interpretation did not follow the plain language of the injunction. The IDFG had clearly complied with the stated requirements of the injunction. Moreover, the Act was a constitutional general law, not a special law. It applied to all shooting ranges in like situations, even when considered in conjunction with HB 604. Moreover, the Act had none of the hallmarks of special laws. The Act was also not an unconstitutional deprivation of judicial power under Idaho Const. art. V, § 13.


OUTCOME: The orders were reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


154 Idaho 669; 302 P.3d 9; 2012 Ida. LEXIS 193

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 9, 2012.

Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. The Honorable Cheri C. Copsey, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the owners of a domestic elk ranch, initiated an action against governmental defendants to recover for the loss and destruction of elk that escaped from their ranch in 2006. The Fourth Judicial District Court, Ada County, Idaho, granted summary judgment in favor of defendants. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court concluded that Idaho Code Ann. § 25-3705A(3) provided authorization for the State to legally "take" the escaped domestic elk without liability. Plaintiffs presented no facts indicating that their domestic elk were taken by any non-licensed hunters. The hunt of plaintiffs' domestic elk was effectuated in a manner that complied with Title 36 of the Idaho Code. The district court's dismissal of plaintiffs' 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims on the basis of qualified immunity was proper. The district court did not abuse its discretion by awarding attorney fees to defendants under Idaho Code Ann. § 12-117. Plaintiffs pursued their claims without a reasonable basis in fact or law. Defendants were entitled to attorney fees on appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Delivery Call of A&B Irrigation Dist.


Docket No. 38403/38421/38422, 2012 Opinion No. 115


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


153 Idaho 500; 284 P.3d 225; 2012 Ida. LEXIS 180



August 2, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 24, 2012.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Minidoka County. Hon. Eric J. Wildman, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: District court decision affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant irrigation district filed a petition for a ground water to ground water delivery call. Applying Idaho Admin. Code r. 37.03.11, appellee, the Director of the Idaho Department of Water Resources (IDWR), found that the district was not materially injured. The District Court of the Fifth Judicial District, Minidoka County (Idaho), affirmed. The district appealed. Cross-appeals were filed by a city and others.


OVERVIEW: The irrigation district's delivery call was based on its senior water right. The petition sought both administration of junior priority ground water rights from its water source and a designation of the source as a ground water management area. Among other things, it alleged that junior priority groundwater pumping from the source had lowered the water table, which resulted in a reduction of the irrigation district's diversion rate. The IDWR Director properly found that the irrigation district's water right was subject to the provisions of the 1951 Idaho Ground Water Act, Idaho Code Ann. §§ 42-226 to -239, and that the irrigation district had not been required to pump water beyond a reasonable ground water pumping level. The Director had substantial and competent evidence to support his decision not to set a reasonable groundwater pumping level and to analyze the water right on a system-wide as opposed to a well-by-well basis. Finally, the district court did not err in imposing the clear and convincing evidentiary standard on the Director's determination of material injury in a delivery call.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's decision.

Friends of Minidoka v. Jerome County (In re Jerome County Bd. of Comm'rs)

43 of 368 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lee


Docket No. 39107, 2012 Opinion No. 109


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


153 Idaho 559; 286 P.3d 537; 2012 Ida. LEXIS 175



July 5, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 27, 2012.
Related proceeding at State v. Lee, 2014 Ida. LEXIS 29 (Idaho, Feb. 10, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the district court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Deborah A. Bail, district judge.
State v. Lee, 2011 Ida. App. LEXIS 47 (Idaho Ct. App., June 29, 2011)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County, which convicted him of failure to register as a sex offender in violation of Idaho Code Ann. § 18-8309 (2001) and denied his motion for a judgment of acquittal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that § 18-8309 did not require sex offenders to register or update their address information with the Idaho State Police Sex Offender Registry or the sheriff of the county where the offenders were required to register after moving to another country. The supreme court held that the evidence did not establish beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant failed to register as a sex offender in violation of § 18-8309. Section 18-8309 did not apply when an offender changed his or her address or actual residence to another country. There was no evidence that defendant changed his address to another state. There was no evidence at trial as to how defendant left Idaho. Assuming that defendant traveled through one or more states before leaving the United States, he would not necessarily have had an address in any of those states. Because § 18-8309(2) applied when an offender changed his or her address to another state, § 18-8309(1) applied when an offender changed his or her address or actual residence to another place in Idaho. The supreme court also concluded that there was insufficient evidence that defendant changed his address or actual residence to a place in Idaho.


OUTCOME: The supreme court vacated the district court's judgment of conviction and remanded the case with instructions for the entry of a judgment of acquittal.

State v. Hi Boise, LLC


Docket No. 38344, 2012 Opinion No. 103


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


153 Idaho 334; 282 P.3d 595; 2012 Ida. LEXIS 159



June 29, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 23, 2012.

As Corrected August 30, 2012.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Ronald J. Wilper, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the State of Idaho Transportation Board, brought a condemnation action against defendant company to acquire land for a highway improvement project. Defendant filed a counterclaim for inverse condemnation, claiming damages of $7.5 million for lost rights of access and visibility. The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County, summarily dismissed defendant's counterclaim. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: To complete a highway project, the State acquired two construction easements on defendant's property where it was operating a hotel. In the State's condemnation action, defendant counterclaimed for inverse condemnation and submitted a business damages claim under Idaho Code Ann. § 7-711(2)(b). Defendant claimed: (1) the State effectively condemned its primary access to its property; (2) the hotel's ability to be seen by passing motorists; and (3) produced backed-up traffic. The district court correctly dismissed defendant's circuity claim because its right of access did not include a right to continued traffic flow under Idaho law. Defendant's damages for the taking under Idaho Const. art. I, § 14 could not include the limitation of access to a driveway caused by changes in traffic flow. Motorists still had free access to and from defendant's property. Defendant had no compensable property right in continued visibility under Idaho law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Wasden v. State Bd. of Land Comm'n


Docket No. 39084, 2012 Opinion No. 104


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


153 Idaho 190; 280 P.3d 693; 2012 Ida. LEXIS 163



June 29, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 23, 2012.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Valley County. Hon. Michael R. McLaughlin, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is reversed, in part, and vacated, in part, and the case is remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney general challenged a decision from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Valley County, which dismissed a complaint alleging that Idaho Code Ann. § 58-310A was unconstitutional. Cross-appellant lessees challenged a decision to grant summary judgment in favor of cross-respondents, the State Board of Land Commissioners and the Idaho Department of Lands Director, in a lease dispute.


OVERVIEW: The case was concerning residential leases on endowment lands. The lessees contended that increased rent breached the terms of the existing leases. The attorney general contended that Idaho Code Ann. § 58-310A, which exempted cottage site leases from a conflict auction, violated Idaho Const. art. IX, § 8. The trial court dismissed the constitutional challenge and granted summary judgment against the lessees based on a failure to exhaust administrative remedies. This appeal followed. On review, the supreme court determined that the attorney general was not subject to the usual standing analysis due to his unique position as counsel for the State of Idaho; even if he was, the requirements for standing were met. Next, Idaho Code Ann. § 58-310A was unconstitutional because any disposal of endowment land had to be at public auction. The word "disposal" meant any lease or sale. The entirety of § 58-310A failed because it was not severable. The trial court erred by finding that the lessees had to first exhaust their administrative remedies prior to filing a declaratory judgment action. The merits of the contract claim were left for the trial court on remand.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed as to the constitutional challenge, and Idaho Code Ann. § 58-310A was declared unconstitutional in its entirety. The dismissal of the contract claim was vacated, and that matter was remanded for further proceedings.

Leavitt v. Craven


Docket No. 40021, 2012 Opinion No. 89


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


154 Idaho 661; 302 P.3d 1; 2012 Ida. LEXIS 141



June 8, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Complaint for Writ of Mandamus and Alternate Writ and Request for Stay of Execution.
State v. Leavitt, 153 Idaho 142, 280 P.3d 169, 2012 Ida. LEXIS 138 (Idaho, June 5, 2012)



DISPOSITION: Alternative requests for Writ of Mandamus and Alternate Writ for Stay of Execution, denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, who had been sentenced to death, filed a petition for a writ of mandamus directing respondent Idaho Commission of Pardons and Parole to schedule a full hearing on his petition for commutation and comply with its rules for such a hearing by publishing notice of the time and place of the hearing in a newspaper of general circulation at least once a week for four weeks prior to the hearing.


OVERVIEW: The court concluded that the Commission was not required to grant petitioner a full, open session hearing regarding his commutation petition. The requirement of an open session following notice and publication applied only to the Commission's decisions to grant clemency. In this case, clemency was effectively denied. The Commission's decision to deny the petition for commutation in executive session did not violate Idaho Const. art. IV, § 7. The plain language of the relevant statutes permitted the Commission to meet in executive session. Filing a commutation petition did not grant petitioner the automatic right to a public hearing.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's requests for a writ of mandamus, alternative writ, and stay of execution.

State v. Koivu


Docket No. 38106, 2012 Opinion No. 32

152 Idaho 511; 272 P.3d 483; 2012 Ida. LEXIS 54

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Bonner County. The Hon. Benjamin Simpson, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed an order of the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Bonner County, suppressing methamphetamine obtained from defendant incident to an arrest pursuant to a wrongly issued warrant.


OVERVIEW: The court held that it had jurisdiction over the appeal because the parties and the trial court proceeded as if a motion to suppress had been filed by defendant, albeit maybe implicitly, and the trial court granted the motion, and therefore the State had the right to appeal under Idaho App. R. 11(c)(7). The court upheld the trial court's order holding that the methamphetamine was not admissible into evidence because defendant's arrest pursuant to an invalid warrant of attachment violated his rights under Idaho Const. art. I, § 17. To overrule Guzman and hold that the exclusionary rule's sole purpose was to deter police misconduct, the court would also have to overrule Arregui, which adopted the exclusionary rule in Idaho in a case in which there was no police misconduct. The court held that the State had not pointed to anything in the record showing that during the last 85 years Arregui had proved to be unwise or unjust.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

State v. Adamcik


Docket No. 34639, 2012 Opinion No. 23


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


152 Idaho 445; 272 P.3d 417; 2012 Ida. LEXIS 32



January 25, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: SUBSTITUTE OPINION. THE COURT'S PRIOR OPINION DATED NOVEMBER 29, 2011 IS HEREBY WITHDRAWN.
Rehearing denied by State v. Adamcik, 2012 Ida. LEXIS 47 (Idaho, Feb. 8, 2012)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Adamcik v. Idaho, 184 L. Ed. 2d 68, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 7411 (U.S., Oct. 1, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Sixth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Bannock County. Honorable Peter D. McDermott, District Judge.
State v. Adamcik, 2011 Ida. LEXIS 158 (Idaho, Nov. 29, 2011)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of conviction for first-degree murder and conspiracy to commit first-degree murder is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of the Sixth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Bannock County, convicting him of first-degree murder and conspiracy to commit first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: The evidence was sufficient to support defendant's first-degree murder conviction because: (1) the medical examiner testified that the victim died from multiple stab wounds and at least two knives were used; (2) defendant's friend testified that he bought four knives for defendant and his accomplice, using money given to him by defendant and his accomplice; (3) defendant and his accomplice were recorded discussing their plan to kill the victim; (4) defendant and his accomplice were together immediately after the victim's murder; (5) defendant and his accomplice jointly tried to hide weapons and clothing used during the murder; and (6) defendant made verbal and nonverbal assertions during the police interview that could be reasonably construed as confessing to stabbing the victim. The evidence was also sufficient to convict defendant under an aiding and abetting theory under Idaho Code Ann. § 19-1430 because there was evidence that: (1) defendant and his accomplice were in the house lying in wait for the victim; (2) two knives were used in the murder, both of which potentially caused her death; and (3) video footage showed defendant's preparation for and involvement in the murder.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

49 of 368 DOCUMENTS



Twin Falls County v. Idaho Comm'n on Redistricting


Docket No. 39373, 2012 Opinion No. 16


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


152 Idaho 346; 271 P.3d 1202; 2012 Ida. LEXIS 24



January 18, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Petition challenging the legislative redistricting plan adopted by the commission for reapportionment.



DISPOSITION: The plan violates the Idaho Constitution and is therefore invalid.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner municipalities challenged the constitutionality of a legislative redistricting plan adopted by respondent Idaho Commission on Redistricting.


OVERVIEW: The redistricting plan divided 12 counties. Before adopting the redistricting plan, the Commission considered and rejected other plans that complied with federal constitutional requirements and that divided fewer counties. The court held that the plan was invalid because it divided more counties than necessary to comply with federal constitutional requirements. Pursuant to Idaho Const. art. III, § 5, and Idaho Code Ann. § 72-1506(5), the total number of divided counties in a legislative redistricting plan had to be the minimum number required to comply with the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The Commission had discretion in adopting a redistricting plan that divided counties only to the extent that counties had to be divided to comply with the federal Constitution; moreover, division of counties had to be avoided whenever possible. Because the Commission exceeded the scope of this discretion, it was necessary for the Commission to reconvene and adopt a revised plan pursuant to Idaho Code Ann. § 72-1501(2).


OUTCOME: The court ordered that the redistricting plan be revised.


 

50 of 368 DOCUMENTS


State v. Manzanares


Docket No. 35703, 2012 Opinion No. 9


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


152 Idaho 410; 272 P.3d 382; 2012 Ida. LEXIS 9



January 6, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Third Judicial District, State of Idaho, Canyon County. Hon. Thomas J. Ryan, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment entered upon guilty plea to recruiting criminal gang member, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to recruiting a criminal gang member under Idaho Code Ann. § 18-8504(1)(a) in exchange for the dismissal of a charge for providing a firearm to a criminal gang member under Idaho Code Ann. § 18-8505. The District Court of the Third Judicial District, State of Idaho, Canyon County, imposed a 10-year unified sentence with two years fixed for the recruiting charge. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The recruiting provision in Idaho Code Ann. § 18-8504(1)(a) of the Idaho Criminal Gang Enforcement Act (ICGEA), Idaho Code Ann. § 18-8501 et seq., did not criminalize joining, or advocating for the lawful goals of, an organization that happened to be a criminal gang under the ICGEA. While there might be imaginable instances in which § 18-8504(1)(a) penalized conduct protected under the First Amendment, the statute did not implicate a substantial amount of constitutionally protected conduct. Thus, the recruiting provision was not facially overbroad. Further, because the charging information did not set forth the specific conduct by which defendant allegedly recruited a gang member, and because, by entering an Alford plea, defendant did not admit to any conduct on her part which related to the charge, the appellate court could not ascertain how the recruiting provision was applied to defendant. Thus, defendant failed to show how the recruiting provision was applied to her in a manner that infringed upon her First Amendment rights. Therefore, her conviction pursuant to her conditional plea agreement was upheld.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the district court's judgment.

State v. Johnson


Docket No. 37758, 2011 Opinion No. 130


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


152 Idaho 41; 266 P.3d 1146; 2011 Ida. LEXIS 181



December 8, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 3, 2012.
Later proceeding at State v. Johnson, 2012 Ida. LEXIS 10 (Idaho, Jan. 3, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Canyon County. Hon. Juneal C. Kerrick, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Third Judicial District, Canyon County, Idaho, determined that the 2009 amendments to the Idaho Sexual Offender Registration Notification and Community Right-to-Know Act (SORA) precluded exemptions from sex offender registration requirements and denied defendant's petition. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court noted that the only real issue was whether the Legislature's classification of defendant's offense as an "aggravated offense," subsequent to his guilty plea, was an exception to the general understanding that SORA was nonpunitive. The fact that a sexual offender, convicted of a certain class of crime, may be required to register for life was not so punitive that it overrode SORA's regulatory purpose. This was particularly so because the Legislature need not make particularized findings in the regulatory context. It was unclear how the 2009 SORA amendments could impair defendant's plea agreement. The 2009 amendments did not attach additional notoriety to his registration status but affected his ability to petition for exemption. He had not been deprived of due process. Sexual offenders seeking SORA exemption under Idaho Code Ann. § 18-8310(1) had to file their petition in a new civil action if their criminal case had been dismissed or fully adjudicated, and the time for appeal had run. The district court had dismissed defendant's case seven years earlier. It lacked jurisdiction to consider the merits of defendant's petition.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated.

State v. Delling


Docket No. 36920/36921, 2011 Opinion No. 128


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


152 Idaho 122; 267 P.3d 709; 2011 Ida. LEXIS 174



December 1, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Delling, 2012 Ida. LEXIS 39 (Idaho, Jan. 27, 2012)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Delling v. Idaho, 133 S. Ct. 504, 184 L. Ed. 2d 480, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 8896 (U.S., 2012)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Delling v. State, 2016 Ida. App. Unpub. LEXIS 143 (Idaho Ct. App., Mar. 18, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Deborah Ann Bail, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment, conviction and sentence for two counts of second-degree murder, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County, Idaho, convicted defendant, pursuant to guilty pleas, of two counts of second-degree murder. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Idaho Code Ann. § 18-207, the legislative abrogation of mental condition as a defense, violated U.S. Const. amends. V, VI, VIII, and XIV, and Idaho Const. art. I, §§ 2, 7, and 13. The supreme court found that the opinions referenced by defendant did not appear to question the wisdom of the statutes or the interpreting opinions. Evidence of mental illness was expressly allowed and could rebut the element of intent. Defendant's right to due process was not infringed by the abolition of the insanity defense. In the absence of an insanity defense, defendant was still able to present a defense. The existing Idaho precedent held that an independent defense of insanity was not required, and that evidence of mental illness could still be used to rebut the intent element of a crime. Defendant's Eighth Amendment protection for cruel and unusual punishment was not violated. The sentence imposed by the district court was within the statutory allowances for second-degree murder, Idaho Code Ann. § 18-4004. The district judge adequately addressed the issues of mental illness as required by Idaho Code Ann. § 19-2523.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

53 of 368 DOCUMENTS


State v. Adamcik


Docket No. 34639, 2010 Opinion No. 121


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


2011 Ida. LEXIS 158



November 29, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at State v. Adamcik, 272 P.3d 417, 2012 Ida. LEXIS 32 (Idaho, Jan. 25, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Sixth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Bannock County. Honorable Peter D. McDermott, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of conviction for first-degree murder and conspiracy to commit first-degree murder is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of the Sixth Judicial District, Bannock County, Idaho, that convicted him of first-degree murder and conspiracy to commit first-degree murder, arguing that the evidence was insufficient to support his convictions because the State failed to show that he inflicted the fatal stab would that killed the victim.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's convictions; the medical examiner testified that 12 of the 30 knife wounds on the victim's body were potentially fatal. Although he was unable to identify the specific wound that caused the victim's death, he testified that she died as a result of more than one of those 12 wounds and indicated that one of those wounds was inflicted by a knife with a non-serrated blade, while the remainder were caused by a knife with a serrated blade. Regardless of which knife defendant used, the evidence permitted the jury to conclude that he inflicted the fatal wound. Further, there was sufficient evidence to convict under an aiding and abetting theory. Both defendant and co-defendant lay in wait for the victim, and two knives were used in the murder, both of which potentially caused the death. Because there was no evidence that a single person, holding both knives, inflicted all of the stab wounds, it was both reasonable and likely for the jury to infer that defendant and co-defendant both stabbed the victim until she died. It was simply unnecessary for the State to prove that defendant inflicted the fatal wound.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant of first-degree murder and conspiracy to commit first-degree murder and imposing a fixed life sentence was affirmed.

Sopatyk v. Lemhi County


Docket No. 37186, 2011 Opinion No. 114


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


151 Idaho 809; 264 P.3d 916; 2011 Ida. LEXIS 150



November 9, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 1, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Lemhi County. Hon. Joel E. Tingey, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court affirming the validation of Anderson Creek Road is affirmed. No attorney's fees are awarded. Costs are awarded to Respondent Lemhi County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Seventh Judicial District, Lemhi County, Idaho, affirmed respondent Lemhi County Board of Commissioners' (Board) decision to validate a road, which ran the length of appellant landowner's property. The owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court found that the road was a public road under R.S. 2477 (1873). There was substantial evidence that the road existed in 1881 and there was substantial evidence from which the Board could infer that the public commonly used the road in 1881. Respondent county had substantial evidence on which to find that the owner could not meet the burden of showing that the road went unused for any five year period. Since 1906, the road had accessed public forest lands, a reasonable basis upon which to infer that the public had been using the road for recreation and wood gathering. The road was not abandoned. The owner's Takings Clause, Idaho Const. art. I, § 14 and U.S. Const. amend. V, claim was without merit as neither he nor his predecessors had been deprived of any property. It was in the public interest for the road to be a public highway, Idaho Code Ann. § 40-203A. The county had authority to validate the road even though it intruded into a national forest and could validate it as a fifty-foot wide road, Idaho Code Ann. § 40-2312. The Commissioner did not violate Idaho Code Ann. § 31-807A. Neither party was entitled to attorney's fees.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

55 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Lewiston Indep. Sch. Dist. #1 v. City of Lewiston


Docket No. 38116, 2011 Opinion No. 113


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


151 Idaho 800; 264 P.3d 907; 2011 Ida. LEXIS 148



November 7, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 29, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Nez Perce County. Hon. John H. Bradbury, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is affirmed. Costs are awarded to respondents. No attorney's fees are awarded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a summary judgment from the District Court of the Second Judicial District, Nez Perce County (Idaho), which granted a declaratory judgment to respondent government entities that the city's stormwater fee was an unconstitutional tax.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted an ordinance that created a stormwater utility and imposed a stormwater fee for the operation and maintenance of the stormwater system. Some property owners whose runoff did not enter the city's stormwater drain were subject to the fee. The ordinance contained no pollution control restrictions or other provisions relating to stormwater regulation. The activities funded by the fee included some street maintenance work, and the revenues were not kept segregated from other city funds. The court concluded that the stormwater fee was an unauthorized tax that served the non-regulatory purpose of raising revenue for cleaning, maintaining, and expanding the city's streets and stormwater infrastructure. The benefits provided were a pollutant-free stormwater system and clean streets, which were shared by the general public and were not direct services. The stormwater charge was not a fee incidental to regulation and enacted pursuant to the city's police powers under Idaho Const. art. XII, § 2. As such, it required legislative authorization pursuant to Idaho Const. art. VII, § 6, and its imposition on other governmental entities was prohibited by Idaho Const. art. VII, § 4.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court.
