Hernandez v. Hernandez


Docket No. 37779, Docket No. 37780, 2011 Opinion No. 108


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


151 Idaho 882; 265 P.3d 495; 2011 Ida. LEXIS 143



November 2, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 28, 2011. As Corrected February 10, 2012.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Elmore County. Hon. George G. Hicks, Magistrate Judge; Hon. Michael E. Wetherell, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a custody dispute between appellant, the biological father of two minor children, and respondent, the children's maternal grandmother, a magistrate granted the parties shared physical custody of the children. The Fourth Judicial District Court, Elmore County, Idaho, affirmed the magistrate's decision. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The statute at issue in this case was Idaho Code § 32-717(3), which provides that a court may recognize a grandparent as having the same standing as a parent for evaluating what custody arrangements are in the best interests of the child. The court held that the district court correctly upheld the facial constitutionality of § 32-717(3). The court also held that the statute was constitutional as applied to the father. The magistrate carefully considered the best interests of the children, the fact that they had formed a strong bond with their grandmother, and the fact that the father had tried to have a better relationship with them despite some resistance from the grandmother. After considering at length what would be in the best interest of the children, the magistrate concluded that the father should have sole legal custody and he should share physical custody with the grandmother. The magistrate gave due regard to the father's parental rights, but balanced them with the competing interests of the children. The father did not demonstrate how the magistrate's findings infringed on his rights.


OUTCOME: The decision of the district court was affirmed.

 

57 of 368 DOCUMENTS


State v. Peregrina


Docket No. 37900, 2011 Opinion No. 96


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


151 Idaho 538; 261 P.3d 815; 2011 Ida. LEXIS 129



September 7, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 7, 2011.
Appeal after remand at, Decision reached on appeal by State v. Peregrina, 2012 Ida. App. Unpub. LEXIS 384 (Idaho Ct. App., Oct. 19, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Darla S. Williamson, District Judge.
State v. Peregrina, 2010 Ida. App. LEXIS 21 (Idaho Ct. App., Mar. 24, 2010)



DISPOSITION: District court ruling on divisibility, remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury of the Fourth Judicial District Court, Ada County, Idaho, found defendant guilty of two counts of aggravated battery while using a firearm. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that there was insufficient evidence to support the district court's "implicit" finding that the crimes arose out of divisible courses of conduct, and that even if there was, the State had the burden to submit the issue of divisibility to the jury and prove it beyond a reasonable doubt. The court concluded that a finding of divisibility was not subject to Apprendi v. New Jersey and could be found by the trial judge. The statutory maximum for each crime was 30 years. Idaho Code Ann. § 19-2520E would decrease the statutory maximum penalty as to one of defendant's convictions if both of his crimes arose out of the same divisible course of conduct. Thus, § 19-2520E would operate to reduce defendant's maximum sentence for one of his convictions, not to increase it. As a result, it was within the inherent authority of the trial judge to make a finding regarding the divisibility or indivisibility of defendant's crimes. However, there was no such finding made, and the matter had to be remanded to the district court.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the district court for a finding of divisibility or indivisibility of defendant's conduct, followed by sentencing consistent with that finding.

 

58 of 368 DOCUMENTS


State v. Flegel


Docket No. 35117, 2011 Opinion No. 94


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


151 Idaho 525; 261 P.3d 519; 2011 Ida. LEXIS 128



September 6, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 28, 2011.
As Corrected October 20, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Ada County. The Hon. Michael E. Wetherell, District Judge.
State v. Flegel, 2007 Ida. App. LEXIS 110 (Idaho Ct. App., Dec. 5, 2007)



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Idaho sought review of an order from the Idaho Court of Appeals, which vacated defendant's conviction for sexual abuse of a child under 16 years of age and remanded the case for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant not guilty of lewd conduct with a child under 16 years of age. Without resubmitting the matter to a grand jury, the State filed an amended indictment charging him with sexual abuse of a child under 16 years of age. Defendant was tried by a jury on that charge and found guilty. The court of appeals vacated the judgment and remanded the case for a new trial. On review, the court held that because sexual abuse, in violation of Idaho Code Ann. § 18-1506(1)(b), was not a lesser-included offense of lewd conduct, in violation of Idaho Code Ann. § 18-1508, defendant could only be validly charged by indictment with that crime if the matter was resubmitted to a grand jury and it returned an amended indictment. The prosecuting attorney had no authority under Idaho Const. art. I, § 8 to issue an amended indictment for a crime that was not charged in the original indictment and that was not an included offense of that crime. Because the amended indictment charged a different crime than the crime charged in the original indictment, the amended indictment was a nullity under Idaho Code Ann. § 19-1401.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of the court of appeals and remanded the case to the trial court with instructions to dismiss the case without prejudice.

Allied Bail Bonds, Inc. v. County of Kootenai


Docket No. 36861, 2011 Opinion No. 81


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


151 Idaho 405; 258 P.3d 340; 2011 Ida. LEXIS 107



July 8, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 4, 2011. As Corrected October 5, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Kootenai County. Hon. John T. Mitchell, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bail bond company sought review of a judgment from the District Court of the First Judicial District, Kootenai County (Idaho), which dismissed its claims against respondents, a county, its sheriff, and others, alleging breach of a settlement agreement and other causes of action.


OVERVIEW: The settlement agreement addressed the process for informing inmates of bail bond options. The company alleged that accepting bail bond payments by credit card breached the agreement. The court held that a claim under Idaho Const. art. VIII, § 4, which equated to a cause of action for tortious interference with a business relationship, was properly dismissed for lack of timely notice of the claim under Idaho Code Ann. § 6-908. The sheriff was entitled to dismissal under Idaho Code Ann. § 6-610(4), (5) because the company's filing of a bond one day after it initiated the lawsuit did not comply with the requirement of § 6-610(2) that bond be posted as a condition precedent to suit. Under the doctrine of functus officio, considered in light of Idaho R. Civ. P. 15(c), an amended complaint related back to the date of the original complaint. A public records claim was properly dismissed because the company requested only attorney fees and did not seek the Idaho Code Ann. § 9-343(1) remedy of compelled document production. The county commissioners' supervisory authority under Idaho Code Ann. § 31-802 to control other constitutional officers did not extend to the sheriff's bail procedures.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court.

 

60 of 368 DOCUMENTS


State v. Folk


Docket No. 36244, 2011 Opinion No. 80


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


151 Idaho 327; 256 P.3d 735; 2011 Ida. LEXIS 103



June 30, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 27, 2011.
Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by State v. Folk, 2014 Ida. App. LEXIS 120 (Idaho Ct. App., Nov. 20, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Bonneville County. The Hon. Jon J. Shindurling, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District in and for Bonneville County, Idaho, that convicted him of lewd conduct, arguing that the trial court impermissibly infringed upon his right of self-representation and upon his right to confrontation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with lewd conduct by having oral-genital contact with a child, and he elected to represent himself. The trial court entered an order specifying that the child would testify by closed-circuit television, that defendant was not to speak during the child's testimony, and that standby counsel would voice any objections and cross-examine the child. On review, the court held that, because the child was the only person who could testify to the alleged sexual abuse, requiring defendant to write out questions to be asked by someone else in order to cross-examine the child was a significant impairment of the right to confrontation. Where there was no evidence that testifying in defendant's presence or being cross-examined by defendant would have a devastating emotional effect upon the child or that defendant, if permitted to conduct the cross-examination, would seek to intimidate the child or otherwise abuse the right of cross-examination, the trial court violated defendant's confrontation right and likewise infringed upon his right of self-representation in precluding defendant from cross-examining the complainant himself.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was vacated, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Hall v. State


Docket No. 35055, 2011 Opinion No. 67


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


151 Idaho 42; 253 P.3d 716; 2011 Ida. LEXIS 89



May 27, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected June 7, 2011.

Released for Publication June 21, 2011.
Post-conviction proceeding at Hall v. State, 2013 Ida. LEXIS 342 (Idaho, Dec. 2, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Thomas F. Neville, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Permissive appeal from two interlocutory orders, district court decision affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County, which denied his postconviction motions for juror contact and to depose an investigator for his trial counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder, first-degree kidnapping, and rape. He was sentenced to death for the murder, with consecutive unified fixed life sentences for the kidnapping and rape. The trial court denied his postconviction motion for juror contact. The trial court also denied his postconviction motion to depose an investigator for his trial counsel. On appeal, the court held that the trial court had the inherent authority to enter an order barring contact with the jurors absent prior court approval. The trial court's order did not violate defense counsels' rights under the First Amendment to the United States Constitution, U.S. Const. amend. I. Although the trial court erred in finding that Idaho R. Evid. 606(b) restricted the permissible scope of postconviction juror interviews to those topics on which the jurors themselves might testify, it was correct in finding that lines of inquiry related to the jurors' deliberations, mental processes, minds, or emotions were improper. The trial court did not err in denying defendant's request to depose the investigator because the investigator was not a decisionmaker on what evidence was introduced, known, or unknown.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Ciszek v. Kootenai County Bd. of Comm'rs


Docket No. 37562, 2011 Opinion No. 60


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


151 Idaho 123; 254 P.3d 24; 2011 Ida. LEXIS 85

63 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Idaho Power Co. v. Idaho Dep't of Water Res. (In re Licensed Water Right No. 03-7018)


Docket No. 37348, 2011 Opinion No. 63


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


151 Idaho 266; 255 P.3d 1152; 2011 Ida. LEXIS 84



May 26, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 21, 2011. As Amended September 30, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Washington County. The Honorable Susan E. Wiebe, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Idaho Department of Water Resources, sought review of an order from the District Court of the Third Judicial District, Washington County (Idaho), which required the Department to strike a term condition from respondent power company's hydropower water right license.


OVERVIEW: The Department issued a permit requiring the power company to submit proof that the project had been completed and that the water had been applied to beneficial use by a specified date. The permit did not include a condition limiting the water right to a term of years. The power company submitted the proof required by the permit. Shortly after the enactment of Idaho Code Ann. § 42-203B, which authorized the Department to limit a permit or license involving hydropower rights to a term of years, the Department conducted a beneficial use examination and issued a favorable report. More than two decades later, the Department issued a license that contained a term condition. The court held that the Department did not exceed its statutory authority under § 42-203B by including the term condition because § 42-203B(6), (7) authorized a term condition in a license issued after the statute was enacted, even if such a term was not included in the original permit. The power company did not have a vested right in the water until the license was issued pursuant to Idaho Code Ann. § 42-219. No authority supported the power company's argument that the lengthy delay should entitle it to relief.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order.

Ada County Highway Dist. v. Idaho Pub. Utils.


Docket No. 37294 2011 Opinion No. 56


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


151 Idaho 1; 253 P.3d 675; 2011 Ida. LEXIS 78



May 25, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 21, 2011.
As Corrected August 3, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Idaho Public Utilities Commission.



DISPOSITION: The order of the Commission is set aside.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county highway district challenged an order from respondent Public Utilities Commission (Idaho), which revised respondent power company's tariff with respect to relocating electricity transmission facilities within public rights-of-way.


OVERVIEW: The challenged provisions of the amended tariff allowed the Commission to allocate all or a portion of the costs of relocation to a third party upon finding that the relocation benefited the third party, even if the third party had not requested service, and required other parties involved in the planning process to use their best efforts to minimize relocation costs. The court noted that there was a justiciable controversy regarding the legality of the amended tariff. The court held that the amended tariff did not usurp the district's exclusive jurisdiction over public rights-of-way as set forth in Idaho Code Ann. §§ 40-1310(1), 62-705 because the district's statutory authority, which included implied powers pursuant to Idaho Code Ann. § 40-1312, did not extend to determining whether third parties should pay for electric utility relocations. The Commission exceeded its authority under Idaho Code Ann. §§ 61-501, 61-502, 61-503, 61-507 by attempting to exercise jurisdiction over third parties and to allocate relocation costs to third parties that had not requested service; thus, the challenged provisions of the amended tariff had to be set aside.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the challenged amendments to the rule.

Miller v. Idaho State Patrol


Docket No. 37032, 2011 Opinion No. 52


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


150 Idaho 856; 252 P.3d 1274; 2011 Ida. LEXIS 72



May 18, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 13, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bonner County. Hon. John T. Mitchell, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is vacated. This case is remanded with instructions to enter judgment in favor of Appellants. No attorney fees are awarded. Costs are awarded to Appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the Idaho State Patrol and a police officer, sought review of an order from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bonner County, which denied their motions for summary judgment in an action by plaintiff for violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and assault, battery, negligence, and negligent supervision.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff brought an action against defendants, claiming under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 that an involuntary catheterization after he was arrested for DUI violated his constitutional rights. The trial court denied defendants' motions for summary judgment. On appeal, the court held that the officer was entitled to qualified immunity from plaintiff's claims under § 1983 because the law regarding forced catheterizations was unsettled. Further, the trial court erred in refusing to dismiss plaintiff's intentional tort claims against defendants. A catheterization was a urine test for drugs present in a suspect's body, and because the parties agreed that there was probable cause to believe that plaintiff was operating a vehicle while under the influence of drugs, he impliedly consented to the catheterization under Idaho Code Ann. § 18-8002(1). Plaintiff failed to satisfy his burden under Idaho Code Ann. § 6-903(e) of showing that the officer, who was acting during the course and scope of his employment, acted maliciously or with criminal intent. Because the officer was not liable for any intentional torts against plaintiff, the State Patrol was not vicariously liable either.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's judgment and remanded the case with instructions to enter judgment in favor of defendants.

 

66 of 368 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fluewelling


Docket No. 36648, 2011 Opinion No. 29


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


150 Idaho 576; 249 P.3d 375; 2011 Ida. LEXIS 52



March 17, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 11, 2011. As Corrected May 27, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Ada County. The Hon. Ronald J. Wilper, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, in and for Ada County, Idaho, that convicted him of possession of marijuana with intent to deliver in violation of Idaho Code Ann. § 37-2732(a)(1)(B), arguing that the trial court erred in denying his motion to dismiss because his prosecution violated his right to practice his religion, in which marijuana was used as a sacrament.


OVERVIEW: In a search of defendant's home, the police uncovered nine grams of marijuana. Defendant waived his Miranda rights and spoke with officers, telling them that he was an ordained minister and that he provided marijuana to be smoked by his friends as a sacrament. Based upon his admissions, he was charged with possession with intent to distribute. On review, the court held that, while defendant would have been charged with simple possession under Idaho Code Ann. § 37-2732(c)(3), a misdemeanor, his admission that he supplied it to others made it the felony offense of possession with intent to distribute. Idaho Code Ann. § 37-2732(a)(1)(B) did not violate defendant's right to practice his religion because the statute was of general application and did not proscribe any conduct engaged in for religious reasons or because of the religious belief it portrays. It was entirely neutral with respect to religion, and it did not directly or indirectly give a preference to any religious denomination or mode of worship. While the states could not regulate religious beliefs, religiously motivated conduct could be regulated under an otherwise valid statute of general application.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

Doe v. Doe (In re Doe)


Docket No. 37739, 2011 Opinion No. 21


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


150 Idaho 432; 247 P.3d 659; 2011 Ida. LEXIS 25



February 8, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 4, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Christopher M. Bieter, Magistrate Judge. Hon. Kathryn A. Sticklen, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is affirmed. No attorney fees are awarded. Costs are awarded to Respondents.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents sought review of a decision entered by the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County, which affirmed a magistrate court's decision that it was not in the best interests of the parents' minor children to terminate a guardianship. Respondent guardians had been appointed the children's general guardians after the parents were arrested in Utah on drug charges.


OVERVIEW: The parents had sought to terminate the guardianship, and the magistrate signed a stipulated order setting conditions for visitation, which included a requirement that the parents locate a counselor for the visitations. Another petition to terminate was filed, and the magistrate court found that the parents had not shown that the termination would be in the children's best interests, particularly as the parents had failed to comply with the visitation order. The court affirmed. Although the parents claimed that they were not required to show that termination was in the children's best interests as they were the natural parents and the circumstances giving rise to the guardianship had ended, the preclusion of a best interest consideration had been applied to the standard for the appointment of a permanent guardianship rather than termination of a guardianship by removal under Idaho Code Ann. § 15-5-212(a). The standard for termination in the statute explicitly included a best interest standard. The guardians were not entitled to attorney's fees under Idaho Code Ann. § 12-121 because the parents presented a non-frivolous issue as it was supported by authority from a sister state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's decision. The court declined to award attorney's fees to the guardians.

Halvorson v. N. Latah County Highway Dist.


Docket No. 36825, 2011 Opinion No. 12


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


151 Idaho 196; 254 P.3d 497; 2011 Ida. LEXIS 11



February 2, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 21, 2011.
As Corrected September 14, 2011.
Rehearing denied by Halvorson v. N. Latah County Highway Dist., 2011 Ida. LEXIS 115 (Idaho, Mar. 21, 2011)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Halvorson v. N. Latah County Highway Dist., 132 S. Ct. 118, 181 L. Ed. 2d 42, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 5511 (U.S., Oct. 3, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Latah County. Hon. Carl B. Kerrick, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of a summary judgment and orders from the District Court of the Second Judicial District (Idaho), which ruled that respondents, a highway district and individual officials, had no liability on the owners' tort, takings, and due process constitutional claims arising from highway maintenance. The district court denied leave to amend the complaint and awarded attorney fees to the highway district.


OVERVIEW: After installing a fence beside a public road, the owners complained of damage to their fence from the highway district's maintenance work. The court held that the road was a public highway by prescription as defined by Idaho Code Ann. § 40-202(3). Although Idaho Code Ann. §§ 40-203A, 40-1310 contemplated a validation proceeding and action by the highway district, the district court had power to determine whether the road was a public highway. There was no violation of the owners' rights to procedural and substantive due process. A takings claim under the Fifth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. V, was untimely under Idaho Code Ann. § 5-224. Because Idaho Code Ann. § 40-2312 established a mandatory width of 50 feet for prescriptive highways and the district's undisputed evidence showed that all maintenance took place within the 50-foot right of way, summary judgment was proper. Because the owners' claims lacked merit, leave to amend under Idaho R. Civ. P. 15(a) was properly denied. The district was entitled to attorney fees under Idaho Code Ann. § 12-117 because it was a taxing district pursuant to Idaho Code Ann. §§ 40-1308, 63-3101 and the owners' claims lacked a reasonable basis.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Sixth Judicial District, Bannock County, Idaho, awarded respondent homeowners $896,531.70 in compensatory and punitive damages and the other homeowners $494,033.74, finding appellant realtors liable for breach of fiduciary duty, negligence, breach of express or implied contract and unjust enrichment. State v. Idaho State Bd. of Land Comm'r (In re Verified Petition)


Docket No. 37528, 2010 Opinion No. 144


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


150 Idaho 547; 249 P.3d 346; 2010 Ida. LEXIS 230



December 23, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
SUBSTITUTE OPINION, THE COURT'S PRIOR OPINION DATED DECEMBER 1, 2010 IS HEREBY WITHDRAWN.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Issuance of Writ of Prohibition filed by Hon. Lawrence G. Wasden, Attorney General.
Wasden ex rel. State v. Idaho State Bd. of Land Comm'rs (In re Verified Petition for Issuance of a Writ of Prohibition), 2010 Ida. LEXIS 206 (Idaho, Dec. 1, 2010)



DISPOSITION: The motion to dismiss is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Attorney General sought a writ of prohibition to stop respondent Director of the Idaho Department of Lands (IDL) from executing new lease agreements on recreational home sites (cottage sites).


OVERVIEW: The Attorney General argued that the proposed lease agreements (cottage leases) for the cottage sites violated both the Idaho Constitution and Idaho Code Ann. § 58-310A by failing to secure the maximum long-term financial return for the beneficiaries of the Idaho public lands trust, and failing to generate market rent. The supreme court found that there was a plain, speedy, and adequate remedy in the ordinary course of law as required by Idaho Code Ann. § 7-402, a remedy that was available by means of joining an action for declaratory judgment with a request for injunctive relief. The availability of preliminary injunctive relief was sufficiently "speedy" as to warrant denial of the requested writ of prohibition. The legal issues presented by the Attorney General's claims involved the scope of the Land Board's discretion to determine "market rent" as required by Idaho Code Ann. § 58-310A. If the supreme court were to issue the writ, it would not serve to prohibit future conduct in violation of the Land Board's statutory or constitutional duties.


OUTCOME: The Land Board's motion to dismiss was granted.

 

71 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Wasden v. Idaho State Bd. of Land Comm'rs (In re Verified Petition for Issuance of a Writ of Prohibition)


Docket No. 37528, 2010 Opinion No. 128


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


2010 Ida. LEXIS 205



December 1, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Wasden ex rel. State v. Idaho State Bd. of Land Comm'rs (In re Verified Petition for Issuance of a Writ of Prohibition), 2010 Ida. LEXIS 206 (Idaho, Dec. 1, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Petition for Issuance of Writ of Prohibition filed by Hon. Lawrence G. Wasden, Attorney General.



DISPOSITION: The motion to dismiss is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the Attorney General of Idaho, sought a writ of prohibition to prevent respondents, the Director of the Idaho Department of Lands and the Idaho State Board of Land Commissioners, from executing new lease agreements on recreational home sites.


OVERVIEW: The parties disputed whether the proposed lease agreements would generate market rent as required by Idaho Code Ann. § 58-310A and whether they would obtain the maximum long-term financial return as required by Idaho Const. art. IX, § 8. The court concluded that a writ of prohibition would be inappropriate because there was a plain, speedy, and adequate remedy in the ordinary course of law within the meaning of Idaho Code Ann. § 7-402, by means of joining an action for declaratory judgment with a request for injunctive relief. A preliminary injunction under Idaho R. Civ. P. 65(e)(1) was within the scope of the adequate remedies in the ordinary course of law contemplated by § 7-402. The court further observed that the effectiveness of the writ was doubtful because it would not prohibit conduct with regard to future leases, as to which it would have only an advisory effect. In an action for declaratory and injunctive relief, the district court would be in the best position to assess the fundamental factual question of whether the State Board of Land Commissioners had violated its constitutional or statutory duties or whether it had acted within its discretion.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the petition for writ of prohibition.

 

72 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Woods v. Sanders


Docket No. 37483, 2010 Opinion No. 122


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


150 Idaho 53; 244 P.3d 197; 2010 Ida. LEXIS 199



November 26, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 22, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Gooding County. Hon. Casey Robinson, Magistrate Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the magistrate court as to physical and legal custody is affirmed. The decision of the magistrate court as to the award of attorneys fees is affirmed. Respondent is awarded attorneys fees and costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother, proceeding pro se, sought review of an order from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Gooding County, which awarded sole legal and physical custody of the parties' child to respondent father, and awarded the father attorney fees. The father sought attorney fees and sanctions on appeal.


OVERVIEW: The parties had joint legal and physical custody of their son. The father filed a motion to modify custody, seeking sole physical and legal custody. The mother did not appear at trial. The trial court awarded sole legal and physical custody to the father. The trial court also awarded the father attorney fees under Idaho Code Ann. § 12-121. On appeal, the court declined to review the issues presented by the mother because she failed to properly support them in her brief, as required by Idaho App. R. 35(a)(6), and failed to properly preserve them in the trial court. The trial court had substantial competent evidence to award custody to the father based on his trial testimony. Because the mother did not provide any admissible evidence to support her defense against the custody modification other than the unsupported allegations presented in her affidavit, and because she failed to attend the trial or any other hearing, the trial court had sufficient evidence to conclude that she acted unreasonably in defending the modification motion. Hence, the trial court did not err in awarding attorney fees to the father.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court awarded appellate attorney fees and costs to the father. The court declined to impose sanctions against the mother.

 

73 of 368 DOCUMENTS


State v. Frederick


Docket No. 36493, 2010 Opinion No. 89


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


149 Idaho 509; 236 P.3d 1269; 2010 Ida. LEXIS 144



July 27, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 20, 2010.
As Corrected October 6, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Canyon County. Hon. Juneal C. Kerrick, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court denying the motion to suppress is reversed and the case is remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The district court denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence seized during a search of his automobile after he was arrested on a warrant for failure to appear in court. He entered a conditional plea of guilty to possession of methamphetamine and timely appealed the denial of his suppression motion. The Idaho Court of Appeals affirmed the district court. The state supreme court granted defendant's petition for review.


OVERVIEW: In a motion to suppress, defendant challenged the search of his car incident to his arrest because the officer did not make contact with defendant until he was already outside of his car. Defendant also argued that the search was illegal under Belton due to the fact that the search was not justified by the concern that defendant would grab a weapon or reach into his truck and destroy evidence. In his argument before the district court, defendant made no mention of the state constitution; therefore, his state constitutional claim was not preserved for review. The Supreme Court of Idaho held that the officer's warrantless search of defendant's truck violated the Fourth Amendment. Defendant was not within reaching distance of the passenger compartment of his truck at the time the officer searched it, nor was it reasonable to believe the truck contained evidence of the offense for which defendant was arrested--failure to appear. The State failed to show that the good faith exception to the exclusionary rule applied.


OUTCOME: The district court's decision denying defendant's motion to suppress was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

74 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Credit Bureau of E. Idaho, Inc. v. Lecheminant


Docket No. 36381, 2010 Opinion No. 66


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


149 Idaho 468; 235 P.3d 1188; 2010 Ida. LEXIS 106



June 18, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended June 28, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Madison County. Hon. Brent J. Moss, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is vacated and remanded to district court for proceedings consistent with this Opinion. Idaho Code § 11-204 is unconstitutional. Attorneys fees and costs are awarded to appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Seventh Judicial District, Madison County, Idaho, affirmed the magistrate court's order denying appellant creditor's motion to contest a claim of exemption from garnishment, Idaho Code Ann. § 11-204. The creditor appealed.


OVERVIEW: Respondent debtors claimed that the creditor lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of Idaho Code Ann. § 11-204. The supreme court found that the creditor had standing because a party did not need to be a member of the class excluded from the benefit of a statute in order to have standing. Section 11-204 was unconstitutional, as it treated husbands and wives unequally. The statute no longer conformed with the object of community property law because it required a distinction to be made between the earnings of husband and wives. The creditor cited Idaho Code Ann. § 32-912 to demonstrate that Idaho Code Ann. § 11-204 was contrary to current community property legislation. The debt did not need to benefit the community in order to be satisfied out of the community property. Wives no longer needed the protection provided under § 11-204 and an extension would not serve the legislative purpose because husbands did not need its protection. Attorney fees and costs were awarded to the creditor for its attempt to collect on the judgment on appeal to the district court and the supreme court. Attorney fees were not awarded on appeal under Idaho Code Ann. § 12-120(1) and (3).


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated and remanded to the district court for further proceedings.

State v. Doe


Docket No. 36121, 2010 Opinion No. 60


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


149 Idaho 353; 233 P.3d 1275; 2010 Ida. LEXIS 94



June 1, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 24, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Kootenai County. Hon. John P. Luster, District Judge. Hon. Robert B. Burton, Magistrate Judge.
State v. Jane Doe II (In the Interest of Jane Doe I), 2008 Ida. App. LEXIS 139 (Idaho Ct. App., Nov. 13, 2008)



DISPOSITION: The district court decision affirming the magistrate is reversed and the probation order is vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents appealed probation terms imposed upon them in their daughter's juvenile criminal proceeding. The district court affirmed the magistrate's order; the Idaho Court of Appeals vacated, finding that although the magistrate court acted within its statutory capacity, it nonetheless violated the Fourth Amendment by imposing a urinalysis requirement. The state supreme court granted the State's petition for review.


OVERVIEW: Appellants appeared in magistrate court with their minor daughter. She signed a written admission to two counts of petit theft. The magistrate placed appellants' daughter on formal probation, imposed terms requiring appellants to submit to random urine testing and not to violate controlled-substance laws. The disposition order admonished appellants that they could be subject to contempt proceedings if they disobeyed the order. Appellants refused to sign the order. The district court affirmed the probation terms; the Idaho Court of Appeals vacated, finding that although the magistrate court acted within its statutory capacity under Idaho Code Ann. § 20-520(1)(i), it violated the Fourth Amendment by imposing the urinalysis requirement. The Supreme Court of Idaho agreed with the Court of Appeals. Appellants had a Fourth Amendment privacy interest in their bodies. Requiring them to undergo urinalysis testing constituted a search that was invalid absent a warrant.


OUTCOME: The district court's decision affirming the magistrate was reversed, and the probation order was vacated.

 

76 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Weinstein v. Prudential Prop. & Cas. Ins. Co.


Docket No. 34970-2008, 2010 Opinion No. 61


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


149 Idaho 299; 233 P.3d 1221; 2010 Ida. LEXIS 96



June 1, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Weinstein v. Prudential Prop. & Cas. Ins. Co., 2010 Ida. LEXIS 131 (Idaho, July 1, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Ada County. The Hon. Darla S. Williamson, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a suit seeking damages for breach of an automobile liability insurance contract, defendant insurer appealed the judgment of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County, Idaho, that awarded compensatory and punitive damages to plaintiff insureds. The insureds filed a cross-appeal, challenging the district court's order of a new trial on punitive damages unless they accepted a remittitur.


OVERVIEW: The insureds sustained injuries in an automobile collision with an uninsured driver and made demand upon their insurer to pay their medical bills. When the insurer failed to do so, the insureds filed suit. On review, the court held that compensatory damages based upon the insurer's bad faith failure to pay or delay in making payment were proper, as was an award of punitive damages because the insurer's conduct in delaying payment was intentional and not the result of an honest mistake. Its agents testified that they knew from the day following the accident that the insurer would be liable for the insureds' injuries under the policy's uninsured motorist coverage, and the jury could have concluded that the insurer delayed in making payment to take advantage of the insureds' financial vulnerability. However, attorney fees on the claim for future damages was improper under Idaho Code Ann. § 41-1839 because the insureds never submitted a claim or proof of loss regarding future damages. Further, the trial court's reduction of punitive damages was affirmed, with no need for a new trial, because the reduction was necessary to satisfy constitutional due process concerns.


OUTCOME: The judgment awarding compensatory damages was affirmed, and the case was remanded for entry of an amended judgment reducing the award of punitive damages. The award of attorney fees on the claim for future damages was vacated.

US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Shackelford v. Idaho, 131 S. Ct. 1599, 179 L. Ed. 2d 503, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 1947 (U.S., 2011)
Appeal after remand at, Decision reached on appeal by State v. Shackelford, 2013 Ida. LEXIS 257 (Idaho, Aug. 16, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Second Judicial District, State of Idaho, Latah County. Hon. John R. Stegner, District Judge.
State v. Shackelford, 2010 Ida. LEXIS 5 (Idaho, Jan. 20, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of conviction for first-degree murder, conspiracy to commit first-degree murder, first-degree arson, conspiracy to commit first-degree arson and preparing false evidence, affirmed. Case remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of the Second Judicial District, Latah County, Idaho, that convicted him of two counts of murder, conspiracy to commit murder, arson, conspiracy to commit arson, and preparing false evidence. The State cross-appealed, challenging the district court's grant of post-conviction relief, which set aside the death sentence imposed and required resentencing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murdering his ex-wife and her boyfriend. On review, the court held that the trial court erred under Idaho R. Evid. 803(3) in allowing the State to introduce the ex-wife's out-of-court statements to show that her state of mind was inconsistent with suicide because the evidence was not relevant where the defense did not assert that the victims died as a result of suicide rather than murder. However, in light of the extensive testimony of the State's witnesses, as well as evidence regarding the times of the deaths, the manner in which the victims were shot, the setting of a fire in an attempt to conceal the murders, and further testimony regarding defendant's actions on the day of the victims' deaths, the error was harmless because defendant failed to establish that the error would have changed the outcome of the trial. Further, the court rejected the State's challenge and held that resentencing was proper because it could not find beyond a reasonable doubt that a reasonable jury could have found that the State proved that both victims were killed at the same time as was required by the aggravator under Idaho Code Ann. § 19-2515(h)(2) (2000).


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed, as was the district court's order mandating resentencing.

Stuart v. State


Docket No. 34200, 2010 Opinion No. 51


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


149 Idaho 35; 232 P.3d 813; 2010 Ida. LEXIS 79



May 10, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 1, 2010.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Stuart v. Idaho, 131 S. Ct. 1472, 179 L. Ed. 2d 313, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 1387 (U.S., 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Clearwater County. Hon. Ron Schilling, District Judge.
State v. Stuart, 110 Idaho 163, 715 P.2d 833, 1985 Ida. LEXIS 470 (Idaho, 1985)



DISPOSITION: The appeal is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. In a fourth petition for post-conviction relief, petitioner advanced claims of prosecutorial misconduct, failure to disclose mitigating evidence, and ineffective assistance of counsel. The District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Clearwater County, summarily dismissed the petition under Idaho Code Ann. § 19-2719. Petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted in 1981 for the death of his girlfriend's three-year-old son. More than seven years passed between the appointment of substitute counsel in 1995 and the filing of the fourth petition for post-conviction relief in December of 2002. Furthermore, the petition was silent as to when the facts supporting petitioner's claims were known or reasonably could have been known. It was petitioner's burden to present a petition alleging facts that would show that he fit within the exception in Idaho Code Ann. § 19-2719 to avoid summary dismissal; however, the petitioner did not meet that burden. Thus, petitioner's appeal had to be dismissed absent a statutory or constitutional basis for disregarding the application of § 19-2719 to the petition. There was no statutory basis for disregarding the application of § 19-2719 to the petition. Also, there was no constitutional basis for disregarding the application of § 19-2719 to the petition because (1) there was no violation of the ex post facto laws, the separation of powers provisions, or petitioner's rights to equal protection, due process, or habeas corpus; and (2) the statute was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The supreme court dismissed the appeal.

Alcohol Bev. Control v. Boyd


Docket No. 36124, 2010 Opinion No. 42


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


148 Idaho 944; 231 P.3d 1041; 2010 Ida. LEXIS 70



April 23, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 18, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Clearwater County. Hon. John H. Bradbury, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is reversed and the case is remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Second Judicial District, Clearwater County, Idaho, reversed an administrative hearing officer's decision to suspend respondent licensee's retail alcohol license. Appellant Alcohol Beverage Control (ABC) appealed.


OVERVIEW: The district court held that Idaho Code Ann. § 23-615 was facially unconstitutional because it was both overbroad and vague. The supreme court noted that the district court failed to understand the constitutional parameters of a license to sell alcohol. It was not § 23-615 that directly affected whether a licensee may or may not continue to operate as a retail seller of alcohol. Rather, this provision placed restrictions upon how the licensee may operate his retail alcohol business. Selling alcohol was not constitutionally protected conduct, and thus, statutes that regulated the sale of alcohol could not be challenged as unconstitutionally overbroad. As the licensee's bartender engaged in conduct that was clearly proscribed, § 23-615 was not vague as applied in the case, and the licensee could not complain of the vagueness of the law as applied to the conduct of others. The district court erred in its determination that § 23-615 was unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded, and the district court was instructed to vacate its order staying the suspension of the licensee's license.

State v. Doe


Docket No. 36606, 2010 Opinion No. 37


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


148 Idaho 919; 231 P.3d 1016; 2010 Ida. LEXIS 59



March 26, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 18, 2010.
Rehearing denied by State v. Doe, 2010 Ida. LEXIS 81 (Idaho, May 5, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Gooding County. Honorable Barry Wood, District Judge; Honorable Mark A. Ingram, Magistrate Judge.
State v. Doe (In re Doe), 2009 Ida. App. LEXIS 36 (Idaho Ct. App., Mar. 31, 2009)



DISPOSITION: District court's affirmance of the magistrate court's decision, is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant minor was cited for violating Wendell City, Idaho, Ordinance No. 442, a curfew ordinance. The magistrate judge denied his constitutional challenge to the ordinance. Defendant made a conditional admission of guilt. The district court rejected the constitutional challenge. The Court of Appeals of Idaho reversed, finding that the ordinance was unconstitutionally overbroad. The state supreme court granted the State's petition for review.


OVERVIEW: Wendell City, Idaho, Ordinance No. 442 prohibited a minor from being in public from 11:00 p.m. till 5:00 a.m. When defendant was charged with violating the ordinance, he argued that the ordinance constituted an impermissible restriction on free speech. The Supreme Court of Idaho held that the ordinance was a valid enactment within the power of the City of Wendell under Idaho Const. art. XII, § 2. The ordinance served the government's interest in keeping juveniles off the streets, which was unrelated to the suppression of expression. The ordinance did not reach an amount of conduct that was greater than necessary to further the City of Wendell's interests in the physical well-being of minors. As a result, the ordinance was not unconstitutionally overbroad or vague. The ordinance did not result in the deprivation of a fundamental right, such as a minor's freedom of movement. Because defendant failed to show a bar to his father's ability to challenge the constitutionality of the ordinance, he could not assert a deprivation of parental liberty interests in the matter.


OUTCOME: The decision of the district court was affirmed.

Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Patrick H. Owen, District Judge.

DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is affirmed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County, Idaho, convicted defendant of grand theft, robbery, two counts of murder in the first degree, and two counts of felony murder. Except for robbery, his convictions were affirmed on appeal. The district court denied defendant's sixth petition for post-conviction relief and his amended petition. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court noted that defendant's six asserted claims in his amended petition were barred by Idaho Code Ann. § 19-2719. The statute did not violate U.S. Const. amends. V or XIV and was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Rhoades v. State


Docket No. 35187, Docket No. 34198, Docket No. 34199, 2010 Opinion No. 23


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


149 Idaho 130; 233 P.3d 61; 2010 Ida. LEXIS 52



March 17, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Mc Kinney v. State (In re Rhoades), 2010 Ida. LEXIS 103 (Idaho, June 4, 2010)
Motion granted by Rhoades v. Idaho, 562 U.S. 1090, 131 S. Ct. 811, 178 L. Ed. 2d 529, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 9576 (Dec. 6, 2010)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Rhoades v. Idaho, 562 U.S. 1258, 131 S. Ct. 1571, 179 L. Ed. 2d 477, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 1820 (Feb. 28, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bonneville County, Hon. Jon J. Shindurling, District Judge. (Rhoades). Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Butte County, Hon. James C. Herndon, District Judge. (McKinney). Appeal from the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Idaho County, Hon. John Bradbury, District Judge. (Pizzuto). Rhoades v. Idaho, 552 U.S. 1227, 128 S. Ct. 1441, 170 L. Ed. 2d 271, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 2030 (Feb. 25, 2008)
McKinney v. Idaho, 552 U.S. 1227, 128 S. Ct. 1441, 170 L. Ed. 2d 271, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 2091 (Feb. 25, 2008)
Pizzuto v. Idaho, 552 U.S. 1227, 128 S. Ct. 1441, 170 L. Ed. 2d 271, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 2023 (Feb. 25, 2008)
Hairston v. Idaho, 552 U.S. 1227, 128 S. Ct. 1442, 170 L. Ed. 2d 272, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 2050 (Feb. 25, 2008)
Card v. Idaho, 552 U.S. 1227, 128 S. Ct. 1442, 170 L. Ed. 2d 271, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 2131 (Feb. 25, 2008)
State v. Stuart, 110 Idaho 163, 715 P.2d 833, 1985 Ida. LEXIS 470 (Idaho, May 3, 1985)
State v. Pizzuto, 119 Idaho 742, 810 P.2d 680, 1991 Ida. LEXIS 5 (Idaho, Jan. 15, 1991)



DISPOSITION: The orders of the district courts are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, petitioners, individuals convicted of criminal offenses who received capital sentences, challenged orders issued by the various Idaho district courts that dismissed their successive petitions for post-conviction relief, arguing that the U.S. Supreme Court's Ring ruling was to be applied retroactively and that they were entitled to relief under Ring.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, petitioners contended that they were entitled to a new trial because, in each of their respective cases, the trial judge determined the existence of mitigating factors sufficient to support the imposition of the death penalty, while the Supreme Court's Ring ruling concluded that the jury trial guarantee under the Sixth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. VI, required that the jury find an aggravating circumstance necessary to impose the death penalty instead of the judge. On review, the court adopted the Teague retroactivity test for criminal cases on collateral review and held that the Supreme Court's ruling in Ring announced a new procedural rule that did not apply retroactively to cases already final on direct review. Ring established a new procedural rule because it altered the range of permissible methods for determining whether a defendant's conduct was punishable by death. The ruling did not establish a substantive rule because it did not alter the range of conduct subjected to the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The orders of the district courts were affirmed.

Wright v. Bd. of Psychological Exam'rs (In re Bd. of Psychologist Examiners' Final Order)


Docket No. 35647, 2010 Opinion No. 7


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


148 Idaho 542; 224 P.3d 1131; 2010 Ida. LEXIS 16



January 28, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 24, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Nez Perce County. The Hon. Jeff M. Brudie, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Second Judicial District, Nez Perce County, Idaho, held that appellant doctor could not challenge an earlier final order of respondent Idaho State Board of Psychological Examiners (Board) and it upheld the subsequent final order. The doctor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The doctor argued that the district court erred in holding that she could not challenge the 2005 Order. The supreme court noted that the doctor did not timely seek judicial review of that order. As to the 2006 Order, the supreme court found that there was no allegation in the amended order to show cause that the doctor violated Idaho Code Ann. § 54-2310. The only contention was that she failed to comply with the 2005 Order. In its 2006 Order, the Board imposed a new five-year license suspension commencing on April 19, 2006. The Board's action either extended the doctor's suspension for three years or for one year. The next issue was whether the Board had the authority to impose a new sanction for violating its prior order. There was on provision of the statutes or of any rule adopted by the Board that authorized "additional disciplinary action" for violating an order issued by the Board. Because both parties had prevailed in part on appeal, neither of them was the prevailing party entitled to attorney fees on appeal, Idaho Code Ann. § 12-117(1).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as to the holding that the district court had no jurisdiction to review the 2005 Order; the judgment was reversed as to the judgment upholding the 2006 Order.

State v. Shackelford


Docket No. 27966/31928, 2010 Opinion No. 3


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


2010 Ida. LEXIS 5



January 20, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Shackelford, 2010 Ida. LEXIS 237 (Idaho, May 28, 2010)
Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at State v. Shackelford, 2010 Ida. LEXIS 101 (Idaho, June 1, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Second Judicial District, State of Idaho, Latah County. Hon. John R. Stegner, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of conviction and sentence of death for first-degree murder, conspiracy to commit first-degree murder, first-degree arson, conspiracy to commit first-degree arson and preparing false evidence, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of the Second Judicial District, Latah County, Idaho, that convicted him of first-degree murder, conspiracy to commit first-degree murder, first-degree arson, conspiracy to commit first-degree arson, and preparing false evidence. The State appealed the district court's order granting post-conviction relief and setting aside the death sentences imposed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with and convicted of offenses relating to the murder of his ex-wife and her boyfriend. On review, the court held that, although the trial court erred under Idaho R. Evid. 803(3) in allowing six witnesses to testify to statements made by the victim, defendant's ex-wife, expressing her fear that defendant was going to harm her, the error was harmless because any guilt that may have stemmed from the victim's out-of-court statements was outweighed by testimony regarding defendant's own statements expressing his desire to kill the victim, along with the testimony of his co-conspirators and the forensic evidence regarding the murders and the arson. The court rejected the State's challenge to the granting of post-conviction relief. Defendant's death sentence was required to be set aside by the U.S. Supreme Court's Ring ruling, which held that the Sixth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. VI, entitled a capital defendant to a jury determination of any fact on which the legislature conditioned an increase in their maximum punishment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and the order granting post-conviction relief were affirmed. The case was remanded for resentencing.

State v. Maybee


Docket No. 35200, 2010 Opinion No. 2


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


148 Idaho 520; 224 P.3d 1109; 2010 Ida. LEXIS 4



January 15, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended January 21, 2010.

Released for Pulication February 10, 2010.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Maybee v. Idaho, 178 L. Ed. 2d 37, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 6004 (U.S., Oct. 4, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Kathryn A. Sticklen, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: District court order granting summary judgment for State in case involving unstamped cigarettes sold in interstate commerce, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action to enforce Idaho's Tobacco Master Settlement Agreement Complementary Act, Idaho Code Ann. § 39-8401 et seq., appellant, a Native American living and conducting business upon a reservation located in the State of New York, appealed the decision of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County, granting summary judgment in favor of respondent, the State of Idaho.


OVERVIEW: As the sole proprietor of several websites, appellant sold over 2,500,000 cigarettes from brands not listed on the Idaho Directory to consumers in Idaho. He conducted his business from a reservation located in New York. Appellant did not possess an Idaho tobacco permit, as required by Idaho Code Ann. § 39-5718. The State filed a complaint against appellant, alleging violations of the Complementary Act and Idaho's Prevention of Minors' Access to Tobacco Act (MAA). The district court granted the State summary judgment. The Supreme Court of Idaho upheld the decision, based on findings that: (1) the Complementary Act applied to both intrastate and interstate sellers of Noncompliant Cigarettes; (2) appellant sold Noncompliant Cigarettes, in violation of the Complementary Act; (3) the Interstate Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3, did not preempt application of the Complementary Act to appellant; (4) he sold tobacco products in Idaho without obtaining an Idaho tobacco permit, in contravention of the MAA; and (5) the Indian Commerce Clause did not preempt application of either the Complementary Act or the MAA to appellant.


OUTCOME: The summary judgment was affirmed. The State of Idaho was awarded attorney fees on appeal.

Doe v. BSA


Docket Nos. 35639/35681, 2009 Opinion No. 152


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


148 Idaho 427; 224 P.3d 494; 2009 Ida. LEXIS 233



December 29, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected March 31, 2010. Rehearing denied by Doe v. BSA, 2010 Ida. LEXIS 32 (Idaho, Feb. 8, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Michael McLaughlin, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The district court's order is reversed and the case is remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, Boy Scouts of America (BSA), appealed an order of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County, Idaho, that denied its motion to dismiss under Idaho R. Civ. P. 12(b)(6), arguing that the district court erred in finding that the claims of plaintiffs, former boy scouts, were not barred by the statute of limitations pursuant to Idaho Code Ann. § 6-1704.


OVERVIEW: Former boy scouts filed suit against BSA, alleging that they had been molested by their scout leader. BSA moved to dismiss, arguing that the claims were barred by Idaho Code Ann. § 6-1701. On review of the order denying BSA's motion, the court held that the parties and the district court were erroneous in presuming that Idaho Code tit. 6, ch. 17, applied. The legislation created a cause of action for children harmed by sexual conduct, but no such cause of action existed when the former boy scouts were victimized by their scout leader. Because the liability imposed under Idaho Code tit. 6, ch. 17, substantially differed from that formerly available, the statutory scheme could not be retroactively applied. Regardless of when the former boy scouts' cause of action accrued, the statute could not be applied to conduct that occurred at least six years before the statutory scheme was enacted, and BSA could not be held accountable for behavior that was not actionable at the time it occurred.


OUTCOME: The district court order refusing dismissal was reversed, and the case was remanded to the district court for further proceedings.

State v. Korn


Docket No. 34965, 2009 Opinion No. 150


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


148 Idaho 413; 224 P.3d 480; 2009 Ida. LEXIS 229



December 24, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 15, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Payette County. Hon. Renae J. Hoff, District Judge. Hon. William B. Dillon, Magistrate Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved to dismiss the charge of possession of exotic animals contending that the ordinance prohibiting the possession of exotic animals was unconstitutional. The magistrate judge denied the motion and refused to admit uncertified copies of orders from defendant's bankruptcy case. The District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho affirmed the magistrate's decision. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The bankruptcy court ordered defendant to sell his zoo. He entered into an agreement with his mother to buy the property. The county passed an ordinance that prohibited the possession of exotic animals. The State filed a criminal complaint alleging defendant possessed exotic animals in violation of the county's ordinance. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss, alleging that the ordinance violated the contract clauses of the federal and state constitutions. In an effort to prove the defense of necessity, defendant attempted to admit copies of two orders from the bankruptcy court. Defendant was excused from Idaho R. Evid. 1002's requirement that he produce the original orders if his copies were certified in accordance with Idaho R. Evid. 902. Defense counsel admitted that the copies of the alleged orders were not certified copies. Therefore, the magistrate court did not abuse its discretion in excluding the exhibits.


OUTCOME: The decision of the district court was affirmed.

Knox v. State ex rel. Otter


Docket No. 35787-2008, 2009 Opinion No. 144


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


148 Idaho 324; 223 P.3d 266; 2009 Ida. LEXIS 223



November 27, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 12, 2010.
Rehearing denied by Knox v. State ex rel. Otter, 2010 Ida. LEXIS 8 (Idaho, Jan. 8, 2010)
Related proceeding at Knox v. United States DOI, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 136660 (D. Idaho, Dec. 27, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Bingham County. The Hon. Darren B. Simpson, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sought review of an order from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Bingham County, which granted defendant State of Idaho's motion to dismiss their action against the State and defendant State officials to have Idaho Code Ann. §§ 67-429B and 67-429C declared unconstitutional as violating Idaho Const. art. III, § 20. Plaintiffs sought appellate attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs brought an action against defendants to have Idaho Code Ann. §§ 67-429B and 67-429C declared unconstitutional as violating Idaho Const. art. III, § 20. Plaintiffs asserted that they became addicted to gambling by playing the video gaming machines at a casino located on an Indian reservation. Plaintiffs claimed that because of their gambling addictions, they each lost tens of thousands of dollars and suffered stress, anxiety, humiliation, and emotional distress. The trial court granted the State's motion to dismiss the action. On appeal, the court determined that a judgment entered in a federal case regarding whether video gaming machines were permitted on the reservation was final and would be res judicata in any further litigation between the State and the tribes as to whether tribal video gaming was permissible. The fact that the State did not raise the constitutionality of §§ 67-429B and 67-429C in the federal case did not prevent res judicata from barring future litigation. A judgment for plaintiffs that declared that the statutes were unconstitutional would not result in a substantial likelihood that video gaming machines would be removed from the casino.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court denied plaintiffs' request for appellate attorney fees.

Urban Renewal Agency v. Hart


Docket No. 35435, 2009 Opinion No. 141


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


148 Idaho 299; 222 P.3d 467; 2009 Ida. LEXIS 206



November 25, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 12, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Madison County. Hon. Brent J. Moss, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent urban renewal agency petitioned the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Madison County, for judicial confirmation for the validity of bonds the agency wished to issue. Appellant citizen challenged the petition. The district court confirmed the validity of the bonds. The citizen appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city council adopted an ordinance that approved the agency's plan to construct an urban renewal project and finance the project. On appeal, the citizen argued the Local Economic Development Act, Idaho Code Ann. § 50-2901 et seq., violated limitations on actions by municipalities. The citizen argued that an urban renewal agency's use of revenue allocation financing was really an action by a city -- that agencies were merely alter egos" of their cities -- and thus urban renewal agencies' use of revenue allocation financing violated Idaho Const. art. VIII, §§ 3 and 4. The supreme court determined that urban renewal agencies were not the alter egos of cities. Therefore, the Act's grant of authority to urban renewal agencies to issue revenue allocation bonds did not violate Idaho Const. art. VIII, §§ 3 or 4. The agencies' brief demonstrated that cities across the State had financed over 60 projects through revenue allocation financing in the 27 years since the supreme court issued previous caselaw on the subject. This widespread reliance on the supreme court's holding that urban renewal agencies were not alter egos of cities was well-justified.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment.

Michalk v. Michalk


Docket No. 35221, 2009 Opinion No. 128


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


148 Idaho 224; 220 P.3d 580; 2009 Ida. LEXIS 191



October 20, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 3, 2009.
Rehearing denied by Michalk v. Michalk, 2009 Ida. LEXIS 220 (Idaho, Nov. 20, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Terry R. McDaniel, Magistrate Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the magistrate court is affirmed. Respondent is awarded attorneys fees on appeal. Costs are awarded to Respondent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fourth Judicial District Court, Ada County, Idaho, dissolved the parties' marriage and granted them joint legal and physical custody of their child, with appellant mother having primary physical custody and respondent father having reasonable visitation upon completing additional counseling and a polygraph. Child custody payment terms were ordered, the parties' property and debt were divided. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the mother raised several issues challenging the trial court's judgment. The supreme court found that because the mother chose to remain silent during the entirety of the trial proceedings, the supreme court could consider very few of the issues she raised on appeal. Many of her arguments had no citations to any evidence in the record or relevant legal authority, and were thus barred under Idaho App. R. 35(a)(6). She also failed to raise many of her arguments before the trial court and was thus barred from raising them on appeal. Because the mother failed to present evidence of her claim that the father was a habitual perpetrator of domestic violence to the magistrate court and did not raise any objection during trial, she failed to preserve this issue for appeal; furthermore, the father the father presented ample evidence to rebut the presumption of Idaho Code Ann. § 32-717B(5). As it was frivolous for the mother to argue on appeal that the father should not have been granted joint custody when that was the only request that the mother properly made before the magistrate court, the father was entitled to attorney fees on appeal pursuant to Idaho Code Ann. § 12-121.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed, and the father was awarded attorney fees on appeal, plus costs.

City of Boise v. Ada County (In re Facilities & Equip. Provided by the City of Boise)


Docket No. 35432, 2009 Opinion No. 110


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


147 Idaho 794; 215 P.3d 514; 2009 Ida. LEXIS 151



August 25, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Judges of the Fourth Judicial District Sitting en banc.



DISPOSITION: The en banc panel's decision is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged an order and decision from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County (Idaho), which granted respondent county's motion to intervene and denied the city's petition to vacate an Idaho Code Ann. § 1-2218 order that required the city to provide suitable and adequate quarters for a magistrate's division of the district court.


OVERVIEW: After the county built a new courthouse, the city agreed to share the facilities and to reimburse the county for expenses. The trial court relied on Idaho R. Civ. P. 24(a) in allowing the county to intervene. The court held that although a § 1-2218 proceeding was not properly categorized as a civil action, the trial court had authority under Idaho Code Ann. § 1-1622 and its inherent power to allow the county to intervene. By analogy to permanent mandatory injunctions, the court concluded that the city had a burden to show good and sufficient cause for setting aside the § 1-2218 order and that it had not met its burden. No significant change in circumstances arose from new case law precluding district judges from ordering a city to reimburse a county for use of county-owned facilities, which did not prohibit voluntary agreements for reimbursement; from the construction of the county courthouse; or from the county's receipt of fees collected under Idaho Code Ann. § 31-3201A. Section 1-2218 did not impose a tax within the meaning of Idaho Const. art. VII, § 5. The city's appeal was not frivolous under Idaho Code Ann. § 12-121 because it raised legitimate questions about the case law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of the county's motion to intervene and affirmed the decision declining to set aside the challenged order.

Rollins v. Blaine County


Docket No. 33658-2006, 2009 Opinion No. 89


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


147 Idaho 729; 215 P.3d 449; 2009 Ida. LEXIS 99



July 7, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 12, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Blaine County. The Hon. Robert J. Elgee, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On plaintiff landowner's judicial review petition, for purposes of Idaho Code Ann. §§ 67-6519, 67-6521, the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District in and for Blaine County (Idaho) (1) held intervenor neighbor had no right to appeal and the landowner established a nonconforming use, and (2) remanded, plus (3) awarded the landowner fees and costs. Defendant county appealed. The landowner and county sought fees under Idaho Code Ann. § 12-117.


OVERVIEW: The county, through its board of commissioners, did not grant or deny any permit. It simply held that the landowner's property was located within the mountain overlay district and that a site alteration permit was required. The landowner did not apply for such a permit and thus he had not exhausted all remedies under the county code. Both Idaho Code Ann. §§ 67-6519, 67-6521 provided for judicial review only after all remedies had been exhausted under local ordinance. Because the landowner failed to exhaust his administrative remedies before filing his petition for judicial review, the court had to vacate the trial court's ruling and remand with instructions to dismiss the petition for judicial review without prejudice. Because the landowner had not prevailed on appeal, he was not entitled to an award of attorney fees under Idaho Code Ann. § 12-117. Because the court dismissed the appeal on an issue not raised by either party, the court declined to award fees to the county.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's judgment, dismissed the appeal, and remanded with instructions to dismiss the petition for judicial review without prejudice. The court declined to award fees or costs on appeal to either the landowner or county.
