Rammell v. Idaho State Dep't of Agric.


Docket No. 34927, 2009 Opinion No. 78


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


147 Idaho 415; 210 P.3d 523; 2009 Ida. LEXIS 84



June 1, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, for Madison County. Honorable Brent J. Moss, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The district court's order is affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Seventh Judicial District, Madison County, Idaho, affirmed an order by respondent Department of Agriculture (Department) imposing $29,000 in fines against appellant ranchers for nine violations of a statute and regulations pertaining to domestic cervidae. The ranchers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The ranchers argued that the hearing officer should have disqualified herself in response to the December 13, 2004 motion to disqualify they made pursuant to Idaho Code Ann. § 67-5252. The supreme court found that the ranchers did not move to disqualify the hearing officer until just two days before the hearing was scheduled to occur. The motion was untimely filed and properly denied. The hearing officer had no authority to hear a challenge to the validity of the Department's regulation based on the rule being outside of the Department's rulemaking authority. The hearing officer's decision to exclude certain evidence as lacking proper foundation or relevancy did not violate the ranchers' due process rights, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, as they had notice and an opportunity to be heard. The issues of whether the regulations were invalid and whether Idaho Code Ann. § 25-3708 was constitutional were not properly before the supreme court. The award of attorney fees and costs to the Department was improper, Idaho Code Ann. § 12-117(1). The Department was entitled to costs and fees on appeal, Idaho Code Ann. § 12-117.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated on the issue of attorney fees; as to all other issues, the judgment was affirmed.

Terrazas v. Blaine County


Docket No. 34106, 2009 Opinion No. 58


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


147 Idaho 193; 207 P.3d 169; 2009 Ida. LEXIS 65



April 15, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 8, 2009.
Rehearing denied by Terrazas v. Blaine County, 2009 Ida. LEXIS 123 (Idaho, May 5, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Blaine County. Honorable Robert J. Elgee, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners appealed the order of the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Blaine County, affirming the decision of respondent Blaine County Board of County Commissioners (Idaho), denying appellants' subdivision application.


OVERVIEW: Appellants submitted an application to subdivide 115 acres of real property in Blaine County, Idaho. The Board of County Commissioners found that the areas of disturbance on two of the four lots in the proposed subdivision encroached upon the Mountain Overlay District (MOD). The intent of the MOD was to direct development away from the mountains. The Board issued a lengthy, written decision denying the application. The district court did not err by affirming the Board's decision. The Supreme Court of Idaho held that the Board had the sole authority to make final decisions on subdivision applications and its decision was supported by substantial evidence. The Board was not estopped from enforcing the MOD ordinance, because a planning and zoning staff member originally believed that the subdivision was outside the MOD. The MOD ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague, and appellant's due process rights were not violated by the Commissioner's site visit. The Board's decision was not arbitrary and capricious and did not violate appellant's equal protection rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Wheeler v. Idaho Dep't of Health & Welfare


Docket No. 34426, 2009 Opinion No. 52


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


147 Idaho 257; 207 P.3d 988; 2009 Ida. LEXIS 60



April 8, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 5, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. D. Duff McKee, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: District court decision affirming suspension of driver's license for failure to pay court ordered child support, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner father appealed a judgment of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County (Idaho) affirming the suspension of the father's driver's license for failure to pay court-ordered child support, pursuant to the Family Law License Suspensions Act (FLLSA), Idaho Code §§ 7-1401 to 7-1417, in a license suspension proceeding commenced by respondent Idaho Department of Health and Welfare.


OVERVIEW: The Department suspended the father's driver's license for non-payment of court-ordered child support for three children under three separate orders. The father contended that the Department did not have authority to commence license suspension proceedings against him under the FLLSA and that the FLLSA was applied to all three of his child support orders ex post facto. The court found that the Department substantially complied with the requirements of FLLSA, Idaho Code § 7-1404, to commence the license suspension proceedings. There were no ex post facto violations, under Idaho Const. art. I, § 16 or under U.S. Const. art. I, § 9, cl. 3, because the FLLSA did not invoke criminal jurisprudence. A retrospective argument was inapplicable because the father's child support arrearages were in excess of the amount that provided the Department with grounds to initiate license suspension proceedings, under Idaho Code § 7-1404. A driver's license was not an exempt property interest under the FLLSA, Idaho Code § 7-1402(5). The Department's request for attorney fees on appeal, under Idaho Code § 12-121, was denied because the matter was one of first impression.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court, denied the Department's request for attorney fees on appeal, and assessed costs to the Department.

Lochsa Falls, L.L.C. v. State


Docket No. 34039, 2009 Opinion No. 51


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


147 Idaho 232; 207 P.3d 963; 2009 Ida. LEXIS 61



April 7, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 21, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Honorable Michael R. McLaughlin, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment dismissing the complaint is vacated and the case is remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a developer, appealed the order of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County, dismissing its complaint against defendants, the Idaho Transportation Department (ITD) and the Board of ITD, for failure to exhaust administrative remedies.


OVERVIEW: The developer presented a preliminary plat of a subdivision. Because the plat called for an internal street to intersect with a controlled-access highway, ITD required that the developer obtain an encroachment permit. The ITD approved the encroachment permit with the condition that the developer design and construct a traffic signal. The cost was estimated at $ 180,000. After the new road was built and the traffic signal was installed but not operational, the developer sued ITD for reimbursement of the expense of constructing the traffic signal. The district court erred by dismissing the complaint for failure to exhaust administrative remedies. The Supreme Court of Idaho held that while judicial review of ITD's action on an encroachment permit application was governed by the APA, the applicable rules did not provide a mechanism whereby an applicant whose permit application had been approved subject to conditions could challenge those conditions. The Supreme Court of Idaho also held that it was not an impermissible tax for the ITD to impose the condition of erecting a traffic signal as a requirement for a developer seeking an encroachment permit.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing the complaint was reversed, and the case was remanded to the district court for further proceedings. The parties' request for attorney fees and costs on appeal was denied.

Banner Life Ins. Co. v. Mark Wallace Dixson Irrevocable Trust


Docket No. 34873, 2009 Opinion No. 47


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


147 Idaho 117; 206 P.3d 481; 2009 Ida. LEXIS 55



April 3, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 30, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Honorable Thomas A. Neville, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Orders granting summary judgment and costs are vacated and the case is remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an interpleader action initiated by plaintiff insurance company, defendant-appellant, the wife of the insured, challenged summary judgment granted by the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District (Idaho) in favor of defendant-respondent, an irrevocable trust established in the insured's name, arguing that the district court erred in finding that the trust was entitled to the proceeds of the insured's life insurance policy.


OVERVIEW: After the deceased insured's wife and the trust filed competing claims to life insurance proceeds, the insurance company filed an interpleader action so that the district court could determine to whom it should pay the proceeds. The parties filed cross-motions for summary judgment, and the district court granted that of the trust. On review, the court held that the district court erred in concluding that there was no genuine issue as to the character of the final premium payment, that the premium had been paid with the insured's separate property, and that the policy was the insured's separate property. The character of the payment was a material fact that controlled the disposition of the case, and there was conflicting evidence regarding the donor's intent in giving funds to the insured to pay the insurance premium. If the district court determined on remand that the policy was the insured's separate property, then the wife was not entitled to the funds. If the policy was community property, then the wife was entitled to one-half of the proceeds, and the remaining one half, as the insured's share of the community property, belonged to the trust as the policy's named beneficiary.


OUTCOME: The district court's judgment was vacated, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Smith v. State


Docket No. 33254, 2009 Opinion No. 22


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


146 Idaho 822; 203 P.3d 1221; 2009 Ida. LEXIS 31



February 10, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
AMENDED OPINION, THE COURT'S PRIOR OPINION DATED FEBRUARY 9, 2009 IS HEREBY WITHDRAWN.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Twin Falls County. Honorable John C. Hohnhorst, District Judge.
Smith v. State, 2009 Ida. LEXIS 28 (Idaho, Feb. 9, 2009)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Fifth Judicial District, Twin Falls County, Idaho, upheld the Sexual Offender Classification Board's (Board) decision classifying defendant as a violent sexual predator (VSP). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his constitutional rights were violated. The supreme court found that defendant was not provided notice or opportunity to be heard before the Board. Idaho's statutory scheme violated an offender's right to procedural due process by failing to provide notice and an opportunity to be heard at a meaningful time and in a meaningful manner and by placing the burden of proof on the offender at the only hearing in which he was permitted to appear. The proceedings did not satisfy defendant's right to procedural due process where defendant could not view the conclusions of the psychosexual evaluator or other test results. Defendant was not afforded the opportunity to review confidential parole commission notes that were included in the sealed file. Defendant demonstrated ineffective assistance of counsel where he was prejudiced by counsel's failure to timely assert defendant's claim that he was denied due process in the VSP designation process; in failing to timely assert a challenge to the Board's failure to adopt and apply objective criteria for VSP designation; and in failing to properly preserve defendant's due process challenge to the judicial review process.


OUTCOME: The district court judgment was reversed and remanded to the district court with direction to vacate defendant's designation as a VSP.

Smith v. State


Docket No. 33254, 2009 Opinion No. 22


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


2009 Ida. LEXIS 28



February 9, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Reprinted as amended at Smith v. State, 203 P.3d 1221, 2009 Ida. LEXIS 31 (Idaho, Feb. 10, 2009)

Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Twin Falls County. Honorable John C. Hohnhorst, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed a judgment of the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District, Twin Falls County (Idaho) upholding a decision of the Sexual Offender Classification Board that petitioner should be classified as a violent sexual predator (VSP) upon his release from imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was incarcerated for a rape of a fifteen-year-old girl, in violation of Idaho Code Ann. § 18-6101(1). HIs counsel should have presented petitioner's challenges that he was denied due process in the VSP designation process and that the Board failed to apply objective criteria, pursuant to the guidelines set forth in Idaho Code Ann. § 18-8314(5). This deficient performance resulted in prejudice to petitioner.

State v. Bishop


Docket No. 35241, 2009 Opinion No. 18


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


146 Idaho 804; 203 P.3d 1203; 2009 Ida. LEXIS 19



January 30, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at State v. Bishop, 2009 Ida. App. LEXIS 47 (Idaho Ct. App., Feb. 20, 2009)
Petition denied by State v. Bishop, 2009 Ida. App. LEXIS 42 (Idaho Ct. App., Mar. 13, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Gooding County. Honorable R. Barry Wood, District Judge.
State v. Bishop, 2007 Ida. App. LEXIS 108 (Idaho Ct. App., Dec. 4, 2007)



DISPOSITION: The district court's order denying the motion to suppress is reversed, the judgment of conviction is vacated, and the case is remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to felony possession of a controlled substance under Idaho Code Ann. § 37-2732(c)(1) and resisting an officer under Idaho Code Ann. § 18-705, after his motion to suppress was denied. The Court of Appeals of Idaho vacated defendant's convictions after determining that defendant's motion to suppress should have been granted. The State sought review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested after a police officer found methamphetamine in a bag he was carrying. On appeal, the court held that the trial court erred by denying defendant's motion to suppress the evidence because the officer's frisk of defendant was unlawful, as a reasonable person would not conclude that defendant posed a risk of danger. The officer's encounter with defendant took place in public while it was still light out and there was no suggestion that defendant was stopped in a high crime area. The officer's subjective feelings could not be relied on to justify the frisk, and evidence that defendant was acting nervous and may have been under the influence of a narcotic did not justify the frisk. Because the frisk was unlawful, it was not a duty under Idaho Code Ann. § 18-705 and defendant was entitled to peacefully refuse the frisk. Because defendant peacefully refused the frisk by merely turning around and telling the officer "no," the officer did not have probable cause to arrest defendant for obstructing an officer, and therefore the arrest was unlawful, and the methamphetamine that was seized after that unlawful arrest should have been suppressed.


OUTCOME: The order denying defendant's motion to suppress was reversed, defendant's conviction was vacated, and the case was remanded.

State v. Payne


Docket No. 28589, Docket No. 32389, 2008 Opinion No. 122


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


146 Idaho 548; 199 P.3d 123; 2008 Ida. LEXIS 224



December 15, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at State v. Payne, 2009 Ida. LEXIS 22 (Idaho, Jan. 9, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Thomas Neville, District Judge.
State v. Payne, 2008 Ida. LEXIS 121 (Idaho, June 18, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Conviction for first-degree murder, kidnapping, robbery and rape affirmed. Sentence of death on post-conviction vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County, convicting him of first-degree murder, first-degree kidnapping, robbery, and rape and sentencing him to death. He also appealed a judgment denying him postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for abducting the victim from a park, raping her, and then shooting and killing her. On appeal, the court held that the district court did not err by denying defendant's motion to suppress incriminating statements he made to police because defendant's statement "I don't think I should answer that" was not sufficiently clear such that a reasonable officers would understand it as an invocation of the right to remain silent, and therefore the officer had no duty to discontinue his questioning. In addition, the district court's conclusion that defendant knowingly and voluntarily waived his right to remain silent was supported by the evidence, including testimony from officers and medical personnel that defendant knew where he was, knew what day it was, answered questions accurately, and that his aspirin level did not require hospitalization and that he was not given any medication that would interfere with his mental processes. The court held that counsel was not ineffective for failing to move to suppress an eyewitness' identification of defendant because there was no state action and no police suggestiveness.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed but his sentence was vacated and the case was remanded for resentencing.

 

102 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Univ. of Idaho Found., Inc. v. Civic Partners, Inc. (In re Univ. Place/Idaho Water Ctr. Project)


Docket No. 34461, 2008 Opinion No. 121


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


146 Idaho 527; 199 P.3d 102; 2008 Ida. LEXIS 225



December 10, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at Univ. of Idaho Found., Inc. v. Civic Partners, Inc. (In re Univ. Place/Idaho Water Ctr. Project), 2009 Ida. LEXIS 23 (Idaho, Jan. 9, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Ada County. The Hon. Daniel C. Hurlbutt, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action for declaratory judgment, the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Ada County, entered a partial summary judgment holding that appellant college foundation was obligated to make payments under a contract between it and respondent civic entities. Respondent lessor was awarded costs and attorney fees. The college foundation appealed.


OVERVIEW: Ada County, Idaho, acquired property for a development project. A college foundation sub-leased a portion of the property. The foundation executed a memorandum of understanding with several civic entities, providing that the foundation, which was a tax-exempt entity, would make certain payments to help pay for improvements. Upon termination of the memorandum of understanding, the parties entered into a reconciliation agreement. The foundation filed suit against the lessor, the developer, and the civic entities, seeking a declaratory judgment of its obligations under the agreement. The lessor was the prevailing party on the foundation's claim that it had no legal obligation to make payments in lieu of taxes; the district court did not err by granting partial summary judgment against the foundation. The reconciliation agreement contained a merger clause, and it was unambiguous. The Supreme Court of Idaho upheld the district court's ruling that the lessor was entitled to an award of $ 213,600.95 in attorney fees under Idaho Code Ann. § 12-120(3), as it was the prevailing party in an action arising out of a commercial transaction.


OUTCOME: The partial judgment of the district court on the third count of the foundation's complaint was affirmed. The developer and the lessor were awarded costs on appeal. The lessor was also awarded attorney fees on appeal.

 

103 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Bartosz v. Jones


Docket No. 35091, 2008 Opinion No. 115


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


146 Idaho 449; 197 P.3d 310; 2008 Ida. LEXIS 198



October 16, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 5, 2008
Review denied by Bartosz v. Jones, 2008 Ida. LEXIS 216 (Idaho, Dec. 5, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Canyon County. Hon. Bradley S. Ford, Magistrate Judge.



DISPOSITION: Order on child custody is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged an order of the District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Canyon County, denying her petition to modify a child custody order to permit her to move her and respondent father's daughter to Hawaii under Idaho Code Ann. § 32-717.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that the magistrate did not abuse his discretion by denying the mother's request to modify the custody order because: (1) the magistrate considered factors relevant to whether a custodial parent should be permitted to relocate with a child, including the mother's motive for the move, the extent alternative visitation would allow the father and his daughter to maintain a close relationship, and the effect of the move on the daughter's extended family; (2) the magistrate did not apply an irrebuttable presumption against the physical separation of a child and a non-custodial parent; and (3) the magistrate's findings of fact and conclusions of law were supported by the evidence. The court further held that the custody order did not violate the mother's constitutional right to travel because the restriction on the mother's right to travel was necessary to serve a compelling state interest, namely the daughter's best interest. The magistrate found that the move was not in the daughter's best interest and there was no less restrictive alternative to achieve the state's objective.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

104 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Federated Publ'ns, Inc. v. Idaho Bus. Review, Inc.


Docket No. 34343, 2008 Opinion No. 104


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


146 Idaho 207; 192 P.3d 1031; 2008 Ida. LEXIS 164; 36 Media L. Rep. 2309



August 26, 2008, Filed 
September 18, 2008, Released for Publication


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Deborah A. Bail, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is reversed. Costs are awarded to Appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff newspaper sought a declaration that Idaho Code Ann. § 60-106 applied to all legal notices, including private and governmental notices. The Fourth Judicial District Court of the State of Idaho, Ada County, held that the statute did not violate Idaho Const. art. III, § 16. Defendant corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: The corporation contended that the district court's interpretation of the statute violated the single subject-in-title requirement of Idaho Const. art. III, § 16. A previous version of the statute, before its amendment, did not define "general circulation." The amended version of the statute required notice to be published in a newspaper of general interest, and it defined the "newspaper of general circulation." The supreme court first determined the proper interpretation of Idaho Code Ann. § 60-106, then it addressed whether the statute's title was consistent with the mandate of Idaho Code Ann. art. III, § 16. The supreme court concluded that the statute referred to where notice must be published, by governmental and non-governmental entitites alike, and not who was publishing the notice. As a result, the statute applied to both entities. The substance of the statute with respect to non-governmental entities was void because the substantive change was not indicated in the title. Finally, the newspaper was not entitled to attorney's fees because it was not the prevailing party.


OUTCOME: The supreme court found that Idaho Code § 60-106 constitutional as it applies to governmental entities, but unconstitutional and void in regard to non-governmental entities.

AmeriTel Inns, Inc. v. Pocatello-Chubbuck Auditorium


Docket No. 33448, 2008 Opinion No. 99


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


146 Idaho 202; 192 P.3d 1026; 2008 Ida. LEXIS 145



July 23, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 16, 2008
Rehearing denied by AmeriTel Inns, Inc. v. Pocatello-Chubbuck Auditorium, 2008 Ida. LEXIS 184 (Idaho, Sept. 12, 2008)
Petition denied by Ameritel Inns, Inc. v. Pocatello-Chubbuck Auditorium Dist., 2008 Ida. App. LEXIS 132 (Idaho Ct. App., Sept. 12, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Sixth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bannock County. Honorable Peter D. McDermott, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The district court order granting summary judgment is reversed and the case is remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Sixth Judicial District, Bannock County, Idaho, granted summary judgment in favor of respondent Pocatello-Chubbock Auditorium District (District) on appellant company's declaratory judgment action concerning the permissibility of expenditures made by the District. The company appealed; the District cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The company argued that Idaho Code §§ 67-4902, 67-4904, and 67-4922A did not authorize the District to market facilities that it did not own or operate and the legislature intended Idaho Code § 67-4902 to encourage local communities to build public facilities. The supreme court found that § 67-4902 defined "auditorium or community center district" and Idaho Code § 67-4912 enumerated the powers of the district's board. An auditorium district may build a facility that did not exist in its district, such as a convention center. The provisions of Idaho Code § 67-4904, as codified in 1998, did not reflect a legislative intent to expand the purposes or powers of an auditorium district. An auditorium district did not have the power to simply market public facilities within its borders. The District was not entitled to an award of attorney fees. The company was declined attorney fees as the District did not act without a reasonable basis in fact or law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded for further proceedings.

 

106 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Arel v. T & L Enters.


Docket No. 34562, 2008 Opinion No. 90


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


146 Idaho 29; 189 P.3d 1149; 2008 Ida. LEXIS 129



June 30, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 22, 2008


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the State Industrial Commission.



DISPOSITION: Industrial Commission decision dismissing worker's compensation claim, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Idaho Industrial Commission, adopting a referee's proposed finding that appellant employee had failed to meet a requirement of Idaho Code Ann. § 72-701 by failing to notify respondent employer of the employee's fall at work within 60 days of the fall, dismissed the employee's worker's compensation claim.


OVERVIEW: The requirement under Idaho Code Ann. § 72-701 that an employee who suffered an accident give the employer timely notice of the accident, even if that employee was unaware of the extent of the personal injury caused by the accident, did not violate the equal protection clause of either U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1 or Idaho Const. art. I, § 2 and was not a special law prohibited by Idaho Const. art. II, § 19. The terms of the statute applied to all persons and subject matters in a like situation. All employers under the worker's compensation law having employees who made a claim based on an occupational disease were treated the same. Additionally, all employers in the like situation of having employees who made a claim based on an accident were treated the same. Under the plain and unambiguous wording in Idaho Code Ann. § 72-701 and Idaho Code Ann. § 72-102(18)(b), a worker's compensation claimant was required to give notice of an accident within 60 days after it occurred and not within 60 days after the claimant became aware that the accident had caused a personal injury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision.

State v. Payne


Docket No. 28589, 2008 Opinion No. 86, Docket No. 32389


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


2008 Ida. LEXIS 121

Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Thomas Neville, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Conviction for first-degree murder, kidnapping, robberyand rape affirmed. Sentence of death on post-conviction vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County (Idaho), which convicted him of first-degree murder, kidnapping, robbery, and rape and summarily denied all but one of his claims for post-conviction relief. Respondent State cross-appealed the district court's order setting aside defendant's death sentence on post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant abducted, raped and murdered the victim, dumped her body in a drainage tank, and stole her car and credit cards. Reviewing the death penalty case in accordance with Idaho Code Ann. § 19-2827, the court found no errors at the trial level. Unlike the guilt phase, the court found reversible errors in the sentencing trial and accordingly vacated defendant's sentence. On remand, the district court should examine mitigating factors to determine if the death penalty would be unjust.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions, but vacated defendant's sentence. The court remanded to the district court for resentencing.

Pizzuto v. State


Docket No. 32679, 2008 Opinion No. 32


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


146 Idaho 720; 202 P.3d 642; 2008 Ida. LEXIS 39



February 22, 2008, Filed 
March 14, 2008, Released for Publication


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Pizzuto v. State, 2008 Ida. LEXIS 44 (Idaho, Mar. 14, 2008)
Stay lifted by, Habeas corpus proceeding at Pizzuto v. Hardison, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 42040 (D. Idaho, May 16, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Idaho County. The Hon. George R. Reinhardt, III, District Judge.
State v. Pizzuto, 119 Idaho 742, 810 P.2d 680, 1991 Ida. LEXIS 5 (Idaho, 1991)



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted in the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Idaho County of, inter alia, two counts of murder and was sentenced to death. After his petition for postconviction relief was denied, petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by dismissing his motion for postconviction relief because he was mentally retarded, and therefore, not eligible for execution. The supreme court disagreed. One requirement of proving mental retardation was that petitioner had an IQ of 70 or below at the time of the murders and prior to his eighteenth birthday. He did not offer any expert opinion showing that he did. He likewise did not offer any expert opinion stating that he was mentally retarded at the time of the murders or prior to age eighteen. The record reflected only one IQ score for petitioner. He scored an IQ of 72 when he was twenty-eight years old. There was no expert testimony opining what petitioner's IQ probably would have been eleven years earlier. Petitioner was found to be competent to stand trial. In an expert's opinion, petitioner understood the charges against him and their potential consequences and he was capable of assisting in his defense. Petitioner had the capacity to enter into a state of mind which was an element of the offense for which he was charged. Petitioner did not challenge on appeal the finding that he was competent to stand trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Ada County Highway Dist. v. Total Success Invs., LLC


Docket No. 32726, 2008 Opinion No. 29


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


145 Idaho 360; 179 P.3d 323; 2008 Ida. LEXIS 33



February 19, 2008, Filed 
March 12, 2008, Released for Publication


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Total Success Invs., LLC v. Ada County Highway Dist. (In re Encroachments), 2010 Ida. App. LEXIS 15 (Idaho Ct. App., Mar. 4, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Joel David Horton, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: District court decision holding highway district acquired highway pursuant to I.C. § 40-202(3), affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County, Idaho, granted judgment in favor of respondent Ada County Highway District (ACHD) to quiet title asserting it had acquired a highway over a portion of appellant property owner's property between the prior location of the fence and the current location of the fence under Idaho Code § 40-202 and an action for ejectment of the relocated fence. The owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owner argued that ACHD did not meet the elements of Idaho Code § 40-202, its quiet title action was barred by Idaho Code § 5-202. The supreme court found that a maintenance had been performed by ACHD continuously and as necessary from 1978 on. The strip in question was used frequently by adjacent landowners and individuals accessing the businesses and, therefore, supported a conclusion of extensive public use. Because ACHD brought the action within ten years of the encroachment, the suit was not barred by Idaho Code § 5-202. The record did not contain a decision by the district court regarding spoliation. Idaho Code § 40-202 was not unconstitutional on its face. The landowner had four years from the accrual of the cause of action to bring a claim of inverse condemnation. The owner was not entitled to a jury trial on ACHD's ejectment claim. There was no waiver and the unclean hands doctrine did not preclude ACHD from quieting title in the roadway or requiring the owner to remove the encroaching fence. The owner had notice and the opportunity to be heard. The owner failed to meet its burden to show the indispensability of the city, federal government, power company, or the bank.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Joslin


Docket No. 32483, 2007 Opinion No. 136


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


145 Idaho 75; 175 P.3d 764; 2007 Ida. LEXIS 230



December 24, 2007, Filed 
January 15, 2008, Released for Publication


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Bingham County. The Hon. James C. Herndon, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Seventh Judicial District Court, Bingham County, Idaho, convicted defendant of statutory rape. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the district court committed various errors during the trial and that the statutes defining the crime and fixing the punishment were unconstitutional. The supreme court disagreed, holding first that the district court did not abuse its discretion in refusing to instruct the jury further on the definition of vaginal opening because two physicians explained for the jury where the vaginal opening was, the victim testified that defendant penetrated her vagina with his penis, and defendant admitted to a police officer that he had done so. Further, the victim's testimony and defendant's confession provided evidence upon which a reasonable trier of fact could have found that defendant penetrated the victim's vaginal opening with his penis. Contrary to defendant's assertion, Idaho Code Ann. § 18-6101(1) did not violate the state or federal equal protection provisions; nor did the sexual offender registration requirements of Idaho Code Ann. § 18-8304(4) violate protections against cruel and unusual punishment as the requirements did not impose punishment. The purpose of the registration statute was not punitive, but remedial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

111 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Pizzuto v. State


Docket No. 32679, 2007 Opinion No. 115


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


2007 Ida. LEXIS 209



November 23, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Pizzuto v. State, 2008 Ida. LEXIS 46 (Idaho, Mar. 19, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Idaho County. The Hon. George R. Reinhardt, III, District Judge.
State v. Pizzuto, 119 Idaho 742, 810 P.2d 680, 1991 Ida. LEXIS 5 (Idaho, 1991)



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Idaho County, found petitioner inmate guilty of two murders. He was sentenced to death. He filed his fifth petition for post-conviction relief, challenging his death sentence on the ground that he was mentally retarded. The district court dismissed his petition on summary judgment. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: One requirement of proving mental retardation under Idaho Code Ann. § 19-2515A was that the inmate had an intelligence quotient (IQ) of 70 or below at the time of the murders and prior to his 18th birthday. He did not offer any expert opinion stating that he was mentally retarded at the time of the murders and prior to the age of 18. In its briefing opposing the inmate's motion for summary judgment, the State argued that the inmate had failed to provide evidence that his IQ was 70 or below and failed to provide evidence showing it was 70 or below prior to his 18th birthday. The inmate's alleged IQ was obviously a matter requiring expert testimony; however, the inmate did not offer any expert testimony opining that his IQ was ever 70 or below, nor did he allege that the additional testing he requested intended to address that issue. Whether or not a person was mentally retarded was obviously a matter requiring an expert's opinion, but he did not offer any expert testimony on that issue. Thus, the district court did not err in granting summary judgment to the State on the inmate's petition for post-conviction relief, challenging his death sentence because he was mentally retarded.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the district court's judgment.

Karel v. Dep't of Fin. (In re Karel)


Docket No. 33191, 2007 Opinion No. 93


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


144 Idaho 379; 162 P.3d 758; 2007 Ida. LEXIS 165



June 27, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 19, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. D. Duff McKee, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Decision and order of the district court on judicial review of a Department of Finance decision suspending a securities agent's license is: reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County, Idaho, affirmed a final order by respondent Department of Finance (Department), which resulted in the suspension of appellant employee's license as a securities agent. The Department suspended her license for a six-month period based on its finding that the employee violated Idaho Code § 30-14-411(d) by refusing to provide records requested. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee argued that the Department had no authority to request the records it did because the pertinent statutes did not list those items as records the employee was required to maintain and provide for inspection. Idaho Code § 30-14-411(d) simply permitted the Department to conduct a reasonable audit and inspection of all records the administrator reasonably considered necessary or appropriate to conduct the audit or inspection. The supreme court found that securities agents like the employee had an obligation to make certain records available upon reasonable request by the Department. The records to be made available for audit and inspection were those required to be maintained in Idaho Code § 30-14-411(c). Even though the employee was not personally required to make or maintain the records outlined in subsection (c), she was required to surrender those documents for inspection pursuant to Idaho Code § 30-14-411(d). However, the Department did not have the authority to request the documents it sought pursuant to § 30-14-411(d). Both parties were denied attorney's fees on appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded to the Department of Finance for further action.

Doe v. Dep't of Heath & Welfare

DISPOSITION: The judgment of the magistrate court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Idaho Department of Health and Welfare filed a petition under the Child Protective Act, Idaho Code Ann. § 16-1601 et seq., seeking to terminate appellant father's parental rights to his five children. The District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Canyon County, entered an order terminating the father's parental rights. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The sole issue on appeal was whether there was substantial and competent evidence to support the magistrate judge's finding of chronic abuse. The evidence clearly supported the finding that the father subjected his youngest child to chronic abuse where it showed that the child had been deprived of food for a sufficiently long period of time that his height and weight were well below the third percentile, he had muscle wasting and was very weak, he lacked subcutaneous tissue, and his abdomen was protruding. A pediatrician had testified that it would have taken about five months for a healthy child to reach that condition.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

114 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Cowles Publ'g Co. v. Kootenai County Bd. of County Comm'rs


Docket No. 32195, Docket No. 32206, 2007 Opinion No. 74


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


144 Idaho 259; 159 P.3d 896; 2007 Ida. LEXIS 120; 35 Media L. Rep. 2107



May 4, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 28, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District, State of Idaho, Kootenai County. Honorable John R. Stegner, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The district court's order granting Cowles's petition for access to public records is affirmed and the district court's permanent protective order sealing the settlement agreement is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county employee appealed an order of the First Judicial District Court, Kootenai County, Idaho, which concluded that certain e-mail correspondence between the employee and intervenor county prosecutor were public records and not exempt from disclosure. Respondent publishing company cross-appealed from a protective order permanently sealing a settlement agreement between intervenor insurer and the employee.


OVERVIEW: The court concluded that the e-mails in question were public records pursuant to Idaho Code Ann. § 9-337(13). The e-mails contained information relating to the conduct and administration of the public's business. The public had a legitimate interest in these communications between the prosecutor and the employee because the prosecutor defended the employee's management of a county program when an investigation of the program's finances was started by the board of county commissioners. The e-mails were not exempt from disclosure under Idaho Code Ann. § 9-340C because they were informal communications between an employee and her supervisor, unrelated to personnel administration. The employee had no legitimate expectation of privacy in the e-mails. The settlement agreement between the county's insurer and the employee was properly sealed. The settlement was executed in order to conclude any potential claims between the employee and the county. Under Idaho Code Ann. § 9-340D(11) only statistical data and the actual amount paid were public records. Any other information contained in the settlement or other records relating to the employee's claim were exempt from disclosure.


OUTCOME: The orders were affirmed.

Baird Oil Co., Inc. v. Idaho State Tax Comm'n


Docket No. 31668, 2007 Opinion No. 68A


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


144 Idaho 229; 159 P.3d 866; 2007 Ida. LEXIS 112



May 1, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 25, 2007.
As Amended May 3, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Michael R. McLaughlin, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The district court decision affirming the Idaho State Tax Commission is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff oil company sought review of an order from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County (Idaho), which held that its action against defendant, the Idaho State Tax Commission, for a refund of transfer fees paid into the Idaho petroleum clean water trust fund was barred by res judicata.


OVERVIEW: The company sought judicial review of an order from the Commission that the company and members of the Idaho Petroleum Marketers Association were not entitled to a refund of transfer fees paid into the fund for periods before October 1, 1999. The trial court upheld the Commission's interpretation of the Idaho Petroleum Clean Water Trust Fund Act, Idaho Code Ann. § 41-4901 et seq., finding that the Commission could not suspend transfer fees until the Director of the Idaho Department of Insurance had determined that the cap had been reached. The company later filed a request with the Commission for a refund of fees. The Commission denied the request. The trial court ruled that the company's action was barred by res judicata. On appeal, the court found that the issue of whether the company was entitled to a refund was previously resolved. The company was barred from litigating the issue further. The Commission did not waive its right to rely on res judicata when it entered a stipulation to stay the claims of other petroleum distributors; the Commission was simply agreeing that it would go forward with the case against the oil company first, and obtain a resolution through appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Hairston v. State


Docket No. 28528/29653/29680, 2007 Opinion No. 52


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


144 Idaho 51; 156 P.3d 552; 2007 Ida. LEXIS 78



March 28, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 19, 2007.
Vacated by, Remanded by, Motion granted by Pizzuto v. Idaho, 128 S. Ct. 1441, 170 L. Ed. 2d 271, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 2023 (U.S., 2008)
Vacated by, Remanded by, Motion granted by Rhoades v. Idaho, 128 S. Ct. 1441, 170 L. Ed. 2d 271, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 2030 (U.S., 2008)
Vacated by, Remanded by, Motion granted by Hairston v. Idaho, 128 S. Ct. 1442, 170 L. Ed. 2d 272, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 2050 (U.S., 2008)
Vacated by, Remanded by, Motion granted by Card v. Idaho, 128 S. Ct. 1442, 170 L. Ed. 2d 271, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 2131 (U.S., 2008)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Hairston v. State, 2008 Ida. LEXIS 226 (Idaho, Mar. 28, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Sixth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bannock County. Hon. Peter D. McDermott, District Judge.
State v. Hairston, 133 Idaho 496, 988 P.2d 1170, 1999 Ida. LEXIS 100 (Idaho, 1999)



DISPOSITION: The Motion to Dismiss Petitioner's consecutive petitions for post-conviction relief is: granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision from the District Court of the Sixth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bannock County, which dismissed his consolidated successive petitions for post-conviction relief, petition for a writ of habeas corpus, a motion to correct an illegal sentence, a motion to vacate a sentence of death, and a motion for a new sentencing trial. The State filed a motion to dismiss the appeal.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's murder and robbery convictions were affirmed on direct appeal. Later, the district court denied his request for several types of relief. The cases were consolidated, and this appeal followed. In dismissing, the supreme court determined that appellant had one opportunity to raise all challenges to the capital conviction and sentence under Idaho Code Ann. § 19-2719(2), except in unusual cases where it was demonstrated that the issues were not known and reasonably could not have been known in the 42-day time frame in § 19-2719(3). Section 19-2719 was not unconstitutional as violative of equal protection and due process of law. Moreover, it was not unconstitutionally vague because it identifies two possibilities under a clear single standard. Moreover, appellant's ineffective assistance of counsel claims were untimely under § 19-2719(5) because they were raised three years after his appellate briefing. Res judicata barred his argument regarding the failure to supply a mitigation expert. Finally, the motion to correct the sentence under Idaho Crim. R. 35 was untimely because the time periods in Idaho Code Ann. § 19-2719(3) applied instead.


OUTCOME: The State's motion to dismiss was granted.

 

117 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Am. Falls Reservoir Dist. No. 2 v. Idaho Dep't of Water Res.


Docket No. 33249/33311/33399, 2007 Opinion No. 40


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


143 Idaho 862; 154 P.3d 433; 2007 Ida. LEXIS 55



March 5, 2007, Filed  
August 31, 2007, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Am. Falls Reservoir Dist. No.2 v. Idaho Dep't of Water Res., 2007 Ida. LEXIS 182 (Idaho, Aug. 30, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Gooding County. Hon. R. Barry Wood, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Decision of the district court granting summary judgment to the plaintiffs, finding the Rules for Conjunctive Management of Surface and Ground Water Resources unconstitutional, is: Reversed. Decision of the district court denying the City of Pocatello intervention in the case is: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Fifth Judicial District, Gooding County, Idaho, granted judgment in favor of respondents, water districts and corporations, finding that the Rules for Conjunctive Management of Surface and Ground Water Resources (CM Rules) lacked certain procedural components necessary to the proper administration of water rights. Appellant Idaho Department of Water Resources (IDWR) and intervenor company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court noted that its review would be in terms of the CM Rules' constitutionality on their face and not in terms of their "threatened application" or "as applied." The issue was whether the challenged provisions were void in all possible applications, or whether there were a set of circumstances in which they may be constitutionally applied. The failure to explicitly recite certain procedural components such as the burdens of proof did not make the CM Rules unconstitutional. The Rules could be constitutionally applied to provide for the timely delivery of water. There was no basis for setting aside the CM Rules based upon the lack of specifically articulated time standards. The CM Rules did not unconstitutionally force a senior water rights holder to re-adjudicate a right, nor did they fail to give adequate consideration to a partial decree. The CM Rules were not unconstitutional in permitting some discretion in the IDWR Director to determine whether the carryover water was reasonably necessary for future needs. There was no requirement that the CM Rules had to incorporate every possible remedy to a senior who felt that his water right had been improperly reduced.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed as to the finding of unconstitutionality; the district court's revocation of the city's motion to intervene was affirmed.

State v. District Court (In re Petition for Writ of Prohibition)


Docket No. 29203, 2007 Opinion No. 6


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


143 Idaho 695; 152 P.3d 566; 2007 Ida. LEXIS 10



January 26, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 20, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for a Writ of Prohibition against the Honorable Deborah A. Bail, District Judge.
Idaho Schs. for Equal Educ. Opportunity v. State, 142 Idaho 450, 129 P.3d 1199, 2005 Ida. LEXIS 189 (Idaho, 2005)



DISPOSITION: The Petition for a Writ is: Denied. The decision of the district court is: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District and a judge, appointed a special master to assist with the "remedial phase" of litigation related to the funding of public schools by petitioner, the State of Idaho. The district court charged the State with payment of the special master fees, and the State sought a writ of prohibition under Idaho Const. art. V, § 9, to enjoin the district court from assessing said fees against it.


OVERVIEW: The district court hired a special master under Idaho R. Civ. P. 53(a)(1) to conduct a survey of every school district in Idaho to determine the extent of the buildings needing repair as well as the most cost-effective method of addressing the hazards they presented. The State claimed that the district court exceeded its jurisdiction in ordering the State to bear the costs. The court found that a writ of prohibition was not proper because the appointment of a special master and the assessment of costs under Idaho R. Civ. P. 54(d) fell within the discretion of the district court. Because the issues were identical to those raised on direct appeal, the court treated the matter as a direct appeal and upheld the award of fees against the State. Idaho Code Ann. §§ 12-101 and 12-121, as well as Idaho R. Civ. P. 53, provided clear authority for the award of costs for the special master. Further, Idaho Code Ann. § 12-118 provided the relevant direction as to how costs awarded against the State were to be paid. Finally, the court denied the request for attorney fees by intervenors under the private attorney general doctrine because the issue was not a matter of substantial public policy.


OUTCOME: The court denied the writ of prohibition, addressed the case as if on direct appeal, affirmed the district court's award of costs against the State, and found a statutory basis for the award. The court awarded costs on appeal to the district court and the judge and denied the request for attorney fees by intervenors.

United Investors Life Ins. Co. v. Severson


Docket No. 31690, 2007 Opinion No. 2


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


143 Idaho 628; 151 P.3d 824; 2007 Ida. LEXIS 3



January 16, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 7, 2007.
Related proceeding at State v. Severson, 2009 Ida. LEXIS 89 (Idaho, May 29, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Elmore County. Honorable Michael E. Wetherell, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: District court order granting summary judgment, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband challenged a decision from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Elmore County, which granted partial judgment in favor of respondent primary beneficiary in a life insurance dispute and determined that the husband was not entitled to any of the proceeds. It also held that the estate was entitled to half of the proceeds.


OVERVIEW: The husband attempted to get the proceeds of a term life insurance policy. However, he was merely listed as the contingent beneficiary. The proceeds were deposited with the trial court. One-half was given to the beneficiary. After the husband was convicted of first degree murder, the district court ruled that the other half should pass to the decedent's estate as the husband was barred from receiving his share under Idaho Code Ann. § 15-2-803. This appeal followed. In partially affirming, the supreme court determined that § 15-2-803(e) did not apply to this case because the proceeds in question were not characterized as community property. It was a term life insurance policy; the husband had no vested interest in such until the death of his wife. However, there was an alternative reason for the district court's decision. Section 15-2-803(b), (n) prohibited the husband from acquiring any benefit as a result of the death of his wife. Next, the criminal appeal had no effect on the case. The husband provided no basis for his argument that § 15-2-803 amounted to an unconstitutional taking. Finally, neither party was entitled to attorney's fees.


OUTCOME: The decision to grant summary judgment was affirmed. The decision that one-half of the policy passed to the decedent's estate was reversed. The supreme court held that the entire policy passed according to the terms of the policy. The case was remanded for further proceedings.

Cowan v. Bd. of Comm'rs


Docket No. 30061, 2006 Opinion No. 107


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


143 Idaho 501; 148 P.3d 1247; 2006 Ida. LEXIS 151



November 29, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 21, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District, State of Idaho, Fremont County. Honorable Brent J. Moss, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: District court decision approving preliminary and final plats for proposed subdivision, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Fremont County Board of Commissioners and defendant individual commissioners approved the preliminary and final plats for a proposed subdivision. The District Court of the Seventh Judicial District, State of Idaho, Fremont County, affirmed the decision. Plaintiff landowner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Several petitions for review were filed, which the district court consolidated. The property developer planned to subdivide and develop home sites on a parcel located adjacent to the landowner's property. At issue on appeal were: (1) alleged due process violations; (2) alleged arbitrary and capricious actions; and (3) alleged unsupported decisions. The arguments related to the developer's first application were moot. The landowner, however, did have standing to allege an injury. The Board correctly argued that Idaho Code § 67-6535(b) did not apply to decisions of the planning and zoning commission. Also, the Board did comply with § 67-6535(b). The landowner's due process rights were not violated by the limitation of public comments. Although notices for two meetings were defective, the landowner failed to show prejudice. Next, the supreme court had never adopted the appearance of fairness doctrine with respect to due process. Next, the supreme court could not find that the Board's interpretation was arbitrary or capricious. The Board also reasonably applied Section 402 of the Clean Water Act, 33 U.S.C.S. § 1342. The evidence the Board chose to rely on was substantial and competent.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the Board's approval of the application for a Class II permit. Neither party was awarded attorney's fees on appeal. Costs were awarded to the Board.

Davidson v. Wright


Docket No. 31792, Docket No. 31793, 2006 Opinion No. 89


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


143 Idaho 616; 151 P.3d 812; 2006 Ida. LEXIS 128



September 27, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 15, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Davidson v. Wright, 2007 Ida. LEXIS 4 (Idaho, Jan. 18, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Blaine County. Robert James Elgee, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: District court decision denying petition for city initiative, reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant presenters challenged a decision from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Blaine County, which ruled that respondent city was permitted to refuse to approve a petition for a city initiative. The presenters sought attorney fees on appeal.


OVERVIEW: The city clerk rejected a proposed marijuana initiative, and presenters filed an action against the city under Idaho Code § 50-406. The city filed an action for declaratory relief, and the two actions were consolidated. The district court ruled in favor of the city, and the presenters sought review. In reversing, the appellate court determined that the city clerk was not vested with authority to evaluate the constitutionality of the proposed initiative under Sun Valley, Idaho, Code § 1-7-2-3(C). The city was obligated to follow its own ordinance. The city clerk's review was limited to form only, and nothing gave the clerk authority to review it for validity or constitutionality. Next, the district court erred by ruling on the declaratory judgment action under Idaho Code Ann. § 10-1201 because whether the initiative concerned matters outside the scope of such was not ripe for adjudication since it was a pre-election challenge. Finally, the city was not entitled to attorney fees as it was not the prevailing party, and the presenters were not entitled to such fees on appeal since there was a reasonable basis for the city's action under Idaho Code Ann. § 12-117.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed. Costs were awarded to the presenters, but no attorney fees on appeal were awarded.

City of Boise City v. Keep the Commandments Coalition (In re Initiative Petition for a Ten Commandments Display)


Docket No. 31308, 2006 Opinion No. 84


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


143 Idaho 254; 141 P.3d 1123; 2006 Ida. LEXIS 115



August 14, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Honorable Ronald J. Wilper, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County, Idaho, granted a declaratory judgment in favor of respondent city on its petition requesting the district court to decree that the city was not authorized or required to hold an initiative election on appellant coalition's petition demanding the enactment of a proposed ordinance for a Ten Commandments display to be placed in a park. The coalition appealed.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court noted that the issue was whether the initiative process should be interpreted by the court to consider the validity of the initiative on an otherwise qualified initiative petition prior to submission to the voters. The initiative process arose from Idaho Const. art. III, § 1, and extended to the cities by legislative mandate, Idaho Code § 50-501. The initiative process was a mandate that enabled voters to address issues of concern. The initiative might not pass in which case the issue of whether it stepped over the bounds of a proper initiative would be moot. The initiative might pass and be the proper subject of an adjudication, or the city council might exercise its authority and amend or reject it. Just as the supreme court would not interrupt the legislature in the consideration of a bill prior to enactment, it would not interrupt the consideration of a properly qualified initiative.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

123 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Sanchez v. State


Docket No. 32266, 2006 Opinion No. 82


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


143 Idaho 239; 141 P.3d 1108; 2006 Ida. LEXIS 114



August 8, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. D. Duff McKee, District Judge.
Sanchez v. State Dep't of Correction, 134 Idaho 523, 5 P.3d 984, 2000 Ida. LEXIS 63 (Idaho, 2000)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court in reviewing a Personnel Commission decision is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fourth Judicial District Court, Ada County, Idaho, reversed the decision of the Idaho Personnel Commission (Commission) in denying respondent employee attorney fees and prejudgment interest on the employee's wrongful discharge case against appellant Idaho Department of Correction (IDOC). IDOC appealed.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court noted that as the employee chose not to make the argument about why Idaho Code § 12-117 might support a fee award against IDOC, it would not address the statute further. Rule 201, Idaho Admin. Code 15.04.01.201.10, was not an independent basis for a fee award, but only described the procedure to be followed if there was a statutory basis for such an award. The Commission did not err in ruling it did not have authority under Idaho Code § 12-121 to award fees as the proceedings were not a civil action commenced by the filing of a complaint as required by Idaho R. Civ. P. 3(a). Idaho Code § 67-5316(4) specifically mentioned reinstatement, with or without loss of pay. Nothing in that phrase would lead to the conclusion the legislature also intended to include an award of attorney fees as a possible "other remedy." The employee presented no arguments as to whether any of the statutes were unconstitutional. Neither the general law on interest, Idaho Code § 28-22-104, nor the general language of Idaho Code § 67-5316(4) overcame the presumption of IDOC's sovereign immunity from an award of prejudgment interest. The employee was not entitled to an award of attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Idaho Press Club, Inc. v. State Legislature


Docket No. 31667, 2006 Opinion No. 24


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


142 Idaho 640; 132 P.3d 397; 2006 Ida. LEXIS 35; 34 Media L. Rep. 1436



March 20, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for publication April 11, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Ada County. The Hon. Kathryn A. Sticklen, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant press club filed an action seeking a declaratory judgment holding that the conduct of the Idaho Legislature, in closing legislative committee meetings to the public, violated Idaho Const. art. III, § 12. The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Ada County, held that article III, § 12 did not apply to meetings of legislative committees, and the press club appealed.


OVERVIEW: The issue before the supreme court was whether article III, § 12 required all meetings of legislative committees to be open to the public. The task was solely to decide whether the constitution required that they must be open. "Expressio unius est exclusio alterius" applied as a rule of construction. The press club correctly admitted that the ability to close committee meetings was never discussed or raised by the constitutional delegates when framing the constitution; however, the press club contended that the phrase "business of each house" should be construed to include legislative committees. Nevertheless, the supreme court recognized that there were problems with the press club's argument that because each house utilized legislative committees in order to function, the work of such committees was included in the phrase "business of each house." The supreme court concluded that, using the recognized rules of construction, Idaho Const. art. III, § 12 did not apply to legislative committee meetings. Where the constitution did not limit the power of the legislature to close its legislative committee meetings, the supreme court did not have the power to order that they be open.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the district court's judgment.

Sons & Daughters of Idaho, Inc. v. Idaho Lottery Comm'n


Docket No. 31609, 2006 Opinion No. 30


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


142 Idaho 659; 132 P.3d 416; 2006 Ida. LEXIS 36



March 20, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for publication April 11, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, for Ada County. Hon. Joel D. Horton, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The district court's opinion is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff organization sought a declaratory judgment against defendant Idaho State Lottery Commission, finding that an amendment to the gaming tracking provision was not enacted in substantial compliance with the Idaho Administrative Procedure Act. The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, for Ada County denied the requested relief. The organization appealed.


OVERVIEW: This case arose from 2001 amendments to the Gaming Rules, Idaho Admin. Code r. 52.01.02 for bingo which, among other things, required bingo operators to track all bingo paper used. The organization argued that Idaho Admin. Code r. 52.01.02.106.01 (Rule 106.01) was void because the Lottery failed to provide sufficient notice prior to enacting the rule and because the Lottery failed to maintain an adequate rulemaking record. These issues were moot. Also, the organization did not have a legally cognizable interest in the outcome of these issues. As to the organization's argument that Rule 106.01 was unconstitutionally vague, this contention also failed. While the Gaming Update was not legally enforceable, it did provide guidance in the interpretation of the Gaming Rules. Additionally, Rule 106.01 was better understood when read with the other provisions of Idaho Admin. Code r. 52.01.02.106. When considering these rules, a practical interpretation of Rule 106.01 was that bingo operators could track and group the bingo papers used per session according to their appropriate designation. The Lottery was not required to prescribe a form for the Rule 106.01 paper tracking requirements.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the district court's order denying the request to declare paper tracking requirements void.

Gibson v. Ada County

SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


142 Idaho 746; 133 P.3d 1211; 2006 Ida. LEXIS 12

Rehearing denied by Gibson v. Ada County, 2006 Ida. LEXIS 79 (Idaho, May 9, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Gibson v. Ada County, 549 U.S. 994, 127 S. Ct. 496, 166 L. Ed. 2d 366, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 8036 (2006)
Related proceeding at Gibson v. Ada County Sheriff's Office, 2009 Ida. LEXIS 92 (Idaho, June 8, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District for Ada County. Honorable Ronald J. Wilper, District Judge and Joel D. Horton, District Judge.
Gibson v. Ada County, 138 Idaho 787, 69 P.3d 1048, 2003 Ida. LEXIS 61 (Idaho, 2003)



DISPOSITION: The orders of the district court are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee challenged defendant county's termination of her employment. The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District for Ada County, Idaho, affirmed a hearing officer's decision. The employee filed a second complaint alleging civil rights violations. A third suit was later filed seeking repayment of wages. The county filed suit, seeking to collect an overpayment of wages. The employee appealed, and all the matters were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: In the first case, the district court's decision was vacated, and the claims were dismissed on appeal. In the second case, the district court denied the employee's petition for judicial review. Summary judgment for the county was granted in the third and fourth cases. The suits arose out of the alleged overpayment of wages that were deposited into the employee's personal account. On appeal, the supreme court determined that the civil rights actions, based on 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, were properly dismissed because they were time barred; however, an award of attorney fees arising out of these claims was not appropriate. P. 84, a petition for judicial review would only lie if permitted by statute. There existed no statute or constitutional authority under Idaho law allowing a Board of County Commissions to review the personnel decision of other elected county officers. The appeal on this issue was frivolous. The employee's request for declaratory judgment in the third case was misplaced. Finally, summary judgment for the county was proper in its suit.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the district court's decisions to deny the employee's petition for judicial review and motion to remand. Attorney fees were awarded to the county in the third case. The supreme court affirmed the district court's decision to grant summary judgment in favor of the county, and it awarded attorney fees incurred on appeal to the county.

Idaho Legislative Reapportionment Plan of 2002 v. Ysursa


Docket No. 30236, 2005 Opinion No. 138


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


142 Idaho 464; 129 P.3d 1213; 2005 Ida. LEXIS 193



December 28, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 14, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Bingham County v. Idaho Comm'n for Reapportionament (In re Petition Challenging Legislative Redistricting), 137 Idaho 870, 55 P.3d 863, 2002 Ida. LEXIS 35 (Idaho, 2002)



DISPOSITION: The Petition challenging Legislative Redistricting Plan L97 is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, county commissioners, voters, and state representatives, filed a petition against defendants, the secretary of state and the State, contending that a reapportionment plan violated the federal one-person, one-vote requirement and state constitutional and statutory provisions controlling the district-drawing process. Petitioners sought declaratory and injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: The commission for reapportionment adopted the plan at issue after other plans failed. Under the plan, the total maximum population deviation was 9.71 % and the court held that the plan was presumptively constitutional. The court found that petitioners had not demonstrated that regional deviation created constitutional problems for the plan. Under the plan the number of districts in any region corresponded closely to the number of people therein. The numerical discrepancies between districts in the "northern" region and the rest of the state did not show that the regional deviation was significant enough to effectively dilute the right to vote for non-northern voters, and there was no evidence showing that the commission intentionally favored one region to the detriment of another. As to splitting a county, the record showed that if that county were not split, another county would have to be split so that the other county did not have all its districts wholly contained within it. The court found that Idaho Code § 72-1506 qualified as the statute referenced in Idaho Const. art. III, § 5. Furthermore, petitioners did not explain how 78 precinct splits affected their right to vote.


OUTCOME: The court held that the plan was constitutional and dismissed the petition.

Kolar v. Cassia County Idaho


Docket No. 30727, 2005 Opinion No. 137


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


142 Idaho 346; 127 P.3d 962; 2005 Ida. LEXIS 192



December 28, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication: January 19, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, for County of Cassia. Hon. Monte B. Carlson, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Fifth Judicial District for the County of Cassia, Idaho, granted judgment in favor of respondents, a county, highway districts, and a driver, on appellant worker's claim after he was run over by a dump truck. The district court found that the respondents were the worker's so-called statutory employers and immune from suit. The worker appealed.


OVERVIEW: The worker argued that the district court lacked jurisdiction to determine whether the respondents were his statutory employers. The appellate court noted that the legislature granted a common law right of action in an injured worker against a third party, under Idaho Code § 72-223(2). Since status as a statutory employer was a defense to a common law negligence action, deciding whether a defendant was a third party or statutory employer necessarily attended the district court's task in ruling on matters in such suits. The respondents were an "employer" within the meaning of that term as found in Idaho Code § 72-223(1) and Idaho Code § 72-216. A rational basis existed for the grant of immunity in Idaho Code § 72-223, even if the statutory employer did not have to pay benefits because the direct employer had. While the worker's due process issue was raised and argued, it was not supported with any real authority. The vagueness and uncertainty arguments were belied by the plain language of the statute, which clearly stated who was not a third party. Idaho Code § 54-1218 was not irreconcilable with Idaho Code §§ 72-223 and 72-216. None of the parties were entitled to attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
