Oldcastle Precast, Inc. v. Parktowne Constr., Inc.


Docket No. 30549, 2005 Opinion No. 132


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


142 Idaho 376; 128 P.3d 913; 2005 Ida. LEXIS 181



December 22, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 8, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Oldcastle Precast, Inc. v. Parktowne Constr., Inc., 2006 Ida. LEXIS 13 (Idaho, Feb. 8, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Canyon County. The Hon. Gregory M. Culet, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant subcontractor sued respondents, a contractor and its insurer, in the District Court of the Third Judicial District, Canyon County, Idaho, to recover an unpaid amount of money on a construction project, and the contractor counterclaimed for breach of contract. The insurer paid all amounts due under a performance bond, and the contractor's counterclaim was found to be meritless. The subcontractor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court awarded the subcontractor attorney fees against the contractor and the insurer up to the date of trial pursuant to Idaho Code § 54-1929; however, it refused to award the subcontractor attorney fees under that statute for successfully defending against the contractor's counterclaim. The supreme court initially noted that the trial court properly awarded the subcontractor attorney fees incurred by it up to the date it was paid all sums due under the bond by the contractor's insurer. The supreme court held that attorney fees incurred by the subcontractor after it had been paid in full were not incurred in an action under the performance bond; therefore, the trial court correctly found that the subcontractor was not entitled to attorney fees under Idaho Code § 54-1929 for successfully defending against the contractor's counterclaim for breach of contract. The supreme court concluded that the subcontractor would have been entitled to an award of attorney fees under Idaho Code § 12-120(3) for successfully defending against the counterclaim but that it did not request attorney fees under that statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Idaho Schs. for Equal Educ. Opportunity v. State


Docket No. 29616, 2005 Opinion No. 131


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


142 Idaho 450; 129 P.3d 1199; 2005 Ida. LEXIS 189

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication: January 12, 2006.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Deborah A. Bail, District Judge.
Idaho Schs. for Equal Educ. Opportunity v. State, 140 Idaho 586, 97 P.3d 453, 2004 Ida. LEXIS 166 (Idaho, 2004)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court granting Respondents' declaratory judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents and plaintiff school districts sought declaratory relief against defendant state in an action challenging the adequacy and method of funding public education in Idaho. The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County , issued findings of fact and conclusions of law that the current state system was inadequate and unconstitutional pursuant to Idaho Const. art. IX, § 1. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: In complex litigation involving multiple parties, the district court determined that the state failed in its constitutional duty to provide a thorough education for Idaho's public school students in a safe environment conducive to learning, especially as it pertained to the poorest of school districts. When the legislature, in the district court's opinion, had failed to take appropriate action, the district court began implementing its remedial measures. The district court did not commit any error in making some generalized findings about facility problems, after pointing out some specific and illustrative examples. The supreme court noted that the district court used its discretion in admitting certain affidavits. The supreme court commended the legislature for taking steps towards providing a safe environment; however, that legislation did not make this case moot. Under the public interest exception, an otherwise moot issue could be heard if it was one of substantial public interest. The state next charged the district court erred in ordering the state to pay lead testing expenses. The district court did err in this regard. There was no statute authorizing this award.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the district court's conclusion.

State v. Bennett


Docket Nos. 31117/31118/31119, 2005 Opinion No. 122


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


142 Idaho 166; 125 P.3d 522; 2005 Ida. LEXIS 168



November 23, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication: December 15, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court of the Second Judicial District for Latah County. Hon. John R. Stegner, District Judge, Hon. William C. Hamlett, Magistrate Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Second Judicial District for Latah County, Idaho, upheld the magistrate court's denial of defendants' motion to dismiss the charges against them for violating Idaho Code § 23-604, which prohibited individuals under twenty-one years of age from purchasing, consuming, or possessing alcoholic beverages. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued that a spoliation of evidence occurred when the citing officers dumped out the contents of, and then threw away, the can and bottles containing the alcoholic beverages "allegedly" in the possession of defendants. The appellate court found that there was nothing to suggest that defendants were not holding containers, or that they were anything than alcohol containers, or that the liquid inside was anything other than alcohol. There was no showing to support an inference that the destroyed evidence would have been exculpatory. There was no showing of bad faith in the destruction of the cans, bottles or their contents. The State had a legitimate interest in the prevention of underage drinking. Suspension of a driver's license was a form of deterrence. The fact that the suspension was applicable to persons between eighteen and twenty-one did not render it unconstitutional. They were still subject to restrictions on drinking and were subject to the same sanctions for punishment and deterrence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

132 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Hoffman v. State


Docket No. 29354/29355, 2005 Opinion No. 101


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


142 Idaho 27; 121 P.3d 958; 2005 Ida. LEXIS 143



September 14, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication: October 20, 2005.
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Hoffman, 2009 Ida. App. Unpub. LEXIS 402 (Idaho Ct. App., Dec. 1, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Owyhee County. Hon. Gregory M. Culet, District Judge.
State v. Hoffman, 123 Idaho 638, 851 P.2d 934, 1993 Ida. LEXIS 51 (Idaho, 1993)



DISPOSITION: The State's motion to dismiss this appeal from the decision of the district court dismissing Petitioner's Second Petition for Post-Conviction Relief is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Third Judicial District, Owyhee County, Idaho, convicted defendant of first-degree murder and received a death sentence in 1989. The district court dismissed defendant's second petition for post-conviction relief or writ of habeas corpus and a motion to correct illegal sentence. The State motioned to dismiss the appeal. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his sentence of death had to be set aside because the aggravating factors found to support the imposition of the death penalty were found by a judge, not by a jury. Defendant also argued that Ring applied retroactively because it presented a watershed rule and procedures that were so fundamental as to be guaranteed and implicit to the concept of ordered liberty. The supreme court found that the United States Supreme Court held that Ring announced a new procedural rule that did not apply retroactively to cases already final on direct review. Ring had no applicability to defendant's case. Although defendant argued that the Idaho Supreme Court should follow the lead of the Indiana Supreme Court, the supreme court noted that it had confidence in the ability of district judges to carefully and fairly weigh the facts relating to the imposition of the death penalty. The prior process was not unfair or suspect and the supreme court would not set aside the properly imposed sentence of death in defendant's case.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the State's motion to dismiss the appeal was granted.

 

133 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Gallagher v. State


Docket No. 30685, 2005 Opinion No. 83


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


141 Idaho 665; 115 P.3d 756; 2005 Ida. LEXIS 111



June 24, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication: July 20, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Kathryn A. Sticklen, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: District court's judgment and order dismissing plaintiff's case, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a citizen, sued for declaratory judgment and injunctive relief requesting that the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County, find legislation allowing for a one percent sales and use tax and an increase to the cigarette tax unconstitutional. The citizen ultimately moved for summary judgment and class certification but the trial court granted defendant State's motion to dismiss. The citizen appealed.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court noted that taxpayers who had a generalized grievance shared by a large class of citizens did not have standing. In such case, a taxpayer's remedy was through the political process. Thus, the supreme court held the citizen lacked standing to challenge the tax. The supreme court also rejected the citizen's argument that the bill creating the additional revenue arose in the Idaho Senate, and therefore violated Idaho Const. art. III, § 14. To the contrary, the House introduced the sales and use tax bill. Further, art. III, § 14 did not prohibit the Senate from denying passage of a revenue bill, and it did not specifically prohibit the Senate from amending a revenue bill. In sum, the Senate made amendments and the House approved. Thus, the sales and use tax was constitutionally enacted. Finally, the citizen failed to provide any authority to support his claim the district court erred in imposing sanctions against him, thereby waiving that issue on appeal, and the supreme court found that although the law was well settled that the Senate could amend a revenue bill, the appeal was not frivolous, so as to have justified an award of attorney fees for the State.


OUTCOME: The supreme court held that the citizen lacked standing to challenge the cigarette tax and that the sales and use tax bill was constitutionally enacted. Costs on appeal were awarded to the State.

A & B Irrigation Dist. v. Aberdeen-American Falls Ground Water Dist. (In re SRBA Case No. 39576)


Docket No. 29942, 2005 Opinion No. 77


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


141 Idaho 746; 118 P.3d 78; 2005 Ida. LEXIS 106



June 21, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication: August 23, 2005.
Rehearing denied by A & B Irrigation Dist. v. Aberdeen-American Falls Ground Water, 2005 Ida. LEXIS 139 (Idaho, Aug. 16, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Snake River Basin Adjudication Court of the Fifth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Twin Falls County. Hon. Roger S. Burdick, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant irrigation district challenged a decision from Snake River Basin Adjudication Court of the Fifth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Twin Falls County, which affirmed a special master's decision to award partial summary judgment in favor of respondents, the State of Idaho and several ground water users, in a case involving water enlargement claims.


OVERVIEW: The irrigation district filed five claims seeking to enlarge its water rights. It sought amnesty under Idaho Code § 42-1426 (2003). After partial summary judgment was granted, the irrigation district sought review. In affirming, the court determined that the district's position failed whether or not the water in question was treated as recaptured drain/waste water or ground water. The evidence showed that the ground water was collected in drains and commingled with other diffuse sources such as rain. If the district was relying on an unappropriated source for the expansion, it did not qualify for amnesty under § 42-1426. Even if the water was treated as ground water, § 42-1426(2) required subordination to those priority rights established before April 12, 1994. Next, the court held that the district did not qualify for the rebuttable presumption established by Idaho Code § 42-1416 (repealed) because the enlargement would have caused a per se injury to the rights of junior appropriators. The ground water users did not waive their right to object because they filed a recommendation instead of an objection. Finally, attorney fees were not warranted as a sanction.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed. Costs were awarded, but no attorney fees were allowed.

 

135 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Venters v. Sorrento Del., Inc.


Docket No. 29854, Docket No. 29139, 2005 Opinion No. 31


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


141 Idaho 245; 108 P.3d 392; 2005 Ida. LEXIS 35



February 23, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication: March 17, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Canyon County. Hon. Dennis E. Goff (No. 29139) & Hon. Renae J. Hoff (No. 29854), District Judges, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant survivors, a decedent's widow and son, challenged summary judgments of the District Court of the Third Judicial District, Canyon County (Idaho), which dismissed the survivors' wrongful death actions that were brought separately against respondents, a cheese factory and a local farm, after the decedent was killed in a work-related accident.


OVERVIEW: The factory contracted with the decedent's employer to haul wastewater from its facility. The farm entered into a written agreement with the factory to permit it to build a wastewater facility and to truck wastewater onto its farm site for dispersal. The decedent was killed while waiting to dump a load of wastewater at the farm site. While the trial court erred in finding that the farm, as a mere landowner, was the decedent's statutory employer, its grant of summary judgment was affirmed by the court on the alternate basis that the survivors failed to create a material issue of fact for trial that the farm breached any applicable duty of care, or how that breach proximately caused injury. The work being done was the work of hauling wastewater. Nothing indicated that the farm was engaged in the business of hauling water for pecuniary gain. Thus, the farm was not a statutory employer. Summary judgment was proper as to the factory because it qualified as the decedent's statutory employer under Idaho Code § 72-223 due to its contractual relationship with the decedent's employer. Thus, the factory was immune from third-party tort liability under the Idaho Worker's Compensation Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgments.

BHA Invs., Inc. v. City of Boise


Docket Nos. 30004 & 30409, 2005 Opinion No. 24


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


141 Idaho 168; 108 P.3d 315; 2005 Ida. LEXIS 25



February 18, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 14, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Ada County. Hon. Ronald J. Wilper and Darla S. Williamson, District Judges.
BHA Invs., Inc. v. City of Boise, 138 Idaho 356, 63 P.3d 482, 2003 Ida. LEXIS 18 (Idaho, 2003)



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court in Case No. 30004 is affirmed; the judgment of the district court in Case No. 30409 is affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an investment company and two entertainment companies, in a consolidated appeal, challenged decisions of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Ada County, which declined to certify the investment company's action as a class action and, in the entertainment companies' action, held that defendant city was not required to refund an illegally imposed fee.


OVERVIEW: Both cases stemmed from plaintiffs paying liquor license transfer fees to the city. The district court held that 17 members was not a sufficient number to be considered numerous for class action purposes under Idaho R. Civ. P. 23(a), (b). The court held that the district court did not abuse its discretion in that holding. The court held that the city's exaction of a liquor license transfer fee could constitute the taking of property without just compensation where the city had no authority to charge a transfer fee. Further, the court's decision in a previous case holding that the city's ordinance imposing a liquor license transfer fee was invalid applied retroactively to the current case. The court also held that because the entertainment companies' notice of claim did not include the name and address of the entertainment companies, their claims under state law were barred, but that the notice of claim requirements of Idaho Code § 50-219 did not apply to their federal claims. Also, because the sum owing was a transfer fee and not a tax, the district court erred in holding that the entertainment companies were required to have paid the fee under protest in order to bring the action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment regarding the investment company and the class action. The court affirmed that part of the judgment in the entertainment companies' action dismissing the state law claims and vacated that portion of the judgment dismissing the claim based upon federal law.

Owsley v. Idaho Indus. Comm'n


Docket No. 30193, 2005 Opinion No. 15


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


141 Idaho 129; 106 P.3d 455; 2005 Ida. LEXIS 18



January 31, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 22, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District, State of Idaho, Bonner County. Hon. Fred M. Gibler, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the First Judicial District, Bonner County, Idaho, dismissed appellant workers' suit against appellees, Idaho Industrial Commission (commission) and the Idaho Special Indemnity Fund (ISIF), alleging bias, prejudgment, and due process violations in the adjudication of their claims. The workers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The district court found that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction to hear the action. The appellate court found, however, that it was not an action between workers and employers. In addition to naming the ISIF, the workers brought suit against the commission itself. An action by a worker against an entity besides a surety or an employer did not generally fall within the purview of the commission. The appellate court treated the dismissal as coming under Idaho R. Civ. P. 12(b)(1). In order to avoid dismissal, the workers had to assert an exception to the exhaustion requirement that applied. The workers advanced factual assertions by which the appellate court could infer bias or prejudgment. However, the workers' specific facts did not rise to the level necessary to infer bias or prejudgment on the part of the commission. Without some preliminary inquiry into the merits of the claim, the commission could not properly judge whether an injured worker was surrendering a strong claim for too small a settlement, or whether the ISIF was satisfying spurious claims at great cost. The issues raised by the workers were not frivolous, and therefore no award of attorney fees was warranted.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed as to the district court's judgment that it did not have jurisdiction to decide claims such as those brought by the workers; the judgment was affirmed as to the dismissal of the action for failure to exhaust administrative remedies.

E. Idaho Reg'l Med. Ctr. v. Minidoka County (In re Bermudes)


Docket No. 29993, 2005 Opinion No. 11


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


141 Idaho 157; 106 P.3d 1123; 2005 Ida. LEXIS 17



January 28, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 22, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Minidoka County. Hon. John M. Melanson, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Fifth Judicial District, Minidoka County, Idaho, denied appellant medical center's request to have appellee county pay for emergency medical services performed on an indigent patient at the medical center. The medical center appealed.


OVERVIEW: The medical center argued that the statutory definition of "resident" within the medical indigency statutes was vague and did not provide a clear meaning of what constituted "temporary purposes." The appellate court noted that Idaho Code § 31-3502(12) was not vague or uncertain. Neither party disputed the fact that the patient lived in the county for at least 30 days prior to being treated at the center and he was engaged in seasonal labor and intended to leave Idaho after the 2002 farm season. The county correctly determined that he was not a resident for the purposes of the medical indigency statutes. The statute did not violate equal protection where the payment of medical indigency benefits only to persons who were physically present in Idaho for at least 30 days and intended to remain or did not intend to move elsewhere was rationally related to the legitimate state interest of allocating limited funds. The appellate court declined to award attorney fees to either party.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

139 of 368 DOCUMENTS


State v. Stover


Docket No. 30313, 2005 Opinion No. 1


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


140 Idaho 927; 104 P.3d 969; 2005 Ida. LEXIS 1



January 6, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 28, 1005.
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Stover, 2016 Ida. App. Unpub. LEXIS 185 (Idaho Ct. App., Apr. 12, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Deborah A. Bail, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho that imposed concurrent unified prison sentences of 30 years, with 10 years fixed, on two counts of lewd conduct with a minor under 16 years of age against separate victims, and that denied defendant's request for probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that Idaho's sentencing scheme was unconstitutional because it violated his right to a jury trial pursuant to Blakely v. Washington, 124 S. Ct. 2531 (2004), which required that any fact, other than a prior conviction, that increased the penalty for a crime beyond the prescribed statutory maximum must be submitted to a jury, and proved beyond a reasonable doubt. Defendant also claimed that the trial court abused its discretion by imposing concurrent sentences of 30 years with 10 years fixed. The court held that Idaho's sentencing scheme was unaffected by the holding in Blakely because it was an indeterminate sentencing system in which a defendant was given a sentence with a minimum and a maximum. The court noted that there was nothing in Idaho Code § 19-2521 that extended the maximum penalty for defendant's crime. The court also found that defendant failed to show his constitutional rights were violated because the jury and not a judge found him guilty of the two counts of lewd conduct and found him to be a multiple offender. Also imprisonment was appropriate for a multiple offender under § 19-2521(f). The court held that the imposed sentence was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment that sentenced defendant to imprisonment and denied his request for probation.

Dire v. Dire-Blodgett


Docket No. 30060, 2004 Opinion No. 114


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


140 Idaho 777; 102 P.3d 1096; 2004 Ida. LEXIS 186



October 28, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 20, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Dire v. Dire-Blodgett, 2004 Ida. LEXIS 228 (Idaho, Dec. 20, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Bonner County. The Hon. Steven C. Verby, District Judge and the Hon. Debra A. Heise, Magistrate Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the magistrate judge affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sought review of an order from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Bonner County, which upheld a magistrate's award of summary judgment to defendant in a divorce action. Defendant moved for attorney fees on appeal.


OVERVIEW: The parties, who were cohabiting, participated in a wedding ceremony officiated by an acquaintance, who allegedly represented to them that he was a minister. The parties intentionally did not obtain a marriage license prior to the ceremony. Plaintiff later filed an action against defendant for divorce. Defendant filed an answer that denied the existence of the alleged marriage. Defendant moved for summary judgment on the ground that the parties did not have a valid marriage. The trial court upheld a magistrate's decision to grant the motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court held that the Idaho Legislature clearly required a license in order to have a valid marriage. Both the issuance of a license and solemnization were required. Because the parties chose not to obtain a marriage license, their purported marriage violated the provisions of Idaho Code § 32-201(1) (1996). Because they were never married, plaintiff's divorce action was correctly dismissed. Finally, the court held that defendant was entitled to an award of attorney fees on appeal pursuant to Idaho Code § 12-121.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court. The court granted defendant's motion for attorney fees.

 

141 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Porter v. State


Docket No. 29559, 2004 Opinion No. 115


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


140 Idaho 780; 102 P.3d 1099; 2004 Ida. LEXIS 185



October 28, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 20, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Porter v. State, 2004 Ida. LEXIS 229 (Idaho, Dec. 20, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Porter v. Idaho, 125 S. Ct. 2967, 162 L. Ed. 2d 894, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 5097 (U.S., June 27, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Lewis County. The Hon. John H. Bradbury, District Judge.
State v. Porter, 130 Idaho 772, 948 P.2d 127, 1997 Ida. LEXIS 109 (Idaho, 1997)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Second Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Lewis County, granted defendant post-conviction relief based upon the retroactive application of a United States Supreme Court decision. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The district court reasoned that first-degree murder was a lesser-included offense of capital first-degree murder and that because defendant had been tried and found guilty of by a jury of first-degree murder, he could only be resentenced for that offense. Defendant asked that the appellate court apply a more lenient standard of retroactivity. However, the appellate court noted that the retroactivity of the decision was a matter of federal law, not state law. Defendant had no right under either the Idaho or Federal Constitutions to have the jury find the existence of an aggravating circumstance. Because there was no error, habeas corpus did not provide a remedy. Idaho Code § 19-2515 did not define a separate crime of capital first-degree murder. It merely set forth the procedures that had to be followed in order to impose a death sentence. The United States Supreme Court's decision in Ring did not elevate those statutory aggravating circumstances into elements of a crime, nor did it create a new crime. Because Ring simply established a new procedural rule for the imposition of the death penalty that was not retroactive, Ring had no application to defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

Regan v. Kootenai County


Docket No. 29737, 2004 Opinion No. 111


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


140 Idaho 721; 100 P.3d 615; 2004 Ida. LEXIS 180



October 20, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 12, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho for Kootenai County. Hon. Charles W. Hosack, District Judge.
Regan v. Kootenai County, 2004 Ida. LEXIS 129 (Idaho, July 1, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Vacated and the case is remanded to the district court to dismiss the claim for declaratory relief.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners filed a declaratory judgment action to obtain an interpretation of an ordinance regarding the use of a private, noncommercial airstrip. The District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho for Kootenai County granted summary judgment in favor of respondent Kootenai County and issued a permanent injunction against the landowners' use. They appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landowners possessed a parcel of land consisting of approximately 175 acres located in the agricultural suburban zone of Kootenai County, Idaho. A planning director with the Kootenai County Planning Department sent the landowners a letter informing them that their private airstrip was prohibited. According to Kootenai County, Idaho, Zoning Ordinance No. 271, the use of a private noncommercial airfield was neither a permitted nor conditional use of the property. In their complaint for declaratory relief, the landowners sought a determination of whether or not their private landing field and hangar were permissible or impermissible use under the Kootenai County Ordinance. The landowners' failure to exhaust their administrative remedies deprived the district court of subject matter jurisdiction over their claim for declaratory relief. The landowners had the following options for seeking redress of the planning director's interpretation of the ordinance: apply for a text amendment to the ordinance, or zone change and conditional use permit.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the district court to dismiss the claim for declaratory relief. The decision of the district court on the landowners' claim for declaratory relief was vacated, and the case was remanded with instructions to enter an order dismissing their claim. The permanent injunction remained in effect.

Idaho Schs. for Equal Educ. Opportunity v. State


Docket No. 29616, 2004 Opinion No. 105


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


140 Idaho 586; 97 P.3d 453; 2004 Ida. LEXIS 166



August 25, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at Idaho Schs. for Equal Educ. Opportunity, 2005 Ida. LEXIS 189 (Idaho, Dec. 21, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Deborah A. Bail, District Judge. Appeal from a district court decision finding certain statutory provisions unconstitutional.
Idaho Schs. for Equal Educ. Opportunity v. State, 132 Idaho 559, 976 P.2d 913, 1998 Ida. LEXIS 147 (Idaho, 1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State of Idaho appealed a decision of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, which found House Bill 403 of the 2003 Idaho legislative session (HB 403) unconstitutional. Plaintiffs, a group of school districts and parents, brought suit against the State, alleging violations of Idaho Const. art. IX, § 1.


OVERVIEW: The group filed the action over 10 years ago, alleging that the public school funding system failed to provide necessary funding, and the legislature enacted HB 403 in an effort to resolve the lawsuit. The legislation established that the group and the State sue individual school districts and the venues would be changed to the judicial districts of the school district. The court held that the group had standing, as the State did not have power legislatively to remove the group as a party by revoking its standing. The court held that the language of the bill was aimed at essentially disbanding the group's case and restructuring it in a manner that destroyed the group's cause of action, and it was clearly a special law, in violation of Idaho Const. art. III, § 9. Further, Idaho Code § 6-2215(3), as amended by HB 403, directly contradicted Idaho court procedure and effectively dismissed parties to a pending lawsuit without any court action, and, because Idaho Code. § 6-2214, as amended by HB 403, assigned the power to tax to the judiciary, it violated the Idaho Constitution. Therefore, that part of HB 403 that amended Idaho Code §§ 6-2215(3) and 6-2214 was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the district court.

Moon v. N. Idaho Farmers Ass'n


Docket Nos. 29896, 29897, 29898, 29899, 29900, 29901, 2004 Opinion No. 103


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


140 Idaho 536; 96 P.3d 637; 2004 Ida. LEXIS 160



August 2, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 18, 2004.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Moon v. N. Idaho Farmers Ass'n, 543 U.S. 1146, 161 L. Ed. 2d 106, 125 S. Ct. 1299, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 1471 (U.S., Feb. 22, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District, State of Idaho, Kootenai County. Hon. John Thomas Mitchell, District Judge. The Court upholds the amendments to I.C. § 22-4801 et seq., as constitutional according to the Idaho and United States Constitutions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff individuals asserted claims of nuisance and trespass against defendant seed growers. After the enactment of Idaho Code § 22-4801 et seq., the individuals requested that the district court declare the statute unconstitutional. The District Court of the First Judicial District, State of Idaho, Kootenai County, held that the statute was unconstitutional. The seed growers moved for permissive appeal, and the motion was granted.


OVERVIEW: At issue on appeal was whether the district court erred in finding HB 391, 2003 Leg. (Idaho 2003), Idaho Code § 22-4801 et seq. (amended 2003), was an unconstitutional taking; whether the legislation was an unconstitutional limitation that was not in the interests of the common welfare; and whether the district court erred in finding that HB 391 was a local or special law. The taking asserted was in the nature of a regulatory taking, but the landowners did not claim a permanent deprivation of all economically beneficial uses of their land. The provision of Idaho Code § 22-4806A(6) granting immunity to the grass farmers did not represent an unconstitutional taking. Because there clearly were some interests of the common welfare being protected by the legislature's action in allowing field burning, the supreme court could not say that the landowners met their burden to show no conceivable constitutional application for this legislation. Despite some particularized references to the 10 northern counties, including the imposition of stricter requirements on North Idaho counties, the statute applied to all counties. The statute was not a local and a special law.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the district court's conclusion.

Regan v. Kootenai County


Docket No. 29737


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


2004 Ida. LEXIS 129



July 1, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:

THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Rehearing denied by Regan v. Kootenai County, 2004 Ida. LEXIS 182 (Idaho, Oct. 20, 2004)
Substituted opinion at, Remanded by Regan v. Kootenai County, 2004 Ida. LEXIS 180 (Idaho, Oct. 20, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho for Kootenai County. Hon. Charles W. Hosack, District Judge. 2004 Opinion No. 78.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners filed a declaratory judgment action to obtain an interpretation of an ordinance regarding the use of their private noncommercial airstrip. The District Court of the First Judicial District, Kootenai County, Idaho, granted summary judgment in favor of the County and issued a permanent injunction prohibiting the landowners from taking off or landing aircraft on their property. The landowners appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the landowners challenged the trial court's order entering a permanent injunction enjoining them from using their airstrip. The supreme court found that the landowners failed to exhaust their administrative remedies, as the County hearing examiner was designated as the decision maker for appeals concerning issues of interpretation. The landowners failed to demonstrate that justice required relaxation of the exhaustion rule or that the County acted outside its authority. Thus, the general rule of exhaustion of administrative remedies applied. As the landowners' complaint sought declaratory relief from the planning director's interpretation of the zoning ordinance, this issue should have been pursued before the county zoning authorities under the procedures of the county's administrative appeal ordinance and not by the trial court through declaratory relief. Thus, the landowners' failure to exhaust their administrative remedies deprived the trial court of subject matter jurisdiction over their claim for declaratory relief.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was vacated, and the case was remanded with instructions to enter an order dismissing the landowners' claim for declaratory relief.

State v. Doe


Docket No. 29237, 2004 Opinion No. 69.


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


140 Idaho 271; 92 P.3d 521; 2004 Ida. LEXIS 101



May 25, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 16, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho for Ada County. Hon. D Duff McKee, District Judge; Hon. John Vehlow Magistrate Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for entry of an order dismissing the charge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile was charged with disrupting the educational process, pursuant to Idaho Code § 33-512(11). Defendant's motion to dismiss was denied by the magistrate court, and the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County, affirmed. Defendant appealed, challenging the constitutionality of § 33-512(11) on the basis of over-breadth and vagueness.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a 10-year-old elementary student. He stood up in class and asked his teacher for a shotgun, stating that he wanted to shoot another boy. He was immediately removed from the classroom and interrogated by the police. He was subsequently charged with a violation of Idaho Code § 33-512(11), which made it a misdemeanor offense for a person, among other things, to disrupt "the educational process." The Idaho Supreme Court declined to determine the constitutionality of the statute, finding that same was unnecessary for a determination of the case. However, the supreme court concluded that the language of § 33-512(11) evidenced a legislative purpose of protecting, not prosecuting, pupils. Idaho Code § 33-512(6) already granted the board of trustees of each school district specific powers and duties to prescribe rules for the disciplining of unruly or insubordinate pupils. The supreme court held that an interpretation of Idaho Code § 33-512(11) that criminalized student misconduct was not necessary to carry out its purpose or to avoid rendering the statute a nullity. The supreme court further held that § 33-512(11) was not intended to criminalize student misconduct.


OUTCOME: The magistrate's order denying defendant's motion to dismiss was reversed. The case was remanded for entry of an order dismissing the charge.

 

147 of 368 DOCUMENTS


State v. Morton


Docket No. 29698, 2004 Opinion No. 65


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


140 Idaho 235; 91 P.3d 1139; 2004 Ida. LEXIS 99



May 21, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 14, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District, State of Idaho, Kootenai County. Hon. John T. Mitchell, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with possession of sexually exploitative material for other than a commercial purpose under Idaho Code §§ 18-1507 & 18-1507A. The District Court of the First Judicial District (Idaho) denied defendant's motion to dismiss on First Amendment grounds, in which he alleged that the statutes were overbroad. Defendant entered a conditional guilty plea pursuant to Idaho Crim. R. 11(a)(2), and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that §§ 18-1507A & 18-1507, specifically, the definition of "erotic nudity" in § 18-1507(2)(e), were unconstitutionally overbroad in violation of the First Amendment because they criminalized an intolerable range of constitutionally protected conduct by seeking to prohibit possession based upon the thoughts of the possessor. The Supreme Court of Idaho held that § 18-1507(2)(e) was not unconstitutionally overbroad, because it withstood analysis under Ferber and Osborne. First, it limited its reach to works that visually depicted sexual conduct by children below a certain age. The statute limited its scope in § 18-1507(2)(b) & (c) to "sexually exploitative material" such as photographs or videotapes depicting a child under the age of 18. Second, it suitably limited the category of "sexual conduct" proscribed. By limiting the prohibition of such "displays" to material made "for the purpose of overt sexual gratification or stimulation of one or more of the persons involved," the statute simultaneously targeted child pornography, which was not protected speech, and reduced the possibility that the statute would be used to prohibit protected speech.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Purco Fleet Servs. v. Idaho State Dep't of Fin.


Docket No. 29668, 2004 Opinion No. 56


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


140 Idaho 121; 90 P.3d 346; 2004 Ida. LEXIS 85



April 29, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 21, 2004


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. D. Duff McKee, District Judge. The Court reverses the district court and affirms and reinstates the Department of Finance's cease and desist order entered against PurCo.



DISPOSITION: District court's order reversed; Director's cease and desist order affirmed and reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County, Idaho, set aside an administrative cease and desist order issued by appellant Director of the Department of Finance, requiring appellee corporation to cease engaging in collection activity in Idaho without a permit under the Idaho Collection Agency Act, Idaho Code § 26-2221 (2000). The director appealed.


OVERVIEW: The director argued that the corporation had operated a collection agency, in Idaho in violation of the Idaho Collection Agency Act (Act), Idaho Code § 26-2221 (2000), and thus properly issued the cease and desist order. The appellate court found that Idaho had personal jurisdiction over the corporation, which failed to meet its burden of proving unconstitutional selective enforcement to establish impermissible activity by a state agency. No substantial rights were prejudiced by the director's decision. The rental vehicle damage claim, which the corporation collected against the Idaho resident, constituted a claim or other indebtedness within the meaning of Idaho Code § 26-2223(2). According to the corporation's agreement, monies collected were to be placed in a trust account, from which the corporation disbursed the appropriate sums to the car rental agency after retaining a percentage of monies collected. The assignment created between the corporation and the agency was for the purpose of collection. The corporation collected on the agency's behalf, in violation of the Act. Because the case was of first impression, the director's request for attorney fees was denied.


OUTCOME: The director's cease and desist order was affirmed and reinstated.

 

149 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Nampa Charter Sch., Inc. v. Delapaz


Docket No. 29451, 2004 Opinion No. 45


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


140 Idaho 23; 89 P.3d 863; 2004 Ida. LEXIS 71



April 23, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 17, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Canyon County. Hon. James C. Morfitt, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court dismissing the case for failure to state a cause of action is: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant charter school sought an injunction against appellee parent in the District Court of the Third Judicial District, Canyon County, Idaho, alleging libel, slander, and tortious interference. The trial court dismissed the matter pursuant to Idaho R. Civ., P. 12(b) and awarded the parent 20 percent of the attorney fees she requested. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the parent was fired from her position with the charter school in which her child was enrolled, the parent began writing letters criticizing the charter school's special education program. The charter school responded by filing its lawsuit. The trial court held that because the charter school was a governmental entity, it could not maintain an action for libel and slander against an individual. The trial court further held that the charter school failed to provide any Idaho statute or case law supporting a cause of action in tort for interference with an entity's responsibilities under state statutes. The appellate court noted that because a governmental entity could not maintain a libel and slander claim against a person whose speech was protected, dismissal of the libel and slander claim was appropriate because an injunction on speech critical of a public official was an impermissible prior restraint. The appellate court held that a charter school's claim that a parent tortiously interfered with its responsibilities under the Idaho Public Charter Schools Act was a non-existent cause of action and unsupported by the common law, Idaho statutes, or Idaho case law.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Haw v. Idaho State Bd. of Med.


Docket No. 29566, 2004 Opinion No. 42


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


140 Idaho 152; 90 P.3d 902; 2004 Ida. LEXIS 63



April 22, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 14, 2004.
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Haw v. State Bd. of Med., 2006 Ida. LEXIS 88 (Idaho, May 30, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Ada County. Hon. D. Duff McKee, Senior District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Board's order permanently vacating physician's license to practice medicine in Idaho affirmed, imposition of $ 20,000 in fines reversed, award of costs and attorney fees vacated; case remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County (Idaho), affirmed cross-appellant Idaho Board of Medicine's restriction of appellant physician's license for administering estrogen injections in higher dosages and at greater frequencies than permitted by the standard of health care, but it vacated the Board's imposition of fines and assessment of costs and attorney fees. The physician appealed and the Board cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The physician did not challenge the Board's authority to permanently restrict his license. The physician contended that he was denied due process by the Board's failure to promulgate regulations setting forth clearly defined standards with respect to the use of injectable hormones. The Supreme Court of Idaho held that one of the purposes of the Medical Practice Act, Idaho Code § 54-1814, was to assure the public health, safety and welfare, and consistent with that purpose the Board could discipline the physician for providing health care that failed to meet the applicable standard of care even if it could not prove that his patients had suffered any physical harm. The Board found credible the expert physicians it called to testify who appeared to be representative of the community. The Board's findings as to the standard of care were supported by substantial evidence and were not clearly erroneous. The hearing officer issued a protective order, pursuant to the parties' stipulation, preventing the physician from harassing the expert witnesses who were going to testify. But the Board had no contempt power and thus, had no authority to fine the physician for violating the order.


OUTCOME: The Board's restriction of the physician's license was affirmed, the fines were reversed, the attorney fees and costs were vacated, and the case was remanded.

State v. Poe


Docket No. 28404, 2004 Opinion No. 25


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


139 Idaho 885; 88 P.3d 704; 2004 Ida. LEXIS 38



March 4, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Poe, 2004 Ida. LEXIS 81 (Idaho, Apr. 27, 2004)Released for Publication April 27, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, in and for Kootenai County. The Hon. John P. Luster, District Judge; Hon. Eugene A. Marano, Magistrate Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the trial court of disturbing the peace. The District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Kootenai County, affirmed the conviction on appeal. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Idaho Code § 18-6409 was unconstitutionally vague because it encouraged arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement due to its lack of standards defining when someone's peace was disturbed or what words were vulgar, profane, or indecent. The Supreme Court of Idaho held that the third part of Idaho Code § 18-6409 was unconstitutional, because, as written, it criminalized speech that was protected by the First Amendment. Therefore, the court struck that part of the statute to eliminate overbreadth so that it conformed to the opinions of the United States Supreme Court interpreting the First Amendment. However, the court would not reverse defendant's conviction based solely upon his challenge that the statute was facially overbroad. Because defendant did not allege that the statute was unconstitutionally applied to his conduct or that he did not have fair notice that his conduct was proscribed, and because he did not show any error by the trial court, the court affirmed the judgment of conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Eacret v. Bonner County


Docket No. 28092, Docket No. 29137, 2004 Opinion No. 19


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


139 Idaho 780; 86 P.3d 494; 2004 Ida. LEXIS 31



February 27, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 22, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District, State of Idaho, Bonner County. Hon. James F. Judd, District Judge in # 28092, and Hon. John Thomas Mitchell, District Judge in # 29137.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of an order from the District Court of the First Judicial District, Bonner County (Idaho), which vacated and remanded an order awarding a variance to the property owners in an action filed by respondent neighbors. Appellant county challenged an order awarding costs and attorney fees to the neighbors against the county. The neighbors requested attorney fees on appeal.


OVERVIEW: The property owners applied to the county for a variance from the setback requirements after they had begun construction of a boathouse. The board of county commissioners (board) granted the variance. The neighbors challenged the order granting the variance. The trial court vacated the issuance of the variance and remanded the matter to the board. On remand, the board denied the variance. The trial court awarded the neighbors attorney fees and costs against the county. On appeal, the court found that, based on a board member's ex parte contacts and prehearing statements concerning the boathouse, the trial court properly determined that the neighbors' due process rights were violated. The board member's comments not only created an appearance of impropriety, but also underscored the likelihood that he could not fairly decide the issue in the case. The court further found that the filing of the neighbors' memorandum of costs was not in compliance with Idaho App. R. 40(c), as it was not filed within 14 days from the filing and announcement of the opinion on appeal. As a matter of law, the untimely memorandum barred consideration of the neighbors' request for attorney fees and costs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order vacating and remanding the award of the variance to the property owners. The court vacated the order awarding attorney fees and costs to the neighbors against the county. The court declined to award attorney fees in the appeal.

Merrill v. Gibson


Docket No. 28542, 2004 Opinion No. 20


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


139 Idaho 840; 87 P.3d 949; 2004 Ida. LEXIS 33



February 27, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 12, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Merrill v. Gibson, 2004 Ida. LEXIS 66 (Idaho, Apr. 12, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Gibson v. Merrill, 125 S. Ct. 311, 160 L. Ed. 2d 225, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 6725 (U.S., 2004)
Subsequent appeal at Merrill v. Gibson, 2005 Ida. App. LEXIS 114 (Idaho Ct. App., Dec. 9, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Trial court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. D. Duff McKee, District Judge.
Ada County v. Gibson, 126 Idaho 854, 893 P.2d 801, 1995 Ida. App. LEXIS 18 (Idaho Ct. App., 1995)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the trial court quieting title in plaintiffs is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant debtor sought review of an order from the Trial Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County (Idaho), which denied his disqualification motion and awarded judgment to plaintiff creditors in a quiet title action. The creditors challenged an order denying their request for attorney fees. The creditors sought attorney fees on appeal.


OVERVIEW: The debtor purchased land for the purpose of relocating his nursery. The creditors loaned him money for the purchase. The debtor had the warranty deed issued to the creditors so that they could hold the deed as security for the loan. When the creditors discovered that the taxes on the property would increase, they approached the debtor with an offer to either repurchase the property or continue to lease it at a monthly rate. The creditors rejected the debtor's offer to repay the loan. The creditors brought a quiet title action against the debtor. The trial court quieted title in the creditors. The trial court denied the creditors' motion for attorney fees. On appeal, the court found that the trial court did not err in denying the debtor's motion to disqualify. There was no showing that the trial judge lacked the authority to hear the case. The court further found that the trial court properly weighed the evidence and determined the credibility of the parties. There was substantial and competent evidence to support the decision of the trial court. Finally, the court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it denied the creditors' request for attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying the debtor's disqualification motion. The court affirmed the order awarding judgment to the creditors. The court affirmed the order denying the creditors' request for attorney fees. The court granted the creditors' request for attorney fees on appeal. The court awarded the creditors costs on appeal.

Union Pac. Corp. v. Idaho State Tax Comm'n


Docket No. 29219, 2004 Opinion No. 2


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


139 Idaho 573; 83 P.3d 116; 2004 Ida. LEXIS 2



January 4, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 27, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Cheri C. Copsey, District Judge.
Union Pac. Corp. v. Idaho State Tax Comm'n, 136 Idaho 34, 28 P.3d 375, 2001 Ida. LEXIS 72 (Idaho, 2001)



DISPOSITION: District court determination of an alternate apportionment pursuant to I.C. § 63-3027 to determine that portion of Union Pacific Corporation's taxable business income attributable to Idaho, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged a decision from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County (Idaho), which upheld the application of the alternative apportionment provisions of Idaho Code § 63-3027 in determining the taxpayer's business income attributable to Idaho.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer received a deficiency notice from the Commission. On appeal, a district court determined that the apportionment formula under Idaho Code § 63-3027(i) did not fairly represent how the taxpayer earned its income. The case was later remanded for the application of an alternative apportionment formula. On remand, the district court excluded from the sales factor denominator the taxpayer's sales of accounts receivable. The district court then granted partial summary judgment in favor of the Commission. In affirming, the court determined that the law of the case doctrine applied. Therefore, the court was bound by the finding that the inclusion of accounts receivable owing from freight sales and money received from the sale of those accounts receivable resulted in an improper apportionment. The double-counting of income was an "unusual fact situation" that justified avoidance of the apportionment set forth in § 63-3027. Further, the district court considered all three relevant factors when it determined whether the standard apportionment fairly represented the taxpayer's income. Finally, the court declined to engraft a gross distortion requirement into § 63-3027.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

Garza v. State


Docket No. 29646, 2003 Opinion No. 125


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


139 Idaho 533; 82 P.3d 445; 2003 Ida. LEXIS 183



December 4, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 26, 2003. As Corrected February 3, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho, for Owyhee County. Hon. Gerald L. Weston, District Judge. The case is remanded to the district court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.
Garza v. State, 2003 Ida. App. LEXIS 18 (Idaho Ct. App., Feb. 27, 2003).



DISPOSITION: Dismissal of claims affirmed in part and vacated in part; remanded to district court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed an application for post-conviction relief, but did not respond to the district court's notice of intent to dismiss the application. The district court summarily dismissed some of the inmate's claims pursuant to the decision of the Court of Appeals (Idaho) in Sabin. The inmate appealed. On review, the Court of Appeals overruled its decision in Sabin and vacated the dismissal order. The State petitioned for review.


OVERVIEW: The district court ordered a hearing on the inmate's post-conviction claim of deficiency of counsel, but gave notice of its intent to dismiss all other claims. The inmate failed to timely respond to the notice pursuant to Idaho Code § 19-4906(b). The district court denied the inmate's claim that he received ineffective assistance of counsel and dismissed remaining claims. On review, the Court of Appeals overruled its decision in Sabin v. State, 129 Idaho 257, 923 P.2d 502 (Ct. App. 1996), which held applicants for post-conviction relief who failed to respond to a notice of intent to dismiss waived appellate review. The Supreme Court of Idaho upheld the decision of the Court of Appeals. As for the merits of the inmate's post-conviction claim, the Court held that he waived his right to a presentence investigation report, but that he did not waive the right to make corrections to the psychosexual and social assessment reports. The notice of intent to dismiss the inmate's claim was inadequate, because it did not give the rationale for dismissing the claims.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the district court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion, which could include a notice from the district court of the bases for an intent to dismiss all or part of the application. Dismissal of the inmate's post-conviction claim relating to the lack of a PSI was affirmed. Dismissal on all grounds was vacated.

State v. Lovelace


Docket No. 26927, 2003 Opinion No. 89


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


140 Idaho 53; 90 P.3d 278; 2003 Ida. LEXIS 122



July 23, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected July 23, 2003. As Corrected July 25, 2003.
Rehearing granted by Ohio v. Lovelace, 2003 Ida. LEXIS 176 (Idaho, Nov. 20, 2003)
On rehearing at, Affirmed by, in part, Remanded by State v. Lovelace, 140 Idaho 73, 90 P.3d 298 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District, State of Idaho, Bonner County. Hon. James F. Judd, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed, remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After several hearings, the District Court of the First Judicial District, Bonner County (Idaho) found that defendant was competent to waive assistance of counsel and proceed pro se. Defendant was found guilty of first-degree murder and first-degree kidnapping. Defendant was sentenced to death and appealed. Defendant filed a post-conviction application to proceed pro se, which the court summarily dismissed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Inter alia, defendant asserted that he was denied the right to the effective assistance of counsel because of a conflict of interest that the lower courts were aware of, but into which they failed to make adequate inquiry to protect defendant's due process rights. The Supreme Court of Idaho held that defendant had not been denied the right to effective assistance of counsel, and the exercise of his right to waive counsel was found to have been competent. The district court did not err in conducting the competency reviews or in concluding that defendant had voluntarily, knowingly and intelligently waived his right to counsel. Defendant had not established reversible error in the conduct of the trial, the selection of the jury, or in his contests to the summary dismissal of his postconviction application. However, in compliance with Ring v. Arizona, which rendered unconstitutional a sentencing scheme of that required a trial judge to make the factual findings regarding the existence of aggravating circumstances, defendant had to be resentenced under the newly enacted death penalty statute, Idaho Code § 19-2515, which presented neither a double jeopardy nor an ex post facto problem.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed. The case was remanded for resentencing.

State v. Korsen


Docket No. 28276, 2003 Opinion No. 53


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


138 Idaho 706; 69 P.3d 126; 2003 Ida. LEXIS 71



April 24, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 16, 2003.
Related proceeding at State v. Korsen, 2004 Ida. App. LEXIS 8 (Idaho Ct. App., Jan. 21, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Cheri C. Copsey, District Judge; Hon. Christopher Bieter, Magistrate.



DISPOSITION: Magistrate's order dismissing prosecution for trespass, vacated. Case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged a decision of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County, which affirmed a magistrate's dismissal of trespass charges under Idaho Code § 18-7008(8) against defendant and concluded that the statute was void for vagueness and overbroad. Defendant cross-appealed and claimed that the trial court erred in finding that defendant was not protected under double jeopardy grounds against a retrial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appeared at the state health and welfare department to discuss his child support obligations. When defendant refused to leave after being asked to do so, he was arrested for trespassing. The magistrate dismissed the charge and found that the statute was void for vagueness. Alternatively, the magistrate granted defendant's motion for acquittal under Idaho Crim. R. 29 on the ground that the official who requested defendant to leave did not express an adequate reason for doing so. The trial court agreed that the statute was void for vagueness and further found it to be overbroad. The court reversed on appeal. Because Idaho Code § 18-7008(8) informed the public of the prohibited conduct, the statute gave fair notice of the conduct that was made criminal by the statute, and thus the statute was not void for vagueness. Because the statute did not reach a substantial amount of constitutionally protected conduct, the statute was not overbroad. Because the magistrate's dismissal was based on an erroneous legal conclusion, that the official failed to give defendant a reason why he had to leave, double jeopardy did not bar a retrial on the trespass charge.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the conclusion that the trespass statute was void for vagueness and overbroad. The court vacated the magistrate's dismissal and remanded for further proceedings because double jeopardy did not bar a retrial of defendant.

Waters Garbage v. Shoshone County


Docket No. 27532, 2003 Opinion No. 46


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


138 Idaho 648; 67 P.3d 1260; 2003 Ida. LEXIS 64



April 10, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected June 11, 2003. Released for Publication May 2, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Shoshone County. Hon. James F. Judd, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the district court is vacated and the case is remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the First Judicial District Court, Shoshone County, Idaho, granted summary judgment for appellee county holding Idaho Code § 31-4404(2) authorized it to charge a users fee to county residents who did not use the county solid waste disposal facilities and was constitutional. Appellant contractor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The contractor was a licensed public works contractor engaged in collecting solid waste. The contractor sought a declaratory judgment that Idaho Code § 31-4401(2) did not permit the county to charge a user fee to county residents who did not use the county solid waste disposal facilities. The appellate court determined that the trial court erred in holding that the statute permitted the county to charge fees to the nonusers of the county facilities where the contractor had its own disposal facilities. The appellate court held the county could only charge the contractor or its customers fees if they attempted to deliver waste to a county facility. However, the appellate court found there was not a violation of the Commerce Clause because the county ordinance did not prohibit importing solid waste collected outside the state or higher fees charged to process waste generated outside the state. The appellate court concluded the disposal fees did not violate the Commerce Clause because they subsidized the county transfer station, thereby making out-of-state disposal facilities less able to compete with the county facility.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed insofar as the county did not violate the Commerce Clause; however, the portion of the judgment holding that the statute authorized a county to charge a users fee to nonusers of the county solid waste disposal facilities was reversed.

LU Ranching Co. v. United States (In re Snake River Basin Adjudication Case No. 6)


Docket No. 27599, 2003 Opinion No. 36


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


138 Idaho 606; 67 P.3d 85; 2003 Ida. LEXIS 52



April 3, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected June 3, 2003. Released for Publication April 25, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, for Twin Falls County. Hon. Roger S. Burdick, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decisions of the district court are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant rancher challenged the constitutionality of the notice procedures for interested parties involved in the Snake River Basin Adjudication in the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District, Twin Falls County, Idaho, maintaining that they violated minimum due process requirements. The trial court entered judgment for respondent state. The rancher appealed.


OVERVIEW: The rancher and the United States filed de minimis stock water rights claims to the same basin area. A state investigator prepared a director's report listing all existing water rights claims. The rancher received notice that the report was available for his inspection, but was not informed of any actual conflict to his water claims. Later, the Snake River Basin Adjudication (SRBA) granted the United States its beneficial use claims and reserved water rights claims. The rancher then unsuccessfully sought relief from the judgment on the basis of mistake, inadvertence, surprise, or excusable neglect. The appellate court held there was no doubt that the rancher was aware of the commencement of the SRBA and that action concerning its claimed rights and the rights of others in the region would be adjudicated. The appellate court concluded the rancher was able to recognize the conflicts and get notice of the objections to its water claims once it actually looked at the director's report, but that he simply looked too late; therefore, his difficulties arose from a lack of timely attention, not inadequacy of notice.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.
