162 of 368 DOCUMENTS


MDS Invs., LLC v. State


Docket No. 27778, 2003 Opinion No. 20


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


138 Idaho 456; 65 P.3d 197; 2003 Ida. LEXIS 29



February 26, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 20, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Kathryn A. Sticklen, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of district court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated declaratory judgment actions brought against defendant State and defendant city, plaintiff corporation appealed a judgment of the Fourth Judicial District Court, Ada County, Idaho, which held that video machines owned and operated by the corporation were illegal gambling devices.


OVERVIEW: The corporation argued that the trial court erred in: (1) refusing to reallocate the burden of proof as requested; (2) holding that Idaho Code § 18-3810 (1997) was not unconstitutionally vague; (3) holding that the corporation's video machines were illegal gambling devices; and (4) refusing to rule on whether the video machines would be illegal gambling devices if they were operated in some other manner. The instant court held that the trial court did not err in refusing to require the State to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that the machines were gambling devices or slot machines. These lawsuits were not criminal proceedings, and the machines that were the subject of the lawsuits were not persons. Section 18-3810 was not unconstitutionally vague. The definition of slot machine was sufficiently definite so that people of common intelligence did not have to guess at what a slot machine was. The trial court did not err in concluding that the machines constituted illegal gambling devices or in denying the corporation's request for additional findings regarding whether the machines would be illegal gambling devices if they were operated differently than shown during the trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. Costs on appeal, not including a reasonable attorney fee, were awarded to the State and city.

 

163 of 368 DOCUMENTS


BHA Invs., Inc. v. State


Docket No. 28238, 2003 Opinion No. 12


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


138 Idaho 348; 63 P.3d 474; 2003 Ida. LEXIS 19



January 30, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 21, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, for Ada County. Hon. Joel D. Horton, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court dismissing the complaint of BHA Investments, Inc. is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sued appellee State Alcohol Beverage Control Board (ABC) in the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County, Idaho, alleging a liquor license transfer fee triggered by the sale of its liquor license was unconstitutional tax. The trial court dismissed the case for failure to state a claim. The corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: When the corporation sold its liquor license, it was required to pay a transfer fee equal to 10 percent of the sale price to the state, pursuant to Idaho Code § 23-908(5). The corporation paid the transfer fee under protest and filed suit in trial court against the ABC, arguing that the transfer fee was an unconstitutional tax, a taking without just compensation, and an unjust enrichment for the State. The trial court dismissed the case, finding no claim upon which relief could be granted. The appellate court initially noted the transfer fee at issue was not violative of the uniformity and proportionality constitutional requirements for taxes because those provisions did not apply to liquor licensing or transfer fees. The appellate court held the disputed transfer fee fell within a very broad constitutional power of the State to regulate the traffic of liquor. The appellate court concluded deference was given to the State in its use of the police power regarding a transfer fee, and there was no unconstitutional taking of property under either the Idaho or United States Constitution.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

164 of 368 DOCUMENTS


BHA Invs., Inc. v. City of Boise


Docket No. 28039, 2003 Opinion No. 11


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


138 Idaho 356; 63 P.3d 482; 2003 Ida. LEXIS 18



January 30, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 21, 2003.
Subsequent appeal at BHA Invs., Inc. v. City of Boise, 2005 Ida. LEXIS 25 (Idaho, Feb. 18, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, for Ada County. Hon. Ronald J. Wilper, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court dismissing the case is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County, granted judgment in favor of appellee city by dismissing appellant corporation's suit against the city, arguing that a transfer fee was a disguised tax, an illegal taking, and an unjust enrichment for the city. The corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: Upon selling its liquor license to a third party, the corporation was required to pay a transfer fee to the city equal to 7 1/2 percent of the sale price, pursuant to Boise, Idaho, City Code § 5-05-10. The corporation argued that the city was not specifically authorized by statute to impose a liquor license transfer fee, the fee was a disguised and unconstitutional tax, the fee was an unconstitutional taking of property, and the fee was an unjust enrichment for the city. The appellate court found that Idaho Code § 23-916 provided cities with authority to impose a license fee, not a transfer fee. The statute could not have been drafted to include transfer fees, as they were non-existent when the statute was passed. Cities were not granted the authority by the legislature to impose a transfer fee. The city exceeded its power in collecting the transfer fee.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

165 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. Boundary Sch. Dist. # 101


Docket No. 28629, 2003 Opinion No. 9


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


138 Idaho 331; 63 P.3d 457; 2003 Ida. LEXIS 16



January 28, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 19, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District, State of Idaho, Boundary County. Hon. Charles W. Hosack, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Order of dismissal, reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizens challenged a decision from the District Court of the First Judicial District, Boundary County (Idaho), which granted a motion to dismiss filed by defendants, a school board, county commissioners, a county treasurer, and a bank, in a declaratory action involving an election. The citizens also challenged the denial of their motion for leave to file a bond.


OVERVIEW: A special reserve levy was approved to fund the construction of a new high school. As a result, a lease-purchase agreement was entered into with the bank. The citizens filed a declaratory action seeking the invalidation of the levy. After the citizens failed to file a bond, their action was dismissed. The district court determined that the citizens were required to file the complaint and a bond within 40 days of the contested election. The citizens' motion for leave to file a bond was denied. In reversing, the court determined that two counts of the citizens' action challenged the validity of the lease-purchase agreement between the bank and the school district. It did not challenge the election itself. Therefore, the lack of a cost bond was irrelevant to those counts. The third count of the complaint did challenge the election. However, under Idaho Code § 34-2001A(B), the citizens were permitted to post a bond in a school district election contest at any time after a clerk of court or district judge determined the amount of the bond. Bond filing was not jurisdictional in the sense that the case was subject to dismissal merely for failing to file the bond.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the complaint and the denial of the citizens' motion for leave to file a bond. The case was remanded to the district court for further proceedings.

 

166 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Inama v. Boise County


Docket No. 27595, 2003 Opinion No. 6


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


138 Idaho 324; 63 P.3d 450; 2003 Ida. LEXIS 10



January 24, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 19, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Boise County. Hon. George D. Carey, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the district court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant equipment owner filed an action against appellee county, seeking to recover the value of his front-end loader and other damages. The county filed a motion for summary judgment, seeking to have the action dismissed on the ground that it was immune from liability under Idaho Code § 46-1017. The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Boise County, granted the county's motion. The property owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The governor issued a proclamation declaring a disaster emergency as a result of severe winter storms creating excessive snowfall and ice conditions throughout the county. The county and the owner entered into an agreement to use the owner's dump truck to haul debris from the flooding and mudslides. When the county road superintendent heard that the owner also had a front-end loader, he used it to clear debris. The owner was not present, had not known that his loader was going to be used by the county, and did not consent to that use. The loader was destroyed by a mudslide. The district court held that the county was immune from liability, pursuant to Idaho Code § 46-1017, which was part of the Idaho Disaster Preparedness Act of 1975, Idaho Code § 46-1001 et seq. (1997). The Supreme Court of Idaho held that § 46-1012(3) was clear and unambiguous. Compensation for property damaged, lost, or destroyed could be recovered under the Act only if its use or destruction was ordered by the governor or his representative. Idaho Code § 46-1017 did not limit the scope of immunity to damages compensable under § 46-1012. Therefore, the district court had not erred in dismissing the claim.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed. Costs, but not attorney fees, were awarded on appeal to the county.

 

167 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Noh v. Cenarrusa (in Re Action to Determine Constitutionality of Indian Gaming Initiative)


Docket No. 28590, 2002 Opinion No. 112


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


137 Idaho 798; 53 P.3d 1217; 2002 Ida. LEXIS 143



August 28, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 31, 2002. Released for Publication September 19, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceedings Retained by the Supreme Court of the State of Idaho.



DISPOSITION: Petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an original proceeding, petitioner opponents asserted that an Indian gaming initiative, Idaho Proposition 1, violated the Idaho Constitution's prohibition against gambling, violated notions of equal protection, and extinguished existing debts. The opponents sought an order and or writ prohibiting respondent Idaho Secretary of State from placing the initiative on the November 2002 ballot. Respondents moved to dismiss the petition.


OVERVIEW: The opponents alleged that they would suffer injury because the gambling authorized by the initiative, if adopted, would require additional funding of social services and law enforcement. The instant court noted that the opponents had not alleged an injury in fact. Any injury suffered was speculative. It was not possible to determine the accuracy of the alleged future injuries. Under traditional standards for determining standing, the opponents did not have standing. There was not yet a real controversy because the initiative was simply a proposal and had not become a law. There was no need for adjudication. The case did not meet the elements of the traditional ripeness test. The instant court concluded that there was no justiciable controversy. There was no challenge to the process by which the initiative had been qualified to be on the ballot or that the subject matter was beyond the reach of an initiative. If the initiative passed, there would most certainly be a justiciable controversy. If the initiative failed, there would be nothing to adjudicate. The instant court could not be compelled to decide a case that lacked a justiciable controversy.


OUTCOME: The petition to determine the constitutionality of the initiative was dismissed. Respondents were awarded costs. No attorney fees were allowed.

Concerned Taxpayers v. Kootenai County


Docket No. 27032, 2002 Opinion No. 95


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


137 Idaho 496; 50 P.3d 991; 2002 Ida. LEXIS 112



July 2, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 24, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District, State of Idaho, Kootenai County. Hon. Charles W. Hosack, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers filed a declaratory judgment action against defendants, county and county commissioners (county), to declare the Resort County Local Option Sales or Use Tax Act, Idaho Code §§ 63-2601 through 63-2608 (1996), and Kootenai, Idaho, County Ordinance No. 294 unconstitutional. The District Court of the First Judicial District for Kootenai County (Idaho) rendered summary judgment in favor of the county. All parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: Kootenai, Idaho, County Ordinance No. 294 was authorized by the provisions of Resort County Local Option Sales or Use Tax Act (Act), Idaho Code §§ 63-2601 through 63-2608 (1996). The Act was written in such a way that it benefitted only one county in the entire state. The Idaho Supreme Court found that: (1) the Act was directly contrary to the prohibitions contained in Idaho Const. art. III, § 19 against local and special laws, as it was written to benefit only one county; (2) the populations requirements were the major defining characteristics of the Act and were integral or indispensable to the operation of the Act; thus (3) the population requirements in the Act were not severable, and the entire Act was unconstitutional; and (4) consequently Kootenai, Idaho, County Ordinance No. 293 was null and void.


OUTCOME: The decision of the district court was reversed.

Landis v. Delarosa


Docket No. 26064, 2002 Opinion No. 83


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


137 Idaho 405; 49 P.3d 410; 2002 Ida. LEXIS 100



June 12, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 5, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Canyon County. Hon. Sergio A. Gutierrez, District Judge; Hon. Robert M. Taisey, Magistrate Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, appointed guardians, challenged the judgment of the District Court of the Third Judicial District, Canyon County (Idaho), affirming the decision of the magistrate court, denying their appointment as testamentary guardians of the two children, as against appellees, aunt and uncle of the children.


OVERVIEW: The children's mother executed a will designating the guardians in the event of her death. The magistrate court denied the guardians' request for automatic appointment and held that they had not fulfilled the required qualifications for appointment since they had not alleged that the father of the children was unknown or dead. The supreme court ruled that the guardians failed to establish the conditions of Idaho Code § 15-5-202, in that they failed to demonstrate that the father of the children was dead or had been adjudged incapacitated. The argument that a person was incapacitated simply by being unknown was not supported by the probate code. Furthermore, Idaho Code § 15-5-202 was not unconstitutional. The statute allowed a parent to appoint a testamentary guardian, but placed procedural safeguards to protect the rights of a surviving parent, who would also had the right to control the care and upbringing of his or her children.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Creech v. State


Docket No. 27309, 2002 Opinion No. 73


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


137 Idaho 573; 51 P.3d 387; 2002 Ida. LEXIS 86



June 6, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 1, 2002. Released for Publication August 1, 2002.
Rehearing denied by Creech v. State, 2002 Ida. LEXIS 134 (Idaho, Aug. 1, 2002)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by Creech v. Hardison, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 29439 (D. Idaho, Oct. 14, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Ronald J. Wilper, District Judge.
State v. Creech, 105 Idaho 362, 670 P.2d 463, 1983 Ida. LEXIS 568 (Idaho, 1983)



DISPOSITION: The State's motion to dismiss the appeal was granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate appealed an order of the Fourth Judicial District Court, Ada County, Idaho, dismissing his successive petition for postconviction relief in a capital case. The State moved to dismiss the appeal, pursuant to Idaho Code § 19-2719.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was originally convicted of and sentenced to death for first degree murder after pleading guilty in 1981. The inmate, who had previously filed a petition for postconviction relief, raised five claims in his second petition for postconviction relief. The first three claims involved ineffective assistance of counsel, the fourth related to the constitutionality of the statutory scheme for capital postconviction proceedings, and the fifth challenged the constitutionality of the length of the inmate's confinement. The only issue before the instant court was whether it should dismiss the inmate's appeal based upon the provisions of § 19-2719. The instant court held that the inmate failed to raise the claims in his successive petition within the time specified in § 19-2719 because he had made no showing the claims were not known and could not reasonably have been known at the time he filed his first petition. Therefore, the inmate waived his claims pursuant to the statute.


OUTCOME: The instant court granted the State's motion to dismiss the inmate's appeal.

 

171 of 368 DOCUMENTS


In re Writ of Mandamus And/Or for Writ of Prohibition


Docket No. 28408, 2002 Opinion No. 58


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


140 Idaho 316; 92 P.3d 1063; 2002 Ida. LEXIS 69



May 3, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original proceedings retained by the Supreme Court of the State of Idaho.



DISPOSITION: The request for a writ of prohibition or mandamus is denied and the Petition is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners citizens sought an order directing the respondent Secretary of State to instruct all county clerks to comply with the Term Limits Act that was repealed by the legislature.


OVERVIEW: In 1994, the Term Limit Act was passed by the Idaho voters. Subsequently, the Idaho legislature passed legislation that repealed the Term Limits Act. In the body of the law, the legislature declared that an emergency existed so that the repeal would become effective on February 1, 2002, rather than July 1, 2002. The court held that the case was ripe and appropriate for judicial review, as it impacted the primary election that was coming up shortly, and a decision by the court would allow the electoral process to proceed with certainty. The citizens had standing to bring the case, as one of the citizens was running against an opponent who would be ineligible for office, if the repeal of the Term Limits Act was unconstitutional. While the legislature could not violate the right of the people to propose laws and enact them at the polls, it had the legislative right to repeal an initiative, which once enacted, was treated as other ordinary legislative measures. The court also held that the legislature's determination of an emergency in an act was a policy decision exclusively within the ambit of legislative authority, and the judiciary could not second-guess that decision.


OUTCOME: The request for a writ of prohibition or mandamus was denied, and the petition was dismissed.

Bingham County v. Idaho Comm'n for Reapportionament (in Re Petition Challenging Legislative Redistricting)


Docket Nos. 28153/28197, 2002 Opinion No. 30


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


137 Idaho 870; 55 P.3d 863; 2002 Ida. LEXIS 35



March 1, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 25, 2002. As Corrected March 5, 2002.
Judgment entered by Bingham County v. Idaho Comm'n for Reapportionment (In re Petition Challenging Legislative Redistricting), 2002 Ida. LEXIS 138 (Idaho, Mar. 25, 2002)
Related proceeding at In re Alternative Writ of Prohibition Challenging the Idaho Legislative Reapportionment Plan of 2002 v. Ysursa, 2005 Ida. LEXIS 193 (Idaho, Dec. 28, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Original proceedings retained by the Supreme Court of the State of Idaho.
Smith v. Idaho Comm'n on Redistricting (In re Petition to Enjoin Implementation of the Redistricting Plan), 136 Idaho 542, 38 P.3d 121, 2001 Ida. LEXIS 140 (Idaho, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Petition challenging legislative redistricting plan granted; plan found to violate state constitution..


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The petitioners counties filed a petition opposing a redistricting plan created by the respondent Idaho Commission for Reapportionment.


OVERVIEW: The counties argued, inter alia, that the plan violated the state constitution. The supreme court agreed. The plan contained a population deviation of 11.79 percent, well above a prima facie showing of a violation of equal protection standards. The commission justified that deviation on the basis that it occurred as the result of an advancement of rational state policies, particularly maintenance of the integrity of political subdivisions. Idaho Const. art. III, § 5 prohibited the division of counties, except to meet the constitutional standards of equal protection. The prohibition was honored by the commission with respect to Madison and Fremont counties, but was not honored as to Bingham and Bannock counties. In those instances, the idea of joining communities of interest prevailed over the requirement of maintaining county integrity. The basis for justifying the population deviation in the plan was not consistent with other decisions made by the commission that did not honor the integrity of political subdivisions. Therefore, the commission was directed to reconvene to adopt a redistricting plan that was consistent with constitutional standards.


OUTCOME: The petition was granted.

Elec. Wholesale Supply Co. v. Nielson


Docket No. 25807, 2001 Opinion No. 113


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


136 Idaho 814; 41 P.3d 242; 2001 Ida. LEXIS 149



December 31, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 19, 2002. Released for Publication February 15, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bonneville County. Hon. Ted V. Wood, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff supplied electrical materials to defendant subcontractor, who had been hired by defendant general contractor. Because of unpaid credit and purchases, the supplier filed to foreclose its claim of lien and named, inter alia, the general contractor and sub-contractor. The District Court of the Seventh Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Bonneville, imposed liens on the general contractor. The general contractor, inter alia, appealed.


OVERVIEW: The subcontractor had an account with the supplier with an outstanding balance before he began the project. The general contractor disputed the district court's findings regarding what materials were provided to the project, contending that because the subcontractor signed the invoices after the date that the district court determined he was no longer working on the project, those invoices could not be included in the supplier's award. The Supreme Court of Idaho held that there was substantial and competent evidence to support the district court's findings regarding which materials were provided by the supplier to the project. Therefore, they were properly included in the lien amount. Although the district court concluded that the subcontractor's testimony was unreliable, the district court had testimony from the contractor he had hired, who did most of the work on the project, and the correlation between the invoices submitted by the supplier, the bills submitted from the subcontractor to the general contractor, and the payments made by the general contractor to support the decision. That provided substantial and competent evidence.


OUTCOME: The decision of the district court was affirmed.

Rudeen v. Cenarrusa


Docket No. 26975/26976, 2001 Opinion No. 99


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


136 Idaho 560; 38 P.3d 598; 2001 Ida. LEXIS 147



December 13, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 4, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Sixth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Power County. Hon. N. Randy Smith, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The plaintiffs, county officials, mayors and school district trustees filed suit in the Power County District Court (Idaho) against the defendants, county, city and school district clerks. The complaint alleged that Idaho Code §§ 34-907(e)(f), 33-443, and 50-478 violated the state and federal constitutions. The court granted summary judgment for the plaintiffs, and allowed intervention by a citizens' term limit group. The defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The plaintiffs argued, inter alia, that the statutes violated their right to equal protection. The supreme court disagreed. The challenged statutes were not discriminatory on their face and there was not a patent indication of a lack of relationship between the classification and the purpose of the statute. The statutes did not distinguish based upon classifications, but rather applied equally to all candidates based on the number of years served. Considering the rational basis standard, the statutes did not violate the candidates' right of equal protection guaranteed by the Idaho Constitution. The statutes were rationally related by limiting access to the ballot by certain incumbents to the legitimate government goal of giving more individuals the opportunity to hold government offices than would be possible without the benefit of the ballot access restrictions. Therefore, the district court erred in finding the statutes unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

In re Enjoin Implementation of the Redistricting Plan v. Idaho Comm'n


Docket No. 27760, Docket No. 27811


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


136 Idaho 542; 38 P.3d 121; 2001 Ida. LEXIS 140



November 29, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected March 8, 2002. Released for Publication December 21, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original proceedings retained by the Supreme Court of the State of Idaho.



DISPOSITION: Redistricting plan found to violate constitution.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, citizens, sought injunctive relief against respondent State, regarding redistricting of state legislative districts. In a separate action, county filed a substantially similar petition, and the two cases were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: The petition alleged that Legislative Plan 66 (L66) was unconstitutional, and that it impermissibly divided counties to create districts, separated communities with common interests into separate districts, created districts with too large a population disparity, and was enacted without following appropriate procedures. The court determined that L66 deviated in population 10.69 percent between districts, slightly over the 10 percent limit, constituting a prima facie case of discrimination under the Equal Protection Clause. As State failed to show that the population disparity resulted from advancement of a rational policy, the court ruled that the presumption of discrimination applied, and L66 was unconstitutional in violation of the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution. Furthermore, the award of attorney fees to the citizens under the private attorney general doctrine was appropriate.


OUTCOME: Redistricting was found unconstitutional, and costs were awarded to the citizens and county.

Porter v. State


DOCKET NO. 26645, 2001 Opinion No. 78


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


136 Idaho 257; 32 P.3d 151; 2001 Ida. LEXIS 98



August 14, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied September 28, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Ida LEXIS 116. Released for Publication September 28, 2001.
Rehearing denied by Porter v. State, 2001 Ida. LEXIS 116 (Idaho, Sept. 28, 2001)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Second Judicial District, State of Idaho, Lewis County. Honorable George R. Reinhardt, III, District Judge.
State v. Porter, 130 Idaho 772, 948 P.2d 127, 1997 Ida. LEXIS 109 (Idaho, 1997)



DISPOSITION: Appeal from order dismissing petition for post-conviction relief, dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was convicted of first degree murder, appealed a judgment of the Second Judicial District Court, Lewis County, Idaho, which dismissed his second application for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: In his second application for postconviction relief, defendant alleged that: (1) he received inadequate representation on appeal; (2) the State failed to disclose material exculpatory and impeaching evidence; and (3) Idaho Code § 19-2719 was unconstitutional. The instant court held that the three-year span from the date of defendant's first appellate brief to the assertion of his current claims was an unreasonable length of time for the pursuit of postconviction relief because the issues raised or not raised by appellate counsel were known at the time of the filing of the first appellate brief. Despite the fact that information sought by defendant was not discovered until well after the litigation over his first postconviction petition had been completed, the instant court concluded that the information could reasonably have been known to either defendant or his counsel at the time he filed his first petition for postconviction relief. The instant court declined to consider the constitutional arguments raised by defendant for the first time on appeal because it did not appear that there were any subsequent proceedings in the case.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

Aia Servs. Corp. v. Idaho State Tax Comm'n


Docket No. 26029, 2001 Opinion No. 72


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


136 Idaho 184; 30 P.3d 962; 2001 Ida. LEXIS 85



July 31, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 26, 2001. Petition for Rehearing Denied July 31, 2001. Released for Publication August 22, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Daniel T. Eismann, District Judge.

This Opinion Substituted on Denial of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of May 4, 2001, Previously Reported at: 2001 Ida. LEXIS 42.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation appealed an order of the Fourth Judicial District Court, Ada County, Idaho, which granted summary judgment to respondent Idaho State Tax Commission, which had determined a delinquency in Idaho income taxes against the corporation.


OVERVIEW: The corporation filed combined Idaho tax returns with its subsidiary companies for 1990 and 1991. The corporation made "special deductions" to its combined taxable income of the dividend received from one of its wholly owned insurance subsidiaries. The subsidiary was exempt from paying Idaho income taxes but was subject to premium taxes. The commission disallowed the deductions, determining that the corporation failed to establish that it was entitled to deduct income it received as dividends from the subsidiary under the Idaho Income Tax Act. The corporation claimed that it was required to combine its income with that of its subsidiary for reporting purposes under the Act; it argued that the trial court erred in holding that the corporation was not entitled to deduct the dividends paid to it by the subsidiary because the corporation had failed to meet statutory requirements. The instant court held that the corporation and the subsidiary were not required to file a combined return because the subsidiary was an insurance company. The corporation was not entitled to take the deduction because the subsidiary did not pay more than 50 percent of its premium taxes to the State.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision was affirmed. Costs were awarded to the commission.

 

178 of 368 DOCUMENTS


State v. Coassolo


Docket No. 26948, 2001 Opinion No. 70


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


136 Idaho 138; 30 P.3d 293; 2001 Ida. LEXIS 83



July 27, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 20, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Twin Falls County. Hon. Roger S. Burdick, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Orders relinquishing jurisdiction and denying I.C.R. 35 motion for reconsideration of sentence, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State petitioned for review of a decision by the Court of Appeals reversing a decision of the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Twin Falls County, that relinquishing jurisdiction and denied defendant's motion for reconsideration of his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to aiding and abetting the delivery of methamphetamine and was sentenced to imprisonment. The district judge retained jurisdiction and placed defendant in a rider program. Upon completion of the program, the correctional institution did not provide defendant an opportunity to contest the accuracy and fairness of its evaluation. The district judge relinquished jurisdiction and ordered defendant to begin serving his prison sentence. Defendant appealed the order, and the appellate court reversed, finding a violation of defendant's constitutional rights. The state supreme court granted the State's petition for review. Defendant did not have a protectable liberty interest, merely an expectation of such an interest. His due process rights were provided at sentencing, not when jurisdiction was relinquished.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's decision was reversed. The orders relinquishing jurisdiction and denying defendant's motion for reconsideration of sentence were affirmed.

 

179 of 368 DOCUMENTS


State v. Statton


Docket No. 26947, 2001 Opinion No. 71


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


136 Idaho 135; 30 P.3d 290; 2001 Ida. LEXIS 82



July 27, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 20, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Kootenai County. Hon. Gary M. Haman, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Orders relinquishing jurisdiction and denying I.C.R. 35 motion for reconsideration of sentence, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Trial court relinquished jurisdiction after the correctional facility submitted an evaluation of the defendant. No hearing was conducted for the defendant to contest the report. The defendant filed a motion to reconsider the order relinquishing jurisdiction, which the trial court treated as a motion for leniency and denied. The Court of Appeals (Idaho) found that the defendant was denied due process and reversed. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court of appeals held that the defendant had a liberty interest in the accuracy of the prison's report, and by not being given a hearing in which he could challenge the report, the defendant's due process rights were violated and reversed the order relinquishing jurisdiction. The court held that the district court did not err on the merits in relinquishing jurisdiction and denying the motion for leniency. The court found that since the defendant did not possess a constitutionally protected liberty interest, the district court did not violate the defendant's due process rights by relinquishing jurisdiction without holding a hearing on the accuracy of prison's report. The court also found that the district court properly concluded that the defendant was not a good candidate for probation and that a reduction in sentence was appropriate. The trial court noted that the defendant was likely to relapse into substance abuse, had emotional and anger management problems, and an immaturity problem, in making its decision.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals, and the judgment of the district court was affirmed.

 

180 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Bradbury v. Idaho Judicial Council


Docket No. 26361, 2001 Opinion No. 63


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


136 Idaho 63; 28 P.3d 1006; 2001 Ida. LEXIS 66



July 10, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published August 1, 2001. Certiorari Denied January 22, 2002, Reported at: 2002 U.S. LEXIS 544.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Ronald J. Wilper, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court granting the Idaho Judicial Council's motion to dismiss is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County (Idaho) granted respondent Idaho Judicial Council's motion to dismiss appellant attorney's complaint for declaratory judgment seeking access to the council's records of investigatory proceedings. This attorney appealed.


OVERVIEW: The attorney filed a complaint against a judge, and the council determined that there were no violations. The attorney's request for information was denied. The information was unavailable for release pursuant to Idaho Ct. Admin. R. 32(d)(20) and Idaho Code § 1-2103. Confidentiality was required only for the limited purpose of allowing the council to conduct a preliminary investigation into the complaint before determining whether to proceed with a recommendation for discipline. The statute and rule met the rational basis test, and the attorney's substantive due process rights were not violated. The interest asserted by the attorney did not rise to the level contemplated by the Fourteenth Amendment for procedural due process protection. The district court was correct that the attorney lacked a property interest in the council's proceedings. Consequently, there was no violation of procedural due process.


OUTCOME: The judgment granting the council's motion to dismiss was affirmed.

 

181 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Union Pac. Corp. v. Idaho State Tax Comm'n


Docket No. 25876, 2001 Opinion No. 60


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


136 Idaho 34; 28 P.3d 375; 2001 Ida. LEXIS 72



June 27, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published July 19, 2001.
Appeal after remand at Union Pac. Corp. v. Idaho State Tax Comm'n, 2004 Ida. LEXIS 2 (Idaho, Jan. 4, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. D. Duff McKee, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is vacated and this case is remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County (Idaho), reversed appellant state tax commission's assessment of tax deficiencies against respondent corporation and granted summary judgment to the corporation. The state tax commission appealed.


OVERVIEW: The state tax commission assessed income tax deficiencies against the taxpayer. At issue was the taxpayer's apportionment of income to Idaho. Corporations such as the taxpayer operating both in Idaho and in one or more other states were required to apportion some business income to Idaho. The apportionment took into account three factors called the "property factor," the "payroll factor," and the "sales factor." The taxpayer included as part of the sales factor the sales of its account receivables. The state tax commission conceded that item constituted a sale. The trial court thus ruled against the state tax commission. Also, the trial court concluded dividends the taxpayer received from mining soda ash were not "business income" under Idaho Code § 63-3027(a)(1) because they were not received in the regular course of business. After summary judgment was entered for the taxpayer, the appellate court found that including the sale of accounts receivable in the sales factor did not fairly show how the taxpayer earned its income. It also found that the trial court only considered one of two definitions of "business income" and should have considered the other one as well.


OUTCOME: Judgment for taxpayer on the issue of whether including in the income apportionment formula money received from the sale of accounts receivable fairly represented how the taxpayer earned its income was vacated. Judgment that income the taxpayer received from stock dividends was not business income also had to be vacated.

 

182 of 368 DOCUMENTS


State v. Keaveny


Docket No. 25583, 2001 Opinion No. 57


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


136 Idaho 31; 28 P.3d 372; 2001 Ida. LEXIS 73



June 25, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published July 17, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Third Judicial District for the State of Idaho, Canyon County. Hon. James C, Morfitt, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Third Judicial District Court, Canyon County, Idaho, which convicted him of felony domestic violence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the felony domestic violence statute, Idaho Code § 18-918(3) (1998) (amended 2000), was unconstitutionally vague because the term "traumatic injury" was not sufficiently defined. According to defendant, the jury was unable to distinguish a felony from a misdemeanor because of the statute's broad definition of "traumatic injury." This confusion, defendant claimed, forced defendants to prove the absence of a "traumatic injury" in order for a jury to reduce the conviction to a misdemeanor. Defendant contended that the lack of a distinction between a misdemeanor and a felony rendered the statute unconstitutional. Defendant also argued that the jury instructions unconstitutionally shifted the burden of proof to him. The instant court held that the domestic violence statute's definition of "traumatic injury" was sufficiently defined and was not unconstitutionally vague. The jury instructions did not unconstitutionally shift the burden of proving an essential element of the statute from the State to defendant.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

183 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Uranga v. Federated Publs


Docket No. 27118, 2001 Opinion No. 52


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


2001 Ida. LEXIS 71; 29 Media L. Rep. 1961



June 21, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. D. Duff McKee, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: District court's grant of summary judgment, reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The plaintiff filed various defamation claims against the defendant publisher arising from the publication of an article based on statements contained in a 40 year old court file alleging homosexual conduct on the part of the plaintiff. The district court granted the publisher's motion for summary judgment and the Idaho Court of Appeals affirmed. The plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court file containing the statement was related to the criminal prosecution of someone other than the plaintiff. The publisher argued that the trial court's grant of summary judgment should be affirmed because: (1) under U.S. Supreme Court case law, it had an absolute constitutional privilege to publish a statement contained in a public file; and (2) the fair report privilege gave it an absolute right to publish the statement. The Supreme Court of Idaho held that: (1) the U.S. Supreme Court had not established an absolute constitutional privilege to publish information in a public file, and distinguished the present case from one relied on by the publisher; and (2) the privilege did not extend to cloak the press in an absolute privilege to publish a statement regarding the plaintiff's sexuality found in a forty-year-old court file where the statement was not used in an official or judicial proceeding, was never entered into evidence, and was not in a court pleading.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment was vacated and the case was remanded.

 

184 of 368 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hart


Docket No. 26119, 2001 Opinion No. 48


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


135 Idaho 827; 25 P.3d 850; 2001 Ida. LEXIS 59



May 31, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published June 22, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Third Judicial District of the State of Idaho, Canyon County. Hon. Gerald L. Weston, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Order granting motion to dismiss, reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with felony domestic violence. The District Court of the Third Judicial District, Canyon County (Idaho), dismissed after finding that his wife's injuries were not covered by Idaho Code § 18-918(3). The State claimed the dismissal was in error, and defendant claimed the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's wife suffered bruising as a result of defendant's abuse. Defendant claimed the domestic violence statute was unconstitutional. The district judge narrowed the definition of traumatic injury and found that the bruising was not covered by the statute. Idaho Code § 19-918 was not void for vagueness, and it did not violate equal protection. The statute did not obviously and invidiously discriminate and was subject to rational basis review. Decision of the legislature to extend additional protection to household members was rationally related to the state's interest in preventing violence between those involved in some type of domestic relationship. District judge erred in ruling the term traumatic injury as defined by Idaho Code § 18-918(2) did not include the bruising sustained by the wife.


OUTCOME: Judgment dismissing the complaint was reversed. Domestic violence statute was neither vague nor did it violate equal protection. The district judge erred in narrowing the meaning of traumatic injury to exclude bruising.

State v. Davis


Docket No. 26046, 2001 Opinion No. 34


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


135 Idaho 747; 24 P.3d 64; 2001 Ida. LEXIS 49



May 15, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected July 19, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District, State of Idaho, Kootenai County. Hon. Craig Kosonen, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a prosecution of defendant for domestic battery, in violation of Idaho Code § 18-918, the State appealed a decision of the First Judicial District Court, Kootenai County (Idaho), which concluded that § 18-918 was unconstitutionally broad.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the constitutionality of § 18-918 on the basis that the definition of "traumatic injury" failed to adequately provide exceptions for household members who injured each other willfully but not unlawfully, such as bruises or contusions inflicted during a family football game. Defendant claimed that the statute was facially overbroad because it impermissibly proscribed a substantial amount of constitutionally protected conduct and was incapable of any constitutional application. The instant court rejected defendant's argument. Defendant did not assert that the injuries he caused the victim were inflicted while engaged in a constitutionally protected activity. Defendant was provided adequate notice of what behavior was prohibited by the statute and what the punishment for that behavior would be.


OUTCOME: Trial court's decision was reversed.

State v. Prather


Docket No. 25476, 2001 Opinion No. 36


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


135 Idaho 770; 25 P.3d 83; 2001 Ida. LEXIS 50



May 15, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected August 3, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Third Judicial District, State of Idaho, Canyon County. Hon. Dennis E. Goff, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was charged with domestic violence in the presence of a child, in violation of Idaho Code §§ 18-918(3) and 18-918(7)(b). Appellant filed a motion to dismiss the charges on the basis that § 18-918(3) was unconstitutionally vague. The District Court of the Third Judicial District, Canyon County (Idaho) denied the motion. A jury then found appellant guilty of the charges. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued that § 18-918(3) was facially void for vagueness because it failed to specifically define the prohibited conduct. The statute defined "traumatic injury" in part as "a condition of the body whether of a minor or serious nature." Appellant argued that because the statute failed to set forth a sufficient definition of "traumatic injury," neither persons subject to the statute, nor those who had to enforce it, were able to ascertain what conduct was prohibited. The supreme court affirmed, finding that there were circumstances which would allow a defendant to be convicted of the lesser crime of misdemeanor domestic battery, and the legislature had clearly expressed its intent of creating a crime and punishment for those who willfully caused traumatic injuries to other members of a household. Further, the statute did not violate due process by shifting the burden of proof to the defense.


OUTCOME: The trial court judgment was affirmed.

State v. Larsen

SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


135 Idaho 754; 24 P.3d 702; 2001 Ida. LEXIS 47



May 15, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Blaine County. Hon. James J. May, District Judge; Hon. Robert Elgee, Magistrate Judge.



DISPOSITION: Order dismissing felony charge reversed. Case remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State challenged a decision of the District Court of the Fifth Judicial District, Blaine County, Idaho, affirming the magistrate's dismissal of the felony domestic violence charge filed against appellee.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was charged with felony domestic violence in violation of Idaho Code § 18-918(3). Appellee moved to dismiss the charge, arguing the unconstitutionality of the statute on the grounds of vagueness, separation of powers, due process, and equal protection. The magistrate held the statute violated the equal protection guarantees of the Idaho Constitution and dismissed the charge. The district court affirmed on vagueness grounds. The supreme court held that Idaho Code § 18-918(3) was not unconstitutionally void for vagueness. In addition, appellee failed to establish that his prosecution under Idaho Code § 18-918(3) violated the equal protection guarantees of the United States or Idaho Constitutions. The prosecutor did not abuse his discretion by charging appellee.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing the charge was reversed and the case was remanded.

State v. Hellickson


Docket No. 25334, 2001 Opinion No. 35


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


135 Idaho 742; 24 P.3d 59; 2001 Ida. LEXIS 48



May 15, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected July 19, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Deborah A. Bail, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant pleaded guilty to charges of felony domestic violence, Idaho Code § 18-918, and battery, Idaho Code § 18-903(b). The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County (Idaho) placed appellant on probation for five years. Appellant filed an appeal, challenging the constitutionality of § 18-918.


OVERVIEW: Appellant contended that § 18-918 was facially void for vagueness because it failed to specifically define the prohibited conduct. The statute defined "traumatic injury" in part as "a condition of the body whether of a minor or serious nature." Appellant argued that the only difference between a felony and a misdemeanor under the statute was that a misdemeanor did not result in a "traumatic injury," and that because the statute did not require the injury to be caused "unlawfully," any willfully inflicted injury would be a felony. The supreme court affirmed, finding that there were circumstances which would allow a defendant to be convicted of the lesser crime of misdemeanor domestic battery. The legislature had clearly expressed its intent of creating a crime and punishment for those who willfully caused traumatic injuries to other members of a household.


OUTCOME: The trial court judgment was affirmed.

Int'l Ass'n of Firefighters, Local No. 672 v. City of Boise City


DOCKET NO. 25640


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


136 Idaho 162; 30 P.3d 940; 2001 Ida. LEXIS 36; 143 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P59,269



May 2, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Counsel Corrected May 4, 2001. Petition for Rehearing Filed May 23, 2001. Petition for Rehearing Denied July 23, 2001. As Corrected July 24, 2001. Released for Publication September 4, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. Honorable Michael R. McLaughlin, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Declaratory judgment by the district court determining rights under collective bargaining agreement, affirmed in part and reversed in part. Case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant union sought declaratory relief and an injunction precluding respondent city from implementing a subcontract collective bargaining agent. The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County, denied appellant's request, and this appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant firefighters' union claimed Idaho's civil service statutes prohibited the subcontracting of work to non-civil service employees. Had the agreements resulted in termination or demotion of existing civil service employees, respondent's action would have been in conflict with the Civil Service Act. However, none of the union-members lost their jobs. The collective labor agreement (CLA) made arbitration of appellant's grievance compulsory. The issues raised by appellant constituted a grievance under the CLA. It was error for the district court to conclude that the contracts were within the exclusive discretion of respondent. The Collective Bargaining Act, Idaho Code § 44-1801 et seq., required respondent to negotiate its decision to contract out firefighting services. Mandatory negotiations on the subcontracting issue would not have significantly interfered with respondent's management rights.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed in part and reversed in part. Respondent's contracts with non-union firefighters did not violate the Idaho Constitution or the Idaho Civil Service Act. However, respondent was obligated to arbitrate grievances and to negotiate in good faith the terms and conditions of the firefighters' employment.

 

190 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Idaho Endowment Fund Inv. Bd. v. Crane


DOCKET NO. 26304


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


135 Idaho 667; 23 P.3d 129; 2001 Ida. LEXIS 34



April 18, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 10, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. Honorable Michael R. McLaughlin, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment upholding constitutionality of Idaho School Bond Guaranty Act affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state treasurer challenged the judgment of the District Court, Fourth Judicial District, Ada County (Idaho), which ruled, inter alia, that the ballot to amend Idaho Const. amend. IX, §§ 3, 11 was properly submitted to the voters; that the Idaho School Bond Guaranty Act (Act), Idaho Code §§ 33-5301 et seq., 63-3638(6), and 57-728, was constitutional; and ordered appellant to perform the duties of his office as required by the Act.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the appellant contended that the single ballot to amend Idaho Const. art. IX, §§ 3, 11 was illegal because the sections were unrelated and independent of one another; therefore a single ballot should not have been used. Appellant also argued that the Act was unconstitutional because the purchase of notes under the Act was a transfer of endowment funds not authorized by Idaho Const. art. IX, § 3. The court held that the Act was constitutional and immediately subject to implementation by the appellant. The court held that the single ballot was properly submitted to the voters. The two amendments were related and although not dependent one upon the other, they were neither incongruous nor in conflict. The amendments were part of a common scheme to increase the flexibility of the management of the public school endowment fund. The court also held that the purchase of notes was not a transfer, use or appropriation of endowment funds but was the purchase of an investment to be held as an asset of the fund, which in turn will produce income for the fund. Therefore the Act did not violate the state constitution.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

191 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Sanchez v. City of Caldwell


Docket No. 26134, 2001 Opinion No. 10


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


135 Idaho 465; 20 P.3d 1; 2001 Ida. LEXIS 12



March 1, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 23, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Third Judicial District, State of Idaho, Canyon County. Hon. James C. Morfitt, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Third Judicial District Court, Canyon County (Idaho), which upheld the constitutionality of a municipal ordinance denying a retail license for the sale of beer or wine to someone, who within the previous five years, had been convicted of driving while under the influence of alcohol, drugs, or other intoxicating substances.


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued that respondent city's ordinance which prevented him from having his beer and wine license renewed was unconstitutional because there was no rational relationship between his having been convicted of driving while under the influence and his operating a business involved in the retail sale of beer and wine. The instant court upheld the trial court's ruling that the ordinance was constitutional. Respondent could have reasonably concluded that a retail seller of alcoholic beverages who had himself been recently convicted of driving under the influence of alcohol or drugs was less likely to fulfill his obligation of not selling alcoholic beverages to intoxicated customers. For the same reason that the ordinance was rationally related to a legitimate governmental purpose, the instant court concluded that the ordinance was not unreasonable or arbitrary. The instant court declined to award attorney fees to respondent, as appellant's arguments were not frivolous, unreasonable, or without foundation.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed. Ordinance adopted by respondent city was rationally related to a legitimate state purpose. Respondent could have reasonably concluded that a retail seller of alcoholic beverages who had been convicted of driving while under the influence of alcohol or drugs would not use sufficient care to refrain from selling beer and wine to intoxicated customers.

 

192 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Row v. State


Docket No. 26508, 2001 Opinion No. 9


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


135 Idaho 573; 21 P.3d 895; 2001 Ida. LEXIS 14



March 1, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied April 13, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Ida. LEXIS 31. Released for Publication April 13, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. Deborah A. Bail, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed an application for post-conviction relief and for habeas corpus relief. The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County (Idaho) dismissed the requests. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, convicted of aggravated arson and first degree murder, filed an appeal and a petition for post-conviction relief in 1994. The trial court and the supreme court upheld the conviction and dismissed the petition. Appellant filed a second petition in 1999, which also included a claim for habeas corpus relief. The trial court dismissed both claims. The supreme court affirmed. In a successive petition for post-conviction relief, appellant was required to show that the issues raised were excluded from the operation of Idaho Code § 19-2719, which required that the petition be filed within 42 days of the filing of the judgment imposing the death sentence. To do so, appellant had to show that the issues were not known and could not reasonably have been known when the first petition was prosecuted. All of appellant's allegations, including ex parte communications, prosecutorial misconduct, and ineffective assistance of counsel, were known or reasonably could have been known by appellant at the time she filed her first petition for post-conviction relief.


OUTCOME: Dismissal of appellant's appeal and petition affirmed. Appellant failed to show that she did not know or could not have reasonably have previously known of any of the issues she raised in her successive petitions.

State v. Clark


Docket No. 26676, 2000 Opinion No. 135


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


135 Idaho 255; 16 P.3d 931; 2000 Ida. LEXIS 148



December 28, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 19, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. Hon. George D. Carey, District Judge; Hon. Carolyn Minder, Magistrate.



DISPOSITION: Magistrate's decision denying motion to dismiss for violation of statutory rights to speedy trial, reversed. Case remanded for entry of dismissal order.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with misdemeanor battery. He entered a conditional plea of guilty to the charge, reserving the right to appeal the magistrate's denial of his motion to dismiss the charge for violation his right to speedy trial. The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Ada County (Idaho) and the Idaho Court of Appeals affirmed the magistrate's conviction. Defendant appealed the conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with misdemeanor battery, allegedly hitting and choking his ex-wife. The State requested a continuance to accommodate the complaining witness. The magistrate continued the trial. Defendant moved to dismiss because of the denial of his right to a speedy trial. The magistrate granted the State a later continuance, to which defendant again objected in a motion. The magistrate conducted a hearing and stated that the volume of the caseload made it impossible to afford defendant his right to a trial within the required six-month period under Idaho Code § 19-3501 (2000) and denied defendant's motion to dismiss. Defendant entered a guilty plea, reserving his right to appeal the speedy trial issue. The magistrate entered an order withholding judgment and placed defendant on probation. The decision of the magistrate was affirmed by the district court and later by the Court of Appeals. The supreme court found that the magistrate erred by improperly denying defendant's motion to dismiss for violation of his speedy trial rights under Idaho Code § 19-3501(3) as the magistrate granted a continuance beyond the statutory limit without a showing of good cause by the State.


OUTCOME: Judgment was reversed and remanded with directions to dismiss the charge because the magistrate erred in denying defendant's motion to dismiss, as good cause for the trial delay was not shown by the State.

Van Valkenburgh v. Citizens for Term Limits


Docket No. 26080, 2000 Opinion No. 116


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


135 Idaho 121; 15 P.3d 1129; 2000 Ida. LEXIS 121



December 6, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Counsel Corrected December 15, 2000. Released for Publication December 28, 2000. As Corrected March 16, 2001.



DISPOSITION: Petition for Writ of Prohibition, granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners requested writ of prohibition and applied for declaratory judgment, seeking to prevent the respondent Idaho Secretary of State from taking any action pursuant to Idaho Code § 34-970B and seeking to have Idaho Code § 34-907B declared unconstitutional under both the Idaho Constitution and the United States Constitution.


OVERVIEW: The petitioners argued Idaho Code § 34-907B violated the right to suffrage guaranteed by the Idaho Constitution because the statute dictates the way the ballot was written, and therefore violated the integrity of the ballot, as well as the sanctity and privacy of the voting booth. The court agreed and applied a strict scrutiny standard to its analysis. The court found the ballot legend unconstitutional and issued a writ of prohibition prohibiting the Secretary of State from carrying out the directions contained in Idaho Code § 34-907B(3), (4) of as they pertain to the placement of ballot legends on the ballot. Additionally, because the court found that Idaho Code § 34-907B(5) was not severable from the unconstitutional portions of the statute, the court also struck down that subsection.


OUTCOME: Writ was granted. Statutory ballot legend was unconstitutional as it violated a fundamental right.

 

195 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Osmunson v. State


Docket No. 24918, 2000 Opinion No. 109


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


135 Idaho 292; 17 P.3d 236; 2000 Ida. LEXIS 114



October 31, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Filed November 17, 2000. Petition for Rehearing Denied December 28, 2000. Released for Publication January 31, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the First Judicial District, State of Idaho, Bonner County. Honorable James R. Michaud, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In this permissive appeal, the State claimed that the District Court of the First Judicial District, Bonner County (Idaho) erred in ruling that several provisions of the Constitutionally Based Education Claims Act, Idaho Code § 6-2201 et seq., were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, parent and schoolchildren, challenged the constitutionality of procedures prescribed by the Constitutionally Based Education Claims Act (CBECA), Idaho Code § 6-2201 et seq., and alleged that defendant school district was under-funded. The lower court ruled that several provisions of CBECA were unconstitutional. Plaintiffs did not show that CBECA denied them their right to a speedy remedy. CBECA did not impermissibly limit plaintiffs' rights to pursue constitutionally required educational services. Plaintiffs' rights under Idaho Const. art. I, § 18 could have been fully addressed within remedies authorized by CBECA. Plaintiffs failed to show a palpable injury fairly traceable to inability of defendant school district to bring actions directly against legislature.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed. Constitutionally Based Education Claims Act did not violate the Education Article of the Idaho Constitution. Plaintiffs failed to show that they were deprived of their right to a speedy remedy. Joinder was not an issue and separation of powers issue was not ripe for or review.

 

196 of 368 DOCUMENTS


State v. Zaitseva


Docket No. 24986, 2000 Opinion No. 108


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


135 Idaho 11; 13 P.3d 338; 2000 Ida. LEXIS 115



October 31, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 22, 2000. As Corrected February 1, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Elmore County. Hon. Michael R. McLaughlin, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of conviction for possession of a forged instrument, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Fourth Judicial District Court, Elmore County (Idaho), which found her guilty of 14 counts of possession of a forged, blank, or unfinished check, and which sentenced defendant on each count to a unified sentence of 5 years with 2 years fixed, and the court further ordered that the sentences be served concurrently.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant, who was a passenger in a car that was pulled over by a police officer, argued that: (1) the search and seizure of a bag found in the car was unconstitutional; (2) there was insufficient evidence presented which would have allowed jury to properly conclude that defendant was guilty of forgery; (3) the prosecutor engaged in multiplicitous charging; (4) defendant's trial attorney provided ineffective assistance of counsel; and (5) trial court abused its discretion at sentencing. The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and sentence. It was not improper for the officer to search the bag in the course of searching the car with the consents he had obtained from the driver, from the apparent owner, and from defendant. Although some of the documents found in defendant's possession could not have been passed as checks without more work, a rational jury could have determined that defendant intended to continue the process. Defendant was properly charged with 14 counts. The court did not have sufficient evidence to consider defendant's claim of ineffective assistance. The sentences imposed by the trial court were not unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and the imposed sentences were affirmed, as there was sufficient evidence presented which would have allowed jury to properly conclude that defendant was guilty of forgery.

 

197 of 368 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hammersley


Docket No. 24902, 2000 Opinion No. 97


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


134 Idaho 816; 10 P.3d 1285; 2000 Ida. LEXIS 102



September 8, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 2, 2000. As Corrected December 13, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fist Judicial District, State of Idaho, Kootenai County. Hon. James F. Judd, District Judge; Hon. Barry E. Watson, Magistrate Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal from magistrate's denial of motion to dismiss, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the ruling by the Kootenai County (Idaho) District Court, First Judicial District, affirming the magistrate court's denial of her motion to dismiss, based on her challenge to the constitutionality of Idaho Code § 18-6409, under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Idaho Const. art. I, § 9.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with disturbing the peace under Idaho Code § 18-6409 after she yelled at her daughter's young friend in front of her daughter and two other friends, using profanity. The magistrate court found appellant guilty; on appeal, appellant argued that her conviction violated her right to free speech under U.S. Const. amend. I and Idaho Const. art. I, § 9. The court affirmed, holding that appellant's speech was not constitutionally protected because her speech fell within the "fighting words" exception to free speech and was thereby subject to regulation. Appellant's statement contained no message of social or political importance, and the "fighting words" exception applied even though the girl could not physically have retaliated. Second, § 18-6409, which prohibited profane language within the hearing of children, was not vague or overbroad as applied; the terms "profane" and "vulgar" in the statute were adequately defined by their common usage.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed. Appellant's speech constituted "fighting words" and fell outside the scope of constitutional protection, the conduct prohibited was adequately described, and the statute gave adequate notice.

 

198 of 368 DOCUMENTS


Fields v. State


Docket No. 24119, 2000 Opinion No. 93


SUPREME COURT OF IDAHO


135 Idaho 286; 17 P.3d 230; 2000 Ida. LEXIS 100



September 7, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Filed September 26, 2000. Petition for Rehearing Denied January 25, 2001. Released for Publication January 25, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County. Honorable Thomas V. Neville, District Judge.
State v. Fields, 127 Idaho 904, 908 P.2d 1211, 1995 Ida. LEXIS 14 (Idaho, 1995)



DISPOSITION: Order dismissing petition for post-conviction relief, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed an application for post-conviction relief from his first degree murder conviction in the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, State of Idaho, Ada County.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first degree murder and sentenced to death in 1991. His first petition for post-conviction relief was denied. He filed a second petition, claiming that newly discovered evidence indicated that perjured testimony had contributed to his conviction, and alleging ineffective assistance and conflict of interest by trial counsel. The trial court found that all of these claims were either raised or could have been raised in the initial post-conviction application, and denied the petition. The supreme court affirmed, holding that while the issue of conflict of interest by trial counsel was newly discovered and reviewable, appellant failed to show his representation was adversely affected by any conflict. Further claims of ineffective assistance were rejected as untimely. Finally, appellant did not have a right to appointed counsel on his second petition, and denial of appellant's discovery request did not prevent further investigation by appellant's representatives.


OUTCOME: Petition denied. Appellant failed to show that his attorney's representation in the post-conviction proceedings was adversely affected by any conflict of interest, and appellant did not have a right to appointed counsel on his second petition. Further discovery was properly denied as it was not necessary to protect any substantial rights.
